كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته الولي وله أن يأذن لغيره فإن صلى عليه غير الولي والسلطان أعاد الولي ولم يصل غيره فإن كان الأخوان لأب وأم أسنهما أولى فإن أراد الأسن أن يقدم أحداً كان للأصغر أن يمنع، قدم كل واحد منهما رجلاً آخر فالذي قدمه الأسن أولى، وكذلك الابنان على هذا وكذلك أبناء العم، فإن كان الأخ الأصغر لأب وأم والأكبر لأب فالأصغر أولى كما في الميراث، فإن قدم الأصغر جداً فليس للأكبر أن يمنعه، فإن كان الأخ لأب وأم غائباً وكتب لإنسان ليتقدم فللأخ لأب أن يمنعه وحد الغيبة أن لا يقدر على أن يقدم ويدرك الصلاة ولا ينتظر الناس قدومه. والمريض في المصر بمنزلة الصحيح يقدم من شاء وليس للأبعد منعه. ولو ماتت امرأة ولها أب وابن بالغ عاقل وزوج فالأب أحق بها ثم الابن، إن كان من غير الزوج، فإن كان منه فالزوج أحق من الولد ولو مات ابن وله أب وأبو أب فالولاية لأبيه ولكنه يقدم أباه جد الميت تعظيماً له، وكذا المكاتب إذا مات عبده ومولاه حاضر فالولاية للمكاتب لكنه يقدم مولاه احتراماً. ومولى العبد أحق بالصلاة عليه من ابنه الحر على المفتى به لبقاء ملك حكماً، وكذا المكاتب إذا مات عن غير وفاء فإن ترك وفاء، فإن أديت كتابته أو كان المال حاضراً لا يخاف عليه التوى والتلف فالابن أحق وإلا فالمولى وسائر القرابات أولى من الزوج، وكذا مولى العتاقة وابنه ومولى الموالات لأن الزوجية انقطعت بينهما بالموت. وفي المجتبى : والجار أحق من غيره. قوله: (وله أن يأذن لغيره) أي للولي الإذن في صلاة الجنازة وهو يحتمل شيئين : أحدهما الإذن في التقدم لأنه حقه فيملك إبطاله وقدمنا أن محله ما إذا لم يكن هناك ولي غيره أو كان وهو بعيد، أما إذا كانا وليين مستويين فأذن أحدهما أجنبياً فللآخر أن يمنعه . ثانيهما أن يأدن للناس في الانصراف بعد الصلاة قبل الدفن لأنه لا ينبغي لهم أن ينصرفوا إلا بإذنه، وذكر الشارح معنى آخر وهو الإعلام بموته ليصلوا عليه لا سيما إذا كان الميت يتبرك به، وكره بعضهم أن ينادى عليه في الأزقة والأسواق لأنه نعي أهل الجاهلية وهو مكروه، والأصح أنه لا يكره لأن فيه تكثير الجماعة من المصلين عليه والمستغفرين له وتحريض الناس على الطهارة والاعتبار به والاستعداد وليس ذلك نعي أهل الجاهلية، وإنما كانوا يبعثون إلى القبائل ينعون مع ضجيج وبكاء وعويل وتعديد وهو مكروه بالإجماع ا هـ . وهي كراهة تحريم قال في النهر أقول : بل صنة العلم توجب التقديم فيها أيضاً ألا ترى إلى ما مر من أن إمام الحي إنما يقدم على الولي إذا كان أفضل منه نعم علل القدوري كراهة تقديم الابن على أبيه بأن فيه استخفافاً به وهذا يقتضي وجوب تقديمه مطلقاً. قال في الفتح : لا يبعد أن يقال إن تقديمه واجب بالسنة. وفي البدائع قال أبو يوسف وله بحكم الولاية أن يقدم غيره لأن الولاية له وإنما منع من التقدم حتى لا يستخف بأبيه فلم تسقط ولايته في التقديم . للحديث المتفق عليه «ليس منا من ضرب الخدود وشق الجيوب ودعا بدعوى الجاهلية» وقال عليه السلام «لعن الله الحالقة والصالقة والشاقة» والصالقة التي ترفع صوتها بالمصيبة ولا بأس بإرسال الدمع والبكاء من غير نياحة قوله : (فإن صلى عليه غير الولي والسلطان أعاد الولي) لأن الحق له. والمراد السلطان من حق التقدم على الولي فإن الكلام فيما إذا تقدم على الولي من ليس له حق التقدم فليس للولي الإعادة إذا صلى القاضي أو نائبه أو إمام الحي في الخلاصة والولوالجية والظهيرية والتجنيس والواقعات ولو صلى رجل والولي خلفه ولم يرض به إن صلى معه لا يعيد لأنه صلى مرة وإن لم يتابعه فإن كان المصلي السلطان أو الإمام الأعظم في البلدة أو القاضي أو الولي على البلدة أو إمام حي ليس له أن يعيد لأنهم أولى بالصلاة منه وإن كان غيرهم فله الإعادة ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أن الموصى له بالتقدم ليس بمقدم على الولي لأن الوصية باطلة على المفتى به صرح بذلك أصحاب الفتاوى قالوا : ولو أعادها الولي ليس لمن صلى عليها أن يصلي مع الولي مرة أخرى وظاهر كلامهم أن الولي إذا لم يعد فلا إثم على أحد لما أن الفرض وهو قضاء حق الميت قد تأدى بصلاة الأجنبي، والإعادة إنما هي لأجل حقه لا لإسقاط الفرض، هذا أولى مما في غاية البيان من أن حكم الصلاة التي صليت بلا إذن الولي موقوف إن أعاد الولي تبين أن الفرض ما صلى الولي، وإن لم يعد سقط الفرض بالأولى ا هـ . فإنه يقتضي أن لمن صلى أولاً أن يصلي مع الولي وليس كذلك، وبما ذكرناه عن الفتاوى المذكورة ظهر ضعف ما في غاية البيان من أن إمام الحي إذا صلى بلا إذن الولي فإن للولي الإعادة وإنما لم يعد إذا صلى السلطان لخوف الازدراء به، وقد صرح في المجمع وشرحه بأن إمام الحي كالسلطان في عدم إعادة الولي. قوله : (ولم يصل غيره بعده) أي بعد ما صلى الولي لأن الفرض قد تأدى بالأولى والتنفل بها غير مشروع إلا لمن له الحق وهو الولي عند تقدم الأجنبي إن قلنا إن إعادة الولي نفل وإلا فلا استثناء، وقد اختلف المشايخ في إعادة من هو مقدم على الولي إذا صلى الولي كالسلطان والقاضي، فذهب صاحب النهاية والعناية إلى أن المراد بالغير من ليس له تقدم على الولي، أما كان مقدماً على الولي فله الإعادة بعد صلاة الولي لأن الولي إذا كان له الإعادة إذا صلى غيره مع أنه أدنى فالسلطان والقاضي لهما الإعادة بالطريق الأولى وهو مصرح به في رواية
Book of Funerals. Section: The Sultan has more right to his [the deceased's] funeral prayer than the guardian. And he [the guardian] may give permission to someone else. If someone other than the guardian and the sultan prayed upon him, the guardian repeats [the prayer], and no one else prays after him. If there are two full brothers [by both parents], the older of them has more right. If the older wants to put forward someone else, the younger may prevent him. If each of them puts forward a different man, then the one put forward by the older has more right. Similarly, two sons [follow this rule], and similarly, paternal cousins. If the younger brother is full [by both parents] and the older is consanguine [by father only], the younger has more right, as in inheritance. If the younger puts forward a grandfather, the older cannot prevent him. If a full brother is absent and writes to someone to go ahead, a consanguine brother may prevent him. The limit of absence is that he cannot go ahead and catch the prayer, and people do not wait for his arrival. A sick person in the city is like a healthy one; he may put forward whomever he wishes, and the more distant cannot prevent him. If a woman dies and she has a father, an adult sane son, and a husband: the father has more right [to lead her prayer] than the son, [but only] if the son is not from the husband; if the son is from the husband, then the husband has more right than the son. If a son dies and he has a father and paternal grandfather, the guardianship belongs to his father, but he puts forward his father, the grandfather of the deceased, out of respect for him. Similarly, a mukatib [slave under contract of manumission] whose slave dies and his master is present: the guardianship belongs to the mukatib, but he puts forward his master out of respect. The master of a slave [who dies] has more right to pray upon him than his free son, according to the fatwa, due to the survival of ownership in a legal sense. Similarly, a mukatib if he dies insolvent; if he leaves solvent estate, and his kitabah [contract] is paid or cash is present without fear of loss or waste, then the son has more right; otherwise, the master. All relatives have more right than the husband; similarly, the master of emancipation and his son, and the patron of clientage, because the marital tie is severed between them by death. And in al-Mujtaba: the neighbor has more right than others. His statement: 'and he may give permission to someone else' means that the guardian may give permission in the funeral prayer. It bears two meanings: one is permission to go ahead [lead], because it is his right so he can cancel it; we have stated that its place is when there is no other guardian or he is distant; if there are two equal guardians and one gives permission to a stranger, the other may prevent him. The second meaning is that he gives permission to people to leave after the prayer before burial, because they should not leave except with his permission. The commentator mentioned another meaning: informing [people] of his death so they pray upon him, especially if the deceased is blessed. Some disliked announcing him in alleys and markets because it is the announcement of the people of Jahiliyyah, and it is disliked; the correct view is that it is not disliked because it increases the multitude of those praying upon him and seeking forgiveness for him, and encourages people purity, reflection, and preparation, and that is not the Jahili announcement; rather, they used to send to tribes announcing with clamor, weeping, wailing, and enumeration, which is disliked by consensus. It is disliked with tahreemi [prohibitory] karahah. He said in al-Nahr: I say: rather, the Sunnah of knowledge necessitates giving preference in that as well. Do you not see what has passed that the imam of the neighborhood is given preference over the guardian only if he is better than him? Yes, al-Quduri justified the dislike of the son giving preference over his father as [because] it contains disrespect. This necessitates obligation of giving him preference absolutely. He said in al-Fath: it is not far-fetched that giving him preference is obligatory by Sunnah. And in al-Bada'i': Abu Yusuf said: by virtue of guardianship, he may give preference to someone else because guardianship belongs to him; he is only prevented from going ahead so that he does not disrespect his father, so his guardianship in giving preference does not fall. Due to the agreed-upon hadith: 'He is not of us who strikes the cheeks, tears the collars, and calls with the call of Jahiliyyah.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah has cursed the shaver, the screamer, and the tearer.' The screamer is she who raises her voice in calamity. There is no harm in shedding tears and weeping without wailing. His statement: 'If someone other than the guardian and sultan prayed upon him, the guardian repeats [the prayer]' because the right belongs to him. And what is meant by sultan is that he has the right to go ahead over the guardian, because the discussion is about when someone who has no right to go ahead goes ahead over the guardian. So the guardian does not have the right to repeat if the judge or his deputy or the imam of the neighborhood prayed, in al-Khulasa, al-Walwalijiyya, al-Zahiriyya, al-Tajnīs, and al-Wāqi‘āt. And if a man prayed while the guardian was behind him and he did not consent, if he prayed with him, he does not repeat because he prayed once, even if he did not follow him. If the one praying is the sultan, the supreme imam in the city, the judge, the governor of the city, or the imam of the neighborhood, he does not have the right to repeat because they are more entitled to the prayer than him; if it is others, he has the right to repeat. The author indicated that the one appointed by will to go ahead is not given precedence over the guardian because the will is invalid according to the fatwa, as stated by the fatwa authorities. They said: if the guardian repeats, the one who prayed upon him should not pray with the guardian again. It appears from their words that if the guardian does not repeat, no one bears sin, because the obligation—fulfilling the right of the deceased—has been performed by the stranger’s prayer; repetition is only for his right, not to drop the obligation. This is more appropriate than what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that the ruling of the prayer performed without the guardian’s permission is suspended: if the guardian repeats, it becomes clear that the obligation was performed by the guardian’s prayer; if he does not repeat, the obligation falls by the first. That implies that the one who prayed first may pray with the guardian, which is not the case. And by what we have mentioned from the aforementioned fatwas, the weakness of what is in Ghayat al-Bayan becomes clear: that if the imam of the neighborhood prays without the guardian’s permission, the guardian may repeat, and he only does not repeat if the sultan prays out of fear of disrespect. It has been stated in al-Majma‘ and its commentary that the imam of the neighborhood is like the sultan in that the guardian does not repeat. His statement: 'and no one else prays after him' means after the guardian has prayed, because the obligation has been performed by the first, and supererogatory [prayer] for it is not permissible except for the one who has the right, which is the guardian when a stranger has gone ahead if we say that the guardian’s repetition is supererogatory; otherwise, no exception. The scholars differed regarding the repetition of one who is given priority over the guardian if the guardian prays, like the sultan and judge. The author of al-Nihaya and al-‘Inaya held that 'other' means one who does not have priority over the guardian; as for one who has priority over the guardian, he may repeat after the guardian’s prayer because if the guardian has the right to repeat when someone else prays despite being less, then the sultan and judge have the right to repeat a fortiori; this is clearly stated in a narration.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq is an expansion (sharh) on the text of Kanz al-Daqa’iq. It begins the section on funeral prayers by addressing who has the primary right (ahaqq) to lead the janazah prayer. The base text states: 'The sultan has more right to his [the deceased's] funeral prayer than the guardian (wali).' This means that the ruling authority or its representative takes precedence over the deceased's legal guardian. The guardian, however, retains the right to delegate (i.e., give permission to another to lead). If someone other than the guardian or sultan leads, the guardian must repeat the prayer, but no one else may pray after that. The commentary then elaborates on hierarchies among relatives: full brothers take precedence by age; if there are two equal guardians, the older's choice is preferred. The passage also discusses the order of priority for a deceased woman: her father, then her son (if not from the husband), but if the son is from the husband, the husband takes precedence. For a deceased male, the father is the guardian but should show respect by letting the grandfather lead. For slaves, the master has priority due to residual ownership. The text also addresses the concept of 'announcement of death' (na’y): some disliked public announcements resembling jahili practices, but the correct Hanafi view permits it as it encourages attendance and reflection, as long as it lacks wailing and lamentation. There is a discussion about the ruling on repeating the prayer: if an unauthorized person leads, the guardian's repetition is valid, but if the sultan, judge, or imam of the neighborhood leads, the guardian does not repeat because they have priority. In the case of a stranger leading without permission, the guardian's repetition is for his own right, not to fulfill an obligation—the obligation is already discharged by the first prayer. The passage also clarifies that if the guardian does not repeat, no sin is incurred. Finally, there is a difference among later scholars (mashayikh) about whether a person who has priority (like the sultan) may repeat after the guardian's prayer; the author of al-Nihaya and al-‘Inaya hold that they may, by primary reasoning (bi al-tariq al-ula).

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The legal guardian of the deceased, who has the primary right to lead the janazah prayer after the sultan. The wali is typically the closest male relative according to inheritance.
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruling authority (the imam or his representative), who has the highest right to lead the funeral prayer over any other person.
الإعادة (al-i‘adah): The repetition of the funeral prayer by the guardian when an unauthorized person led it. This is done to assert the guardian’s right, not because the first prayer was invalid.
النعي (al-na‘y): The public announcement of someone’s death. The text distinguishes between permissible announcement (to invite people to pray) and the prohibited jahili announcement (with wailing and enumerating virtues).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a stranger leads the funeral prayer without the permission of the guardian, what should the guardian do?
A) The guardian must repeat the prayer, but no one else may pray after him.
B) The guardian may not repeat the prayer because the obligation is already fulfilled.
C) The guardian must repeat the prayer, and everyone else who already prayed must repeat as well.
D) The guardian must repeat the prayer, and he may permit others to join if they wish.

Key Takeaway
The guardian must repeat the janazah prayer if an unauthorized person leads, but the first prayer is valid and fulfills the obligation; the sultan and his deputies are exceptions whose priority the guardian cannot override.

The Guardian's Right to Repeat the Funeral Prayer
Expansion of guardian's right to repeat janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when a guardian may repeat the funeral prayer and identify the exceptions based on the status of the person who led the prayer.

Core Idea
The guardian may repeat the janazah unless a higher authority led it.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq details the guardian's right to lead the funeral prayer and when he may repeat it if someone else led without his permission. The ruling distinguishes between those who have precedence (the sultan and his deputies) and ordinary individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The matn states: if someone other than the wali and sultan prays over the deceased, the wali repeats. This establishes the guardian's right to repeat when his right is violated.
2
Determine who counts as a sultan or deputy
From the sharh, 'sultan' includes the ruling authority, qadi, his deputy, imam of the locality, and governor. These are considered 'auli' (more entitled) than the guardian.
The local imam is treated like the sultan in the relied-upon view.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars (from Ghayat al-Bayan) held that the guardian may repeat even if the local imam led, unless it would disrespect the sultan. The mufta bihi view equates the local imam with the sultan, preventing repetition.
The later fatwa works and al-Majma' support the mufta bihi view.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific case (e.g., neighbor vs. qadi leads), decide if the guardian may repeat, justifying with the principles above.
If the person who led is not among the auli, the guardian may repeat.

Source Text

Chapter of Funerals: Section: The Sultan has the greatest right to his prayer. For him is the hadith agreed upon: 'He is not of us who strikes the cheeks, tears the collars, and calls with the call of Jahiliyyah.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'Allah has cursed the shaver, the screamer, and the tearer of clothes.' The screamer is the one who raises her voice in calamity. There is no harm in shedding tears and weeping without wailing. His saying: ('If someone other than the guardian and the sultan prays over him, the guardian repeats') because the right is his. What is meant by sultan is the one who has the right of precedence over the guardian. For the discussion is about when someone who does not have the right of precedence precedes the guardian. The guardian does not repeat if the qadi or his deputy or the imam of the locality prays, according to al-Khulasa, al-Walwaljiyya, al-Zahiriyya, al-Tajnisi, and al-Waqi'at. If a man prays and the guardian is behind him and he does not consent to him, if he prayed with him he does not repeat because he prayed once, even if he did not follow him. If the one who prayed is the sultan or the supreme imam in the town or the qadi or the governor of the town or the imam of the locality, he (the guardian) does not have the right to repeat because they are more entitled to the prayer than him. If it is someone else, he has the right to repeat. The author indicated that the one appointed by will to lead is not given precedence over the guardian because the will is invalid according to the fatwa; the fatwa scholars stated this. They said: if the guardian repeats it, it is not for anyone who prayed it to pray with the guardian again. The apparent meaning of their words is that if the guardian does not repeat, there is no sin on anyone because the obligation, which is fulfilling the right of the deceased, has been fulfilled by the stranger's prayer. Repetition is only for his right, not for discharging the obligation. This is more appropriate than what is in Ghayat al-Bayan, that the ruling of a prayer that was prayed without the guardian's permission is suspended: if the guardian repeats, it becomes clear that the obligation was the guardian's prayer; if he does not repeat, the obligation is discharged by the first prayer. For that implies that the one who prayed first can pray with the guardian, but it is not so. With what we have mentioned from the fatwas, the weakness of what is in Ghayat al-Bayan becomes apparent: that if the imam of the locality prays without the guardian's permission, the guardian has the right to repeat; he only does not repeat if the sultan prays due to fear of disrespect towards him. It has been explicitly stated in al-Majma' and its commentary that the imam of the locality is like the sultan in that the guardian does not repeat.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq begins the chapter on funerals by establishing the basic ruling: the sultan (ruler) has the greatest right to lead the funeral prayer. The text first quotes hadiths prohibiting excessive wailing and self-harm in mourning, then moves to the main subject. The matn states: 'If someone other than the guardian and the sultan prays over him, the guardian repeats.' The commentator explains that this is because the right belongs to the guardian. However, 'sultan' here means anyone who has the right of precedence over the guardian. Thus, if the qadi, his deputy, or the imam of the locality prays, the guardian does not have the right to repeat, because they are considered more entitled to lead than the guardian. If a common person prays and the guardian is present but did not lead, the guardian does not repeat if he prayed with that person, because he has already performed the prayer. The text then distinguishes between those who are 'more entitled' (the sultan, supreme imam, qadi, governor, local imam) and others. For the former, the guardian cannot repeat; for the latter, he may. The author also clarifies that a person appointed by will to lead the prayer (al-musa lahu) is not considered to have precedence; such a will is invalid according to the fatwa. If the guardian does not repeat, there is no sin, because the obligation of the prayer is fulfilled by the first prayer; repetition is solely for the guardian to assert his right. The commentator refutes a contrary view from Ghayat al-Bayan, which claimed that the guardian could repeat even if the local imam prayed, except out of fear of disrespect. The relied-upon position, from al-Majma' and its commentary, equates the local imam with the sultan in this matter.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The legal guardian of the deceased who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer.
سلطان (sultan): The ruling authority or his deputy; has precedence over the guardian in leading the funeral prayer.
إعادة (i'aadah): Repeating the funeral prayer after it has already been performed by someone else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The guardian must repeat the prayer.
B) The guardian may repeat the prayer.
C) The guardian may not repeat the prayer.
D) The prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the guardian's right to repeat the janazah is conditional: he cannot repeat if the sultan, qadi, or local imam led the prayer.

Repeating Funeral Prayer After the Guardian: The Priority Person's Right
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repeating funeral prayer after the guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on whether a priority person may repeat the funeral prayer after the guardian, and apply the harmonized ruling from al-Mujtaba to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Once the guardian prays, no one else may repeat, except a priority person if the guardian transgressed.

The matn states a general rule: after the guardian prays the funeral prayer, no one else prays. However, early Hanafi scholars differed on whether this includes persons with precedence like the sultan or qadi. This passage presents two opposing views and a harmonization that distinguishes based on the presence of the priority person at the time of the guardian's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn says 'And no one else prays after him.' This is the starting point. Understand that once the guardian has prayed, the obligation is fulfilled and no further prayer is normally allowed.
The phrase 'ghayrahu' (other than him) is the key.
2
Note the disagreement
Two groups of Hanafi scholars disagree. One group (Nihayah, 'Inayah) holds that priority persons (muqaddam 'ala al-wali) may repeat. The other (Fatawa, Siraj Wahhaj) says no one, including sultan, may repeat.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the first view's proof
The first view uses qiyas: if the guardian (who is inferior) can repeat when a stranger prays, then the sultan (superior) has an even greater right to repeat. They cite a riwayah in al-Nawadir.
Qiyas awlawi (greater reasoning) is used.
4
Analyze the second view's proof
The second view points to the general rule and the practice of the Companions, where after the rightful person (Prophet or Abu Bakr) prayed, no one repeated. They argue the guardian's right is primary.
They rely on the apparent meaning and historical practice.
5
Understand the harmonization
The commentator and al-Mujtaba reconcile: if the guardian prayed while the priority person was present, the guardian's prayer was a transgression, so the priority person may repeat. If the priority person was absent, the guardian's prayer is valid and no one may repeat.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يصل غيره بعده أي بعد ما صلى الولي لأن الفرض قد تأدى بالأولى والتنفل بها غير مشروع إلا لمن له الحق وهو الولي عند تقدم الأجنبي إن قلنا إن إعادة الولي نفل وإلا فلا استثناء، وقد اختلف المشايخ في إعادة من هو مقدم على الولي إذا صلى الولي كالسلطان والقاضي، فذهب صاحب النهاية والعناية إلى أن المراد بالغير من ليس له تقدم على الولي، أما كان مقدماً على الولي فله الإعادة بعد صلاة الولي لأن الولي إذا كان له الإعادة إذا صلى غيره مع أنه أدنى فالسلطان والقاضي لهما الإعادة بالطريق الأولى وهو مصرح به في رواية النوادر. ويشهد له ما في الفتاوى وفي السراج الوهاج قوله : فإن صلى الولي عليه لم يجز أن يصلي أحد بعده يعني سلطاناً كان أو غيره، ففيه دلالة على تقديم حق الولي من حيث إنه جوز له الإعادة ولم يجوز للسلطان إذا صلى الولي فافهم ذلك ا.هـ. وكذا ذكر المصنف في المستصفى. وقد ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن الأول محمول على ما إذا تقدم الولي مع وجود من هو مقدم عليه لأنه حيث حضر فالحق له فكانت صلاة الولي تعدياً والثاني محمول على ما إذا لم يحضر غير الولي فصلى الولي. ثم جاء المقدم عليه فليس له الإعادة لأن الفرض قد سقط بصلاة من له ولايتها والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في المجتبى ما يفيده قال : فإن صلى عليه الولي لم يجز أن يصلي عليه أحد بعده، وهذا إذا كان حق الصلاة له بأن لم يحضر السلطان، وأما إذا حضر وصلى عليه الولي يعيد السلطان ا هـ.
His saying: ('And no one else prays after him') meaning after the guardian has prayed, because the obligation is already fulfilled by the first prayer, and supererogatory prayer over the dead is not legislated except for the one who has the right, which is the guardian when a stranger precedes, if we say that the guardian's repetition is supererogatory; otherwise there is no exception. The early scholars have differed regarding the repetition of one who has precedence over the guardian when the guardian has prayed, such as the sultan and the qadi. The author of al-Nihayah and al-'Inayah held that what is meant by 'non-other' is one who does not have precedence over the guardian. As for one who has precedence over the guardian, he has the right to repeat after the guardian's prayer, because if the guardian has the right to repeat when someone else prays despite being inferior, then the sultan and qadi have the right to repeat by even greater reason. This is explicitly stated in the riwayah of al-Nawadir. Supporting this is what is in al-Fatawa and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'If the guardian prays over him, it is not permissible for anyone to pray after him, meaning whether sultan or otherwise.' This indicates the preferment of the guardian's right in that he permitted him to repeat and did not permit the sultan when the guardian prayed. Understand this. Similarly, the author mentioned it in al-Mustasfa. The weak servant (the commentator) has concluded that the first view is applied to the case where the guardian preceded while someone with precedence was present, because when such a person is present, the right belongs to him, so the guardian's prayer was a transgression. The second view is applied to the case where no one other than the guardian was present, so the guardian prayed. Then the one with precedence came and he does not have the right to repeat because the obligation is discharged by the prayer of the one who had the authority. And Allah knows best. Then after that I saw in al-Mujtaba something that supports this: he said: 'If the guardian prays over him, it is not permissible for anyone to pray after him, and this is when the right of prayer belongs to him, i.e., the sultan was not present. But if the sultan was present and the guardian prayed, the sultan repeats.'
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario after the guardian has led the funeral prayer. The matn states: 'And no one else prays after him.' The commentator explains that once the guardian has prayed, the obligation is fulfilled, and no additional prayer is legislated as supererogatory except for the guardian himself when a stranger prayed first (as discussed in the previous lesson). However, the early scholars of the Hanafi school differed on whether a person who has precedence over the guardian (such as the sultan or qadi) can repeat the prayer after the guardian has prayed. Two views are presented: (1) The author of al-Nihayah and al-'Inayah, relying on a riwayah in al-Nawadir, hold that such a person can repeat, arguing by analogy: if the guardian (who is inferior) can repeat when a stranger prays, then the sultan (who is superior) has an even greater right to repeat. (2) The fatwa works and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj hold that no one, including the sultan, can pray after the guardian has prayed, because the guardian's right is primary. The commentator (al-ʿAbd al-Daʿif) attempts to harmonize these views by distinguishing the situation: if the guardian prayed despite the presence of someone with precedence, his prayer was a transgression, so the priority person may repeat (first view). If no one with precedence was present, the guardian's prayer is valid and no one may repeat (second view). He then cites al-Mujtaba which supports this harmonization: the sultan may repeat if he was present when the guardian prayed; otherwise, he cannot. This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
مقدم على الولي (muqaddam 'ala al-wali): A person who has precedence over the guardian, such as the sultan, qadi, or local imam.
إعادة نفل (i'aadah nafal): The repetition of the funeral prayer as a supererogatory act (if the guardian repeats after an outsider).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sultan may never repeat after the guardian.
B) The sultan may always repeat after the guardian.
C) The sultan may repeat if he was present when the guardian prayed.
D) The sultan may repeat only if he gives permission to the guardian.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi ruling on repeating a funeral prayer after the guardian distinguishes based on whether a priority person was present; if present and the guardian prayed, the priority person may repeat, otherwise not.

Praying the Funeral Prayer on the Grave
Ruling with proof on janazah prayer at the grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing funeral prayer on the grave after burial, including its condition and proof.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer can be performed on the grave before decomposition — the Prophet's action is our proof.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: when a deceased person is buried without the janazah prayer, the prayer can still be performed at the grave. The key condition is that the body has not yet decomposed. The ruling is supported by the Prophet's own practice and is a mercy for those who missed the prayer before burial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules that if a person is buried without the janazah prayer, it is permissible to pray at the grave. Note the hukm level: it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
2
Recognize the condition
The condition is 'ما لم يتفسخ' (as long as the body has not decomposed). Decomposition invalidates the prayer at the grave.
Decomposition time varies by climate; the body is considered decomposed when decay begins.
3
Understand the prescribed format
The prayer on the grave consists of four takbirs, with praise (thana) recited after the first takbir.
This is the same format as the standard janazah prayer.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed over the grave of an Ansari woman. This action by the Prophet establishes the permissibility.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear and has been accepted by the Hanafi school.
5
Interpret the commentator's note
The commentator states that the author's wording is absolute (mutlaq), meaning the ruling applies to all deceased persons without distinction.
This removes any doubt about applicability to specific individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعده وإن دفن بلا صلاة صلى على قبره ما لم يتفسخ وهي أربع تكبيرات بثناء بعد الأولى لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى على قبر امرأة من الأنصار. أطلقه فشمل ما مر
After that, if he is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave as long as he has not decomposed, and it consists of four takbirs with praise after the first, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, prayed over the grave of a woman from the Ansar. He (the author) gave it absolutely, so it includes what has passed.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that if a deceased person was buried without the funeral prayer (janazah), it can be performed at the grave site. The condition is that the body has not yet decomposed. The prayer on the grave consists of four takbirs, with praise (thana') after the first. The proof is the hadith that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) prayed over the grave of a woman from the Ansar who had been buried without the prayer. The commentator notes that the wording of the matn is absolute (mutlaq), so it applies to any person regardless of status.

Key Terms
تفسخ (tafasukh): Decomposition of the body; the time limit after which the prayer on the grave is no longer valid.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer consisting of four takbirs with specific supplications.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for performing the funeral prayer on the grave after burial?
A) The prayer must be led by the sultan.
B) The body must not have decomposed.
C) The guardian must give permission.
D) The prayer must be performed within three days.

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer is valid on the grave before decomposition, based on the Prophet's action.

The Sultan's Priority in Funeral Prayer: Right or Respect?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sultan versus wali priority in janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the priority between the sultan and the wali in leading the funeral prayer, differentiate between the sultan's presence and absence, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The sultan's priority is one of respect, not inherent right; the wali retains primary authority.

In the Hanafi school, the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a collective obligation (fard kifayah). A key question arises: who is most entitled to lead it? Is it the sultan (ruler) or the wali (guardian/relative)? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute, focusing on whether the sultan's precedence is a matter of inherent right or mere respect, and the implications for repeating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and the dispute
Recognize the two main figures: the sultan (political authority) and the wali (guardian/relative). The dispute is about who has the right to lead the funeral prayer if both are present.
2
Understand the sultan's basis
The sultan's precedence is based on ta'zim (respect), not because the right transfers to him. The wali has the inherent right (haqq) to lead the prayer.
This is a key conceptual distinction.
3
Distinguish presence from absence
If the sultan is absent and the wali prays, it is valid and cannot be repeated. If the sultan is present and the wali prays, the sultan may repeat the prayer as an exception due to respect.
This is the core of the reconciliation.
4
Examine key evidence
Analyze the hadith of the Prophet praying on a forgotten grave and the precedent of Abu Bakr. Understand the Hanafi response that distinguishes cases where no prayer had been performed.
The Shafi'i school uses this hadith to allow repetition unconditionally.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: the sultan may repeat only if he was present when the wali prayed; otherwise, no repetition. The wali's right is primary, and the sultan's priority is a courtesy.
This is the view preferred by later Hanafi scholars like Ibn Nujaym.

Chapter of Funerals: Section: The Sultan is more entitled to his prayer. After it, and if buried without prayer, prayer is performed on his grave as long as he has not decomposed, and it consists of four takbirs with praise after the first, from al-Nawadir. And what is in al-Fatawa bears witness to it, and in al-Siraj al-Wahhab his statement: 'If the guardian performed prayer on him, it is not permissible for anyone to pray after him,' meaning whether sultan or other. So there is evidence of prioritizing the guardian's right in that it permitted him to repeat and did not permit the sultan if the guardian prayed, so understand that. End. And similarly the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa. And it has become apparent to the weak servant that the first is interpreted as when the guardian preceded while one who is given precedence over him was present, because when he is present the right is his, so the guardian's prayer was transgressive. The second is interpreted as when no one other than the guardian was present, so the guardian prayed, then the one given precedence came; he does not have the right to repeat because the obligation has been fulfilled by the one who has authority over it. And Allah knows best. Then after that I saw in al-Mujtaba something that benefits: He said: 'If the guardian prayed on him, it is not permissible for anyone to pray after him. This is when the right of prayer belongs to him because the sultan was not present. But if he was present and the guardian prayed on him, the sultan repeats.' End. His statement: 'And what is in al-Fatawa bears witness to it' means what was mentioned in the previous statement. And in this witnessing there is consideration because what was mentioned from al-Fatawa is that if the sultan and the like prayed, the guardian has no right to repeat because they are more entitled than him. And there is no indication in that that they have the right to repeat if the guardian prayed because the precedence of the sultan and the like is due to the obligation of honoring him and because advancing over him is belittling him, not because the right belongs to them. Rather the right belongs to the guardian, and their precedence over him is accidental. So if the right-holder prayed and did not regard their sanctity, it does not require that they have the right to repeat. And similar is the son with the father; the right belongs to the son but he gives precedence to his father out of respect. And the imam of the district is not refuted because giving him precedence over the guardian is recommended, not obligatory, like giving precedence to the sultan. His statement: 'And it has appeared to the weak servant etc.' said in al-Nahr: There is consideration in it because their words agree that the sultan has no right when he is absent, and you have known the establishment of the dispute when he is present. End. Its conclusion is that he interpreted between the two statements of al-Nihaya and al-Siraj as the case of his presence. As for his absence, it is not a matter of dispute due to the precedence of the sultan if present. Accordingly, what is in al-Mujtaba is like what is in al-Nihaya. And what appears to me is that the statement of al-Nihaya is not specific to the case of his presence; evidence for that is what he mentioned after it from al-Mabsut in answer to the evidence of al-Shafi'i on the permissibility of repetition where he said: 'The prayer on the deceased is not repeated unless the guardian was present, because the right belongs to him and no one else has authority to drop his right. That is the interpretation of the action of the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, because the right was his. Allah says: 'The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than their own selves' (Ahzab 6). And similarly the interpretation of the action of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them: Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, was busy settling affairs and calming the fitna, so they prayed on him before his presence, and the right was his because he was the caliph. When he finished, he prayed on him, and no one prayed after him.' End. This also creates difficulty for the author's reconciliation, as Shaykh Ismail pointed out, unless it is said that no one prayed before the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, nor before Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, who had authority to pray; rather all who prayed were strangers. By this what was mentioned is repelled, but it depends on proving that and that no relative of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, prayed on him before al-Siddiq, which is far-fetched. Contemplate. Then the apparent answer mentioned from al-Mabsut indicates that those who did not pray may pray before the guardian, and that is not intended because of what is in al-Fath and in the two Sahihs: that the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, came to a forgotten grave, lined them up, and pronounced four takbirs. Evidence that he prayed on the grave even though there was no guardian, and that contradicts our madhhab. There is no escape except by claiming that no one had prayed on it at all, which is extremely far from the Companions. End. I say: Rather this claim is absolutely invalid regarding their prayer on him, peace and blessings be upon him.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the priority between the sultan (ruler) and the wali (guardian/relative) in leading the funeral prayer. The core issue is whether the sultan's priority is a matter of inherent right or merely of respect. The text opens by citing a statement from al-Siraj al-Wahhab that if the guardian prayed, no one may repeat, implying the guardian's right is stronger. The author (Ibn Nujaym) then reconciles this with earlier rulings: if the guardian prayed while the sultan was present, it is transgressive; if the sultan was absent, the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed. The discussion involves multiple authorities—al-Fatawa, al-Mustasfa, al-Mujtaba—and critiques by later scholars. The author ultimately leans toward the view that the sultan's precedence is due to respect (ta'zim), not a transfer of right. The hadith of the Prophet praying on a forgotten grave is used by the opponent (Shafi'i?) to argue for permissibility of repeating prayer, but the Hanafi response distinguishes between cases where no prayer occurred and cases where a valid prayer already occurred. The conclusion reaffirms the Hanafi position that the funeral prayer is not repeated once performed by the rightful person.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): The ruler or his representative with authority over public affairs; in this context, the person who leads the funeral prayer due to political authority.
ولي (wali): The guardian of the deceased, usually a close relative (like the son or father) who has the right to lead the funeral prayer.
إعادة (i'ada): Repeating the funeral prayer on the same deceased after it has already been performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated by the sultan.
B) The prayer is valid, but the sultan may repeat it if he wishes.
C) The prayer is valid and no one may repeat it.
D) The sultan must lead a second prayer immediately.

Key Takeaway
The sultan's precedence in the funeral prayer is a mark of respect, not a transfer of the wali's inherent right; repetition is only allowed when the sultan was present and the wali prayed.

Composition of the Janazah Prayer: Four Takbirs and Their Recitations
Ruling on the composition of the funeral prayer: four takbirs with prescribed recitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four takbirs of the funeral prayer and identify the wajib recitation after each takbir.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer consists of exactly four takbirs with specified recitations after each.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a communal obligation with a unique structure. Unlike other prayers, it has no ruku or sujud; instead, it is a sequence of four takbirs punctuated by specific recitations. In this lesson, we examine the basic ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq as explained by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, establishing the canonical Hanafi composition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall structure
Recognize that the funeral prayer is composed of four takbirs (utterances of 'Allahu Akbar'). This is the foundational element.
Other schools may have different numbers, but the Hanafi position is firmly four.
2
List the recitation after each takbir
After the first takbir, recite thana' (praise). After the second, send salawat on the Prophet. After the third, make du'a for the deceased. After the fourth, conclude with two taslims.
Each recitation is a wajib, not a sunnah or rukn.
3
Differentiate between rukn and wajib
The takbirs themselves are arkan (pillars); omitting one invalidates the prayer. The recitations are wajibat (obligatory elements); omitting them makes the prayer valid but makruh, requiring compensation if possible.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
Consider an imam who forgets the salawat after the second takbir. The prayer is still valid, but it is makruh tanzihan; he should not repeat the prayer but may perform sajdah al-sahw if he remembers.
Sajdah al-sahw is not performed in janazah, but the ruling on omission stands.
5
Memorize the sequence
Use the mnemonic 'Thanā, Salawāt, Du'ā, Taslīm' to recall the order after each takbir.
Repetition will reinforce this basic structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وهي أربع تكبيرات بثناء بعد الأولى وصلاة على النبي بعد الثانية ودعاء بعد الثالثة وتسليمتين بعد الرابعة فلو كبر الإمام وصلاة على النبي بعد الثانية ودعاء بعد الثالثة وتسليمتين بعد الرابعة فلو كبر الإمام
His statement: (And it consists of four takbirs: with praise after the first, sending blessings on the Prophet after the second, supplication after the third, and two taslims after the fourth. So if the imam pronounces takbir...
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This brief passage states the standard Hanafi composition of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) specifies that there are four takbirs. After the first takbir, one recites the thana' (praise of Allah, like 'Subhanaka'). After the second, one sends salawat upon the Prophet (e.g., 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'). After the third, one makes du'a (supplication) for the deceased. After the fourth, one makes two taslims (saying 'Assalamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left). This is the basic ruling without additional proofs. The imam leads the prayer following this sequence.

Key Terms
تكبيرات (takbirat): The four utterances of 'Allahu Akbar' that are the pillars of the funeral prayer.
ثناء (thana'): The praise of Allah recited after the first takbir, typically 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'
تسليمتين (taslimatayn): The two final salutations (saying 'Assalamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah') to the right and left to conclude the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi funeral prayer consists of exactly four takbirs: after the first is thana', after the second is salawat, after the third is du'a, and after the fourth are two taslims.

Detailed Rulings on Salat al-Janazah: Grave Prayer and the Four Takbirs
Sharh expanding rulings on funeral prayer, grave prayer, and takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for praying over a grave after burial in the Hanafi school and describe the sequence of the four takbirs in the funeral prayer with their requisite supplications.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is a four-takbir prayer; prayer over the grave is valid only before decomposition, with reliance on dominant opinion.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands the concise matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It first addresses a practical scenario: when a deceased is buried before the funeral prayer. The author discusses the conditions for praying over the grave and the internal Hanafi differences. Then he details the structure of the funeral prayer itself – the four takbirs and what is recited after each. This lesson will guide you through these two core sections, grounding the rulings in their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario for grave prayer
The passage considers a person buried before the funeral prayer. Determine the key conditions: the body must not have decomposed, and there is a debate about whether the body was washed before burial. The relied-upon position does not allow prayer over the grave if exhumation would be required.
Note the difference between burial with or without washing.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Ibn Samā‘a narrates from Muhammad that prayer over the grave is allowed. However, the relied-upon view in Ghāyat al-Bayān holds that it is not allowed because it would require exhuming the grave, which is haram. This is a legitimate difference within the school.
The muftā bihi follows the relied-upon view.
3
Determine the time limit for grave prayer
The prayer is valid only before the body decomposes. Decomposition is judged by the dominant opinion (ghālib al-ra’y) considering climate, body condition, and soil. No fixed time is set; it varies.
This is based on the principle of using ghālib al-ra’y.
4
Analyze the structure of the funeral prayer
The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs. After the first takbir: thanā’ (praise of Allah). After the second: salawāt upon the Prophet. After the third: du‘ā’ for the deceased. After the fourth: two taslīms. This is proven by the Prophet’s prayer over the Negus (Najashi).
The Hanafi school holds that reciting al-Fātiḥa as Qur’ān is not allowed; it may be recited with the intention of supplication.
5
Examine additional details and rulings
The passage also covers the intention in the taslīms (some say to the right and left, not to the deceased), the recommendation to use specific supplications like the one taught by the Prophet, and the ruling on who leads the prayer (the ruler has priority).
These details show the comprehensive nature of the school's treatment.

Source Text

كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته وصلاة على النبي بعد الثانية ودعاء بعد الثالثة وتسليمتين بعد الرابعة فلو كبر الإمام إذا كان مدفوناً بعد الغسل أو قبله كما قدمناه وهو رواية ابن سماعة عن محمد لكن صحح في غاية البيان معزياً إلى القدوري وصاحب التحفة أنه لا يصلى على قبره لأن الصلاة بدون الغسل ليست بمشروعة ولا يؤمر بالغسل لتضمنه أمراً حراماً وهو نبش القبر فسقطت الصلاة ا هـ. وقيد بالدفن لأنه لو وضع في قبره ولم يهل عليه التراب فإنه يخرج ويصلى عليه كما قدمناه، وقيد بعدم التفسخ لأنه لا يصلى عليه بعد التفسخ لأن الصلاة شرعت على بدن الميت فإذا تفسخ لم يبق بدنه قائماً. ولم يقيد المصنف بمدة لأن الصحيح أن ذلك جائز إلى أن يغلب على الظن تفسخه، والمعتبر فيه أكبر الرأي على الصحيح من غير تقدير بمدة. كذا في شرح المجمع وغيره، وظاهره أنه لو شك في تفسخه يصلي عليه، والمذكور في غاية البيان أنه لو شك لا يصلى عليه. رواه ابن رستم عن محمد ا هـ. وإنما كان هذا هو الأصح لأنه يختلف باختلاف الأوقات في الحر والبرد، وباختلاف حال الميت في السمن والهزال، وباختلاف الأمكنة فيحكم فيه غالب الرأي فإن قيل : روي عنه عليه السلام أنه صلى على شهداء أحد بعد ثمانين سنة. فالجواب أن معناه - والله أعلم - أنه دعالهم قال الله تعالى وصل عليهم إن صلاتك سكن لهم ﴾ [التوبة : ۱۰۳] والصلاة في الآية بمنزلة الدعاء. وقيل: إنهم لم تتفرق أعضاؤهم فإن معاوية لما أراد أن يحولهم وجدهم كما دفنوا فتركهم. كذا في البدائع . وحكم صلاة من لا ولاية له كعدم الصلاة أصلاً فيصلي على قبره ما لم يتمزق. كذا في المجتبى . قوله : (وهي أربع تكبيرات بثناء بعد الأولى وصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الثانية ودعاء بعد الثالثة وتسليمتين بعد (الرابعة لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى على النجاشي فكبر أربع تكبيرات وثبت عليها حتى توفي فنسخت ما قبلها والبداءة بالثناء ثم الصلاة سنة الدعاء لأنه المذكور عن المبسوط يؤذن أن لمن لم يصل عليها الصلاة قبل الولي وليس بمراد لما في الفتح وما في الصحيحين أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أتى على قبر منبوذ فصفهم فكبر أربعاً دليل على لم يصل أن يصلي على القبر وإن لم يكن الولي وهو خلاف مذهبنا فلا مخلص إلا بادعاء أنه لم يكن صلى عليها أصلاً وهو في غاية البعد من الصحابة ا هـ . قلت : بل لا يصح هذا الادعاء أصلاً في صلاتهم عليه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم قوله : (بعد ثمانين سنة لعله بعد ثمانية سنين ثم راجعت البدائع فرأيته كذلك فما هنا تحريف . من أن قوله: (وحكم صلاة من لا ولاية له كعدم الصلاة أصلاً) قيل : هذا مخالف لما قدمه الفرض قد تأدى بصلاة الأجنبي . قلت: لم أجد هذه العبارة في المجتبى وإنما الذي فيه : إذا دفن قبل الصلاة أو صلى عليه لا ولاية له يصلى عليه ما لم يتمزق ا هـ . وهذا لا يخالفه لأنه يقال : المراد بصلى
كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته
. أرجى للقبول، ولم يعين المصنف الثناء وروى الحسن أنه دعاء الاستفتاح والمراد بالصلاة الصلاة عليه في التشهد وهو الأولى كما في فتح القدير، ولم يذكر القراءة لأنها لم تثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وفي المحيط والتجنيس : ولو قرأ الفاتحة فيها بنية الدعاء فلا بأس به وإن قرأها بنية القراءة لا يجوز لأنها محل الدعاء دون القراءة ا هـ . ولم يعين المصنف الدعاء لأنه لا توقيت فيه سوى أنه بأمور الآخرة، وإن دعا بالمأثور فما أحسنه وأبلغه . ومن المأثور حديث عوف بن مالك أنه صلى مع رسول الله على جنازة فحفظت من دعائه: اللهم اغفر له وارحمه وعافه واعف عنه وأكرم نزله ووسع مدخله واغسله بالماء والثلج والبرد، ونقه من الخطايا كما ينقى الثوب الأبيض من الدنس ، وأبدله داراً خيراً من داره وأهلاً خيراً من أهله وزوجاً . من زوجه، وأدخله الجنة وأعذه من عذاب القبر وعذاب النار. قال عوف : حتى تمنيت أن أكون أنا ذلك الميت. رواه مسلم. وقيد بقوله بعد الثالثة» لأنه لا يدعو بعد التسليم كما في الخلاصة وعن الفضلي : لا بأس به. ومن لا يحسن الدعاء يقول: اللهم اغفر للمؤمنين والمؤمنات. كذا في المجتبى. ولم يبين المدعو له لأنه يدعو لنفسه أولاً لأن دعاء المغفور له أقرب إلى الإجابة. ثم يدعو للميت وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات لأنه المقصد منها وهو لا يقضي ركنية الدعاء كما توهمه في فتح القدير لأن نفس التكبيرات رحمة للميت وإن لم يدع له. وأشار بقوله وتسليمتين بعد الرابعة إلى أنه لا شيء بعدها غيرهما وهو ظاهر المذهب. وقيل : يقول اللهم آتنا في الدنيا حسنة إلى آخره. وقيل: ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا إلى آخره. وقيل: يخبر بين السكوت والدعاء ولم يبين المنوي بالتسليمتين للاختلاف ففي التبيين وفتح القدير ينوي بهما الميت مع القوم، وفي الظهيرية ولا ينوي الإمام الميت في تسليمتي الجنازة بل ينوي عن يمينه في التسليمة الأولى، ومن عن يساره في التسليمة الثانية ا هـ. وهو الظاهر لأنَّ عليه الولي قضاء لحقه، ويمكن تأويل ما ذكره المؤلف أيضاً بأن يقال معنى قوله كعدم الصلاة أي في حق الولي يعني أنها معتد بها لكن للولي أن يصليها كما لو لم يصل عليه أحد قوله : (وروى الحسن أنه دعاء الاستفتاح قدمنا قبيل قوله ثم إمام الحي أن ظاهر الرواية أنه يحمد قوله: (وفي المحيط والتجنيس الخ قلت ومثله في الولوالجية والتتارخانية عن فتاوى سمرقند، فما ذكره الشرنبلالي في . بعض رسائله وكذا منلا على القاري من أنها مستحبة لثبوت قراءتها عن ابن عباس كما في صحيح البخارى وأنه قال عمداً فعلت ليعلم أنها سنة ولمراعاة الخلاف فإن الشافعي يقول بفرضيتها مخالف للمنقول في كتب المذهب فلا يعوّل عليه وما استدل به الشرنبلالي من قول القنية «ولو قرأ فيها الحمد لله إلى آخر السورة جاز ولو كان ساكناً تجوز صلاته لا دليل له فيه لاحتمال أن المراد قراءتها على قصد الثناء، أو المراد من الجواز الصحة بدليل مقابله فتنبه قوله : (ولم يبين المنوي الخ) قال الرملي وفي إكمال الدراية شرح مختصر الوقاية للشمني ينوي فيهما ما ينوي في تسليمتي صلاته
Book of Funerals: Chapter: The ruler is most entitled to his prayer. And prayer upon the Prophet after the second [takbir] and supplication after the third and two salams after the fourth. Then if the imam said the takbir [over a grave]...
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq concerning the funeral prayer. It begins by addressing the ruling on praying over the grave after burial. The author discusses conditions such as whether the deceased was washed, the prohibition of exhumation, and the time limit based on the likelihood of decomposition. He cites different opinions within the Hanafi school: a narration from Ibn Samā‘a from Muhammad allows prayer over the grave after washing, but the relied-upon position (as in Ghāyat al-Bayān) is that it is not permitted because washing would require exhuming the grave, which is haram. The prayer is valid only before the body decomposes, and the determination of decomposition is based on dominant opinion (ghālib al-ra’y) rather than a fixed time. The passage then transitions to the structure of the funeral prayer itself: four takbirs, with thanā’ after the first, salawāt upon the Prophet after the second, du‘ā’ after the third, and two taslīms after the fourth. This is proven by the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed over the Negus with four takbirs, and this practice abrogated earlier ones. The commentary further explains the recommended supplications, the permissibility of reciting al-Fātiḥa as supplication (not as Qur’ān recitation), and the intention behind the taslīms. The text also addresses intra-Hanafi differences regarding the prayer of one without guardianship and the debate about the recitation of al-Fātiḥa in janazah prayer, affirming the Hanafi position that it is not required as recitation. The overall discussion is a detailed treatment of the funeral prayer’s rulings, proofs, and scholarly differences.

Key Terms
صلاة الجنائز (ṣalāt al-janā’iz): The funeral prayer, a specific prayer consisting of four takbirs without ruku’ or sujud, performed for a deceased Muslim.
تسليم (taslīm): The salutation of peace to the right and left that concludes the funeral prayer.
ثناء (thanā’): Praise of Allah, specifically the supplication regarding the opening of the prayer (du‘ā’ al-istiftāh) or other praise, recited after the first takbir.
غلب الرأي (ghālib al-ra’y): Dominant opinion or preponderant thought; a legal principle used to determine matters where certainty is not possible, such as whether a body has decomposed.
نبش القبر (nabsh al-qabr): Exhumation of a grave, which is considered haram (forbidden) in the Hanafi school except in specific necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct sequence of recitations after the four takbirs in the funeral prayer?
A) After first takbir: salawat; after second: thana; after third: dua; after fourth: one salam.
B) After first takbir: thana; after second: salawat; after third: dua; after fourth: two salams.
C) After first takbir: dua; after second: salawat; after third: thana; after fourth: two salams.
D) After first takbir: thana; after second: dua; after third: salawat; after fourth: one salam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes four takbirs for the funeral prayer with specific supplications, and allows prayer over the grave only before decomposition, with the prohibition of exhumation overriding weaker narrations.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation, Supplication, and Taslim in Funeral Prayer
Rulings with proof on recitation, dua, and taslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on recitation and supplication in janazah prayer and apply the relied-upon view on the intention in the taslim.

Core Idea
In janazah prayer, recitation is not established; the place is for supplication.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq expands the rulings of the funeral prayer, clarifying what is recited after each takbir, the specific dua transmitted from the Prophet (SAW), and the proper intention for the taslim. We'll navigate through the author's explanation to understand the Hanafi position and the intra-madhhab dispute on the imam's intention in the taslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage covers: (1) recitation after the first takbir, (2) the dua after the third takbir, and (3) the taslim after the fourth takbir.
Focus on how the author uses hadith and scholarly disagreement.
2
Analyze the ruling on recitation
Determine the legal status of reciting al-Fatihah in janazah prayer. The text distinguishes between reciting with the intention of qira'a (invalid) and with the intention of dua (valid).
This hinges on the principle that the janazah is a place for dua, not qira'a.
3
Examine the evidence for the dua
The hadith of Awf ibn Malik is cited as evidence for the recommended supplication after the third takbir. Identify its thubut (qat'i) and dalala (zanni) to understand why it is not obligatory.
The hadith is sahih but its wording is not obligatory; it shows recommendation.
4
Understand the taslim dispute
Trace the intra-Hanafi difference on whether the imam intends the deceased in the taslim. The relied-upon view (from al-Zahirah) is that he intends those on his right and left, not the deceased.
The reasoning is that the deceased is not fit for salutation (ahliyya).

كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته . أرجى للقبول، ولم يعين المصنف الثناء وروى الحسن أنه دعاء الاستفتاح والمراد بالصلاة الصلاة عليه في التشهد وهو الأولى كما في فتح القدير، ولم يذكر القراءة لأنها لم تثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وفي المحيط والتجنيس : ولو قرأ الفاتحة فيها بنية الدعاء فلا بأس به وإن قرأها بنية القراءة لا يجوز لأنها محل الدعاء دون القراءة ا هـ . ولم يعين المصنف الدعاء لأنه لا توقيت فيه سوى أنه بأمور الآخرة، وإن دعا بالمأثور فما أحسنه وأبلغه . ومن المأثور حديث عوف بن مالك أنه صلى مع رسول الله على جنازة فحفظت من دعائه: اللهم اغفر له وارحمه وعافه واعف عنه وأكرم نزله ووسع مدخله واغسله بالماء والثلج والبرد، ونقه من الخطايا كما ينقى الثوب الأبيض من الدنس ، وأبدله داراً خيراً من داره وأهلاً خيراً من أهله وزوجاً . من زوجه، وأدخله الجنة وأعذه من عذاب القبر وعذاب النار. قال عوف : حتى تمنيت أن أكون أنا ذلك الميت. رواه مسلم. وقيد بقوله بعد الثالثة» لأنه لا يدعو بعد التسليم كما في الخلاصة وعن الفضلي : لا بأس به. ومن لا يحسن الدعاء يقول: اللهم اغفر للمؤمنين والمؤمنات. كذا في المجتبى. ولم يبين المدعو له لأنه يدعو لنفسه أولاً لأن دعاء المغفور له أقرب إلى الإجابة. ثم يدعو للميت وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات لأنه المقصد منها وهو لا يقضي ركنية الدعاء كما توهمه في فتح القدير لأن نفس التكبيرات رحمة للميت وإن لم يدع له. وأشار بقوله وتسليمتين بعد الرابعة إلى أنه لا شيء بعدها غيرهما وهو ظاهر المذهب. وقيل : يقول اللهم آتنا في الدنيا حسنة إلى آخره. وقيل: ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا إلى آخره. وقيل: يخبر بين السكوت والدعاء ولم يبين المنوي بالتسليمتين للاختلاف ففي التبيين وفتح القدير ينوي بهما الميت مع القوم، وفي الظهيرية ولا ينوي الإمام الميت في تسليمتي الجنازة بل ينوي عن يمينه في التسليمة الأولى، ومن عن يساره في التسليمة الثانية ا هـ. وهو الظاهر لأنَّ عليه الولي قضاء لحقه، ويمكن تأويل ما ذكره المؤلف أيضاً بأن يقال معنى قوله كعدم الصلاة أي في حق الولي يعني أنها معتد بها لكن للولي أن يصليها كما لو لم يصل عليه أحد قوله : (وروى الحسن أنه دعاء الاستفتاح قدمنا قبيل قوله ثم إمام الحي أن ظاهر الرواية أنه يحمد قوله: (وفي المحيط والتجنيس الخ قلت ومثله في الولوالجية والتتارخانية عن فتاوى سمرقند، فما ذكره الشرنبلالي في . بعض رسائله وكذا منلا على القاري من أنها مستحبة لثبوت قراءتها عن ابن عباس كما في صحيح البخارى وأنه قال عمداً فعلت ليعلم أنها سنة ولمراعاة الخلاف فإن الشافعي يقول بفرضيتها مخالف للمنقول في كتب المذهب فلا يعوّل عليه وما استدل به الشرنبلالي من قول القنية «ولو قرأ فيها الحمد لله إلى آخر السورة جاز ولو كان ساكناً تجوز صلاته لا دليل له فيه لاحتمال أن المراد قراءتها على قصد الثناء، أو المراد من الجواز الصحة بدليل مقابله فتنبه قوله : (ولم يبين المنوي الخ) قال الرملي وفي إكمال الدراية شرح مختصر الوقاية للشمني ينوي فيهما ما ينوي في تسليمتي صلاته البحر الرائق ج ٢ م ٢١

خمساً لم يتبع ولا يستغفر لصبي ولا لمجنون ويقول اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً واجعله لنا أجراً وذخراً واجعله لنا شافعاً ومشفعاً وينتظر المسبوق ليكبر معه لا من كان حاضراً أئمة الميت لا يخاطب بالسلام عليه حتى ينوي به إذا ليس أهلاً له.
Chapter of Funerals: Section: The Sultan is most entitled to lead the prayer. It is more likely for acceptance, and the author did not specify the praise, and it is narrated from Hasan that it is the opening supplication, and the meaning of 'prayer' here is sending blessings upon him in the tashahhud, which is preferable as in Fath al-Qadir. He did not mention recitation because it is not established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). In al-Muhit and al-Tajnis: If one recites al-Fatihah in it with the intention of supplication, there is no problem, but if he recites it with the intention of recitation, it is not permissible because it is a place for supplication rather than recitation. The author did not specify the supplication because there is no specific timing other than that it should be about matters of the afterlife, and if one supplicates with the transmitted supplication, how excellent and eloquent it is. Among the transmitted supplication is the hadith of Awf ibn Malik that he prayed with the Messenger of Allah over a funeral and memorized from his supplication: O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, keep him safe, pardon him, honor his resting place, expand his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail, purify him from sins as a white garment is purified from dirt, replace his home with a better home, his family with a better family, and his spouse with a better spouse, admit him to Paradise, grant him refuge from the punishment of the grave and the punishment of the Fire. Awf said: I wished that I were that deceased person. Narrated by Muslim. He restricted it by saying 'after the third' because he does not supplicate after the taslim as mentioned in al-Khulasa, and from al-Fadli: there is no problem. And whoever does not know supplication says: O Allah, forgive the believing men and women. Similarly in al-Mujtaba. He did not specify for whom to supplicate because one supplicates for oneself first since the supplication of one who is forgiven is more likely to be answered. Then he supplicates for the deceased and for believing men and women because that is the purpose of it, and it does not necessitate the pillar of supplication as mistakenly understood in Fath al-Qadir because the takbirs themselves are a mercy for the deceased even if one does not supplicate. He indicated by his saying 'and two taslims after the fourth' that there is nothing after them except these two, which is the apparent madhhab. It is said: one says 'Our Lord, grant us in this world good...' etc. It is said: 'Our Lord, do not let our hearts deviate...' etc. It is said: he chooses between silence and supplication. He did not specify the intention for the two taslims due to difference: in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir, one intends by them the deceased along with the people; in al-Zahirah, the imam does not intend the deceased in the taslims of the funeral prayer but intends those on his right in the first taslim and those on his left in the second taslim. This is the apparent view because ... The guardian may make up what is owed to him, and the author's statement can be interpreted as meaning 'like the absence of prayer' i.e. regarding the guardian, meaning it is valid but the guardian may pray it as if no one had prayed over him. His statement: (It is narrated from Hasan that it is the opening supplication) we mentioned before near his saying 'then the imam of the neighborhood' that the apparent narration is that he praises. His statement: (In al-Muhit and al-Tajnis etc.) I say: Similar in al-Walwalijiyya and al-Tatarkhaniyya from the fatwa of Samarqand. So what al-Shurnabulali mentioned in some of his treatises and also Mulla Ali al-Qari that it is recommended due to the confirmation of its recitation from Ibn Abbas as in Sahih al-Bukhari and that he said intentionally to show it is sunna and to consider the difference (since Shafi'i says it is obligatory) is contrary to what is transmitted in the madhhab books and is not relied upon. And what al-Shurnabulali argued from the saying of al-Quniyya: 'If one recites al-Hamd to the end of the surah, it is permissible; if he is silent, his prayer is allowed' is no proof for him because it is possible that what is meant is reciting it with the intention of praise, or the meaning of permissibility is validity as opposed to its opposite. So beware. His statement: (He did not specify the intention) al-Ramli said: In Ikmal al-Diraya commentary on Mukhtasar al-Wiqqaya by al-Shamni, one intends in them what one intends in the taslims of his prayer. Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 2, p. 21. Five ... he does not follow and does not seek forgiveness for a child or an insane person, and he says: O Allah, make him our forerunner, make him our reward and treasure, make him our intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted. The latecomer waits to make takbir with him, not the one who was already present. The imams of the deceased are not addressed with greetings of peace until he intends the deceased because he is not fit for it.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary of Al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the rulings of the funeral prayer. The author clarifies that the recommended practice is not to recite the Fatihah as formal recitation but as supplication, citing a hadith from Muslim. The dua after the third takbir is emphasized, with specific transmitted phrases. The number of taslims is two after the fourth takbir, following the apparent Hanafi position. There is a difference among Hanafi scholars regarding the intention of the imam in the taslim: some say he intends the deceased and the congregation, others say he intends those on his right and left. The relied-upon view is the latter. The passage also covers supplication for a child or insane person, and the ruling that the latecomer should wait for the imam to complete takbirs. The overall tone is a detailed expansion of the matn, providing proofs and resolving differences.

Key Terms
دعاء الاستفتاح (du'a al-istiftah): The opening supplication said at the beginning of prayer; here, it refers to the praise recited after the first takbir in janazah prayer.
تسليمتين (taslimatayn): The two greetings of peace (taslim) at the end of the funeral prayer, after the fourth takbir.
المدعو له (al-mad'u lahu): The person for whom supplication is made; here, the imam first prays for himself, then for the deceased and all believers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, whom does the imam intend in the taslim of the funeral prayer?
A) The deceased alone.
B) The deceased and all present.
C) Those on his right and left.
D) Only the men in the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is a place for supplication, not recitation; the relied-upon view on taslim is that the imam intends the congregation, not the deceased.

Raising Hands in Janazah and Following the Imam in Ijtihadi Matters
Inter-madhhab dispute on raising hands in janazah and principle of following the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of following the imam in matters of ijtihad to the case of raising hands in funeral prayer and distinguish it from definitively abrogated practices.

Core Idea
In ijtihadi matters, follow your imam; only refuse in definitively abrogated or non-sunnah acts.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common scenario: a Hanafi praying behind a Shafi'i imam who raises his hands during the funeral prayer takbirs. While the Hanafi school's apparent position is not to raise hands except at the opening takbir, the text explains that this is a matter of ijtihad, not a settled certainty. Therefore, the follower should follow the imam, just as he would follow in additional Eid takbirs or qunut in witr. The key is distinguishing between mujtahad fihi and what is definitively abrogated, like qunut in Fajr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
Determine what act is being debated: raising hands in the funeral prayer takbirs.
This act is not clearly settled in the Hanafi school.
2
Classify its status
Is it a matter of ijtihad (mujtahad fihi) or definitively abrogated? The text shows it is ijtihadi because Hanafi scholars differed on it.
The Balkh scholars' choice to raise hands indicates it is not abrogated.
3
Apply the principle of mutaba'at al-imam
Cite the hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed' and the Hanafi rule that following the imam is wajib in ijtihadi matters.
The follower must abandon his own opinion for the imam's in such matters.
4
Distinguish from definitively abrogated acts
Compare with qunut in Fajr, which is either abrogated or definitively non-sunnah. Here, the follower does not follow the imam.
The difference is the certainty about the act's status.

Source Text

وقد تقدم في كيفية الصلاة أنه لا ترفع الأيدي في صلاة الجنازة سوى تكبيرة الافتتاح وهو ظاهر الرواية، وكثير من بلخ اختاروا رفع اليد في تكبيرة فيها، وكان نصير بن يحيى يرفع تارة ولا يرفع أخرى. ولا يجهر بما يقرأ عقب كل تكبيرة لأنه ذكر والسنة فيه المخافتة كذا في البدائع. وفيه وهل يرفع صوته بالتسليم لم يتعرض له في ظاهر الرواية، وذكر الحسن بن زياد أنه لا يرفع لأنه للإعلام ولا حاجة له لأن التسليم مشروع عقب التكبير بلا فصل ولكن العمل في زماننا على خلافه وفي الفوائد التاجية : إذا سلم على ظن أنه أتم التكبير ثم علم أنه لم يتم فإنه يبني لأنه سلم في محله وهو القيام فيكون معذوراً. وفي الظهيرية وغيرها : رجل كبر على جنازة فجيء ا هـ. وينوي الميت بدل الإمام ا هـ. وفي التبيين وينوي بالتسليمتين كما وصفناه في صفة الصلاة وينوي الميت كما ينوي الإمام ا.هـ. فظاهر كلام الشمني عدم نية الإمام وهو مخالف لما في التبيين،
