السلام على الموتى قوله : ( وكثير من أئمة بلخ اختاروا رفع اليد الخ قال الرملي :أقول: ربما يستفاد من . هذا أن الحنفي إذا اقتدى بالشافعي فالأولى متابعته في الرفع ولم أره تأمل ا هـ . أقول : وجه الاستفادة أن اختيار أئمة بلخ الرفع دليل على أنه ليس منسوخاً ولا مقطوعاً بعدم سنيته بل هو مجتهد فيه. وقد نص علماؤنا الحنفية على أن المقتدي في صلاة العيد يتبع الإمام فيما زاد على الثلاث في تكبيرات الزوائد ما لم يجاوز المأثور كما مر أي لأنه مجتهد فيه، وكذا يتبع الشافعي إذا قنت للوتر بعد الركوع، وعللوه أيضاً بأنه مجتهد فيه ولا يتابعه في قنوت الفجر خلافاً لأبي يوسف لأنه إما منسوخ على تقدير أنه كان سنة ثم ترك، أو مقطوع بعدم سنيته بناء على أنه كان دعاء على قوم شهراً. وعد في الدر المختار من واجبات الصلاة متابعة الإمام في المجتهد فيه لا في المقطوع بنسخه أو بعدم سنيته كقنوت فجرا وظاهره وجوب المتابعة في رفع اليدين هنا لأنه مجتهد فيه ليس مقطوعاً بنسخه ولا بعدم سنيته بدلیل اختلاف علمائنا فيه، وقد نص في البدائع على وجوب متابعة الإمام في تكبيرات الزوائد على العيد ما لم يكبر تكبيراً لم يقل به أحد من الصحابة قال : لأنه تبع لإمامه فيجب عليه متابعته وترك رأيه برأي الإمام لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه) (۱) وقوله عليه السلام تابع إمامك على أي حال وجدته» فما لم يظهر
It has preceded in the description of the prayer that hands should not be raised in the funeral prayer except for the opening takbir, and that is the apparent narration. Many from Balkh chose to raise the hands in its takbir, and Nasir ibn Yahya would raise sometimes and not raise at other times. One should not recite aloud what one reads after each takbir because it is dhikr and the sunnah is to be silent in it, as in al-Bada'i. It contains: Should he raise his voice in the taslim? It is not addressed in the apparent narration, and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad mentioned that he does not raise his voice because it is for notification and there is no need for it since the taslim is legislated immediately after the takbir without a gap, but the practice in our time is contrary to that. In al-Fawaid al-Tajiya: If one makes taslim thinking that he completed the takbir then knows that he did not complete, he builds upon it because he made taslim in its place, which is standing, so he is excused. In al-Zahirah and others: A man made takbir over a funeral and then (something) came. He intends the deceased instead of the imam. In al-Tabyin, one makes intention with the two taslims as we described in the description of prayer, and intends the deceased as the imam intends. So the apparent statement of al-Shamni is that the imam does not make intention, and it contradicts what is in al-Tabyin. What should be relied upon is what is in al-Tabyin, as there is no reason to exclude the imam from that. And his statement here that 'the deceased is not fit' is not accepted, and there will come what is reported about the people of the grave: 'Peace be upon you, O people of the believers' and the Prophet's teaching of greeting the dead. His statement: (Many imams of Balkh chose raising the hands...) al-Ramli said: I say: Perhaps from this it can be understood that if a Hanafi is led by a Shafi'i, it is better to follow him in raising hands, and I have not seen it considered. He said: The benefit is that the choice of the imams of Balkh for raising hands is evidence that it is not abrogated nor definitively without sunnah status; rather it is a matter of ijtihad. Our Hanafi scholars have stated that the follower in Eid prayer follows the imam in the additional takbirs beyond the three, as long as he does not exceed what is transmitted (because it is a matter of ijtihad). Similarly, he follows the Shafi'i if he performs qunut in witr after ruku', and they also justified it as a matter of ijtihad. He does not follow him in qunut of Fajr, contrary to Abu Yusuf, because it is either abrogated (assuming it was sunnah then abandoned) or definitively non-sunnah based on it being a supplication against a tribe for a month. It is counted in al-Durr al-Mukhtar among the obligations of prayer to follow the imam in matters of ijtihad, not in those definitively abrogated or non-sunnah, such as qunut of Fajr. Its apparent meaning is the obligation to follow in raising hands here because it is a matter of ijtihad, not definitively abrogated nor non-sunnah, due to the difference among our scholars. It has been stated in al-Bada'i' that it is obligatory to follow the imam in the additional takbirs of Eid as long as he does not make a takbir that no companion reportedly made, because the follower must follow his imam and abandon his own opinion for the imam's opinion due to the hadith: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed, so do not differ with him' and his saying: 'Follow your imam whatever state he is in' so unless it becomes apparent...
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling of raising hands in funeral prayer. The apparent Hanafi position (zahir al-riwaya) is not to raise hands except at the first takbir. However, many scholars from Balkh chose to raise hands, showing it is a matter of ijtihad. The text then extends to the principle of following an imam (especially a Shafi'i) in actions that are matters of ijtihad, such as raising hands, additional takbirs in Eid, and qunut in witr. The key distinction is between matters that are definitively abrogated or not sunnah (like qunut in Fajr) and those that are still subject to ijtihad. The hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed' is cited as evidence. The author concludes that raising hands in janazah is such a matter, so a Hanafi following a Shafi'i imam should follow him in raising hands.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during takbir in prayer; here specifically in funeral prayer.
مجتهد فيه (mujtahad fihi): A matter open to ijtihad, not settled definitively; here it refers to raising hands in janazah.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; here referring to qunut in Fajr being abrogated, so it cannot be followed.
متابعة الإمام (mutaba'at al-imam): Following the imam in prayer actions; here extended to actions that are matters of ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should a Hanafi follower raise his hands in funeral prayer according to this passage?
A) Always, at every takbir.
B) Never, under any circumstance.
C) Only when following an imam who raises hands, as it is a matter of ijtihad.
D) Only at the opening takbir, as per the apparent narration.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi follower must follow the imam in ijtihadi matters like raising hands in janazah, but not in definitively abrogated acts like qunut in Fajr.

Following the Imam's Fifth Takbira in Funeral Prayer
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih on fifth takbira

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following the Imam's fifth takbira in funeral prayer, explain the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The follower must not follow the Imam in an abrogated act, and should wait until the Imam says salam.

The funeral prayer in the Hanafi school consists of four takbirs. If the Imam mistakenly says a fifth, the follower faces a dilemma: should he immediately end his prayer to show dissent, or remain in prayer to follow the Imam in the obligatory parts? This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute on the correct course of action, resolving it through the principle of abrogation (mansukh) and the duty to follow the Imam in matters of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states: 'If the Imam says five (takbirs), he (the follower) does not follow.' Understand why: the fifth takbira is considered abrogated (mansukh) in the Hanafi school, and the follower must not follow in an abrogated act.
Abrogation here means the practice was later cancelled by the Prophet's action or stronger evidence.
2
Examine the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
The commentator reports two positions: one says the follower should say salam immediately to completely dissent from the Imam; the other says he should wait until the Imam says salam, then say salam with him.
Both are attributed to Abu Hanifa, showing that even within the school there is a difference of opinion.
3
Analyze the basis of each narration
The immediate salam position emphasizes complete dissent. The waiting position emphasizes following the Imam in what is obligatory (the four takbirs and the rest of the prayer) while avoiding the fifth.
The hadith 'The Imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him' supports waiting, as long as the difference is not in a clearly abrogated act.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position
The commentator says the fatwa is on the narration that he waits, as mentioned in al-Waqi'at and favored by Fath al-Qadir. The reasoning: remaining in the state of prayer after completion is not absolutely wrong; the error is only in following the fifth takbira.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
5
Extend the principle to similar cases
The commentator later discusses the general rule: the follower must follow the Imam in matters subject to ijtihad (mujtahad fih), but not in matters definitively abrogated (mansukh) or established as non-sunnah.
This principle applies to e.g., Qunut in Witr, extra takbirs in Eid, and raising hands in funeral prayer.

بجنازة أخرى فكبر ينويه ونوى أن لا يكبر على الأولى فقد خرج من الأولى إلى صلاة الثانية، وإن كبر الثانية ينوي بها عليهما لم يكن خارجاً. وعن أبي يوسف : إذا كبر ينوي به التطوع وصلاة الجنازة جاز عن التطوع ا هـ
هـ.
قوله : (فلو كبر الإمام خمساً لم يتبع) لأنه منسوخ ولا متابعة فيه ولم يبين ماذا يصنع، وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان : في رواية يسلم للحال ولا ينتظر تحقيقاً للمخالفة، وفي رواية يمكث حتى يسلم . معه إذا سلم ليكون متابعاً فيما تجب فيه المتابعة وبه يفتى. كذا في الواقعات. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن البقاء في حرمة الصلاة بعد فراغها ليس بخطأ مطلقاً إنما الخطأ في المتابعة في الخامسة، وفي بعض المواضع إنما لا يتابعه في الزوائد على الأربعة إذا سمع من الإمام أما إذا لم يسمع إلا من المبلغ فيتابعه وهذا حسن وهو قياس ما ذكروه في تكبيرات العيدين ا هـ. وذكر ابن الملك في شرح المجمع قالوا : وينوي الافتتاح عند كل تكبيرة الجواز أن تكبيرة الإمام للافتتاح الآن وأخطأ المنادي . وقيد بتكبيرات الجنازة لأن الإمام في العيد لو زاد على ثلاث فإنه يتبع فيها حتى لو تجاوز الامام في التكبير حد الاجتهاد لا يتابع أيضاً. كذا في شرح المجمع قوله : (ولا يستغفر لصبي ولا لمجنون ويقول اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً واجعله لنا أجرا وذخراً واجعله لنا شافعاً ومشفعاً) كذا ورد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولأنه لا ذنب لهما . والفَرَط بفتحتين الذي يتقدم الإنسان من
لأنه مجتهد
خطؤه بيقين كان اتباعه واجباً الخ لكن رأيت بعد ذلك في شرح المقدمة الكيدانية للقهستاني نقلاً عن الجلابي أنه لا يتابع إمامه في رفع اليدين في الجنازة فتأمل قوله : (قالوا وينوي الافتتاح عند كل تكبيرة الخ) إن كان المراد بقوله عند كل تكبيرة ما زاد على الرابعة فهل يكبر بعد سكوت المنادي شيئاً أم لا، ومقتضى كونه ينوي بذلك الافتتاح أن يأتي بعده بثلاث لتتم صلاته إلا أن يقال: إن نية الافتتاح للاحتياط فلا ينافي أن تكون صلاته تامة بدون زيادة لكن لو كبر المنادي خمساً وقلنا إنه ينوي بالخامسة الافتتاح يكون لا فائدة فيه لأن نيته للافتتاح في الخامسة لا تفيده ما لم يأت بعدها بثلاث أخر، وإن كان المراد أنه ينوي الافتتاح بجميع التكبيرات التي أتى بها ففيه أن النية لا تكون بعد المنوي بل من معه، ومن أين يعلم المقتدي أن المنادي يزيد على الأربعة حتى ينوي الافتتاح عند كل تكبيرة كبرها إلا أن يحمل على أنه متى كان بعيداً عن الإمام
هي
هي
ويعلم أنه لا : يسمع تكبيره بل يأخذ من المنادي يلزمه أن ينوى بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح لاحتمال خطأه في الأولى وأن الثانية هي ا الصواب، أو أنه أخطأ في الثانية أيضاً وأن الثالثة . الصواب، وهكذا فينوي بالكل الافتتاح لكن هذا مع بعده لا يتقيد بحال الزيادة على الأربع لوجود العلة، وحينئذ فما فائدة هذه النية لأنه لو كانت الأولى أو الثانية خطأ. من المنادي سبق بها الإمام كانت الثالثة . الصواب، وكذا الرابعة فيلزم صلاة الجنازة بتكبيرتين ولا تصح بدون الأربع. والحاصل أنه لم يظهر لنا وجه هذا القول فليتأمل وليراجع قوله : (ويقول اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً الخ) أي بعد قوله ومن توفيته منا فتوفه على الإيمان» كما في شرح المنية لإبراهيم الحلبي، وظاهر كلام غيره الاقتصار على قوله واللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً». ثم اعلم أن قول المصنف «لا يستغفر لصبي يرد عليه ما في الحديث اللهم اغفر لحينا وميتنا ، وشاهدنا وغائبنا، وصغيرنا
He does not follow (the Imam) if he says five (takbirs), nor does he ask forgiveness for a child or an insane person, and he says: 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner, and make him for us a reward and a treasure, and make him for us an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.' And the one who is preceded (in some takbirs) waits to say takbir with him, not he who was present. ... The dead person is not addressed with salutation until he intends it, because he is not eligible for it. And it has preceded in the description of the prayer that hands are not raised in the funeral prayer except for the opening takbirah, and this is the apparent (position) of the riwayah. And many of the imams of Balkh chose raising the hands in it. ... And he does not raise his voice in what he recites after each takbirah because it is remembrance and the sunnah in it is lowering the voice, as in al-Bada'i. ...
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of funeral prayer, specifically addressing the issue of the Imam saying more than four takbirs. The matn states that the follower should not follow the Imam if he says five takbirs, because the fifth is abrogated. The commentator explains that there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one says the follower should say salam immediately to completely disagree, and the other says he should wait until the Imam says salam to maintain following in what is obligatory. The relied-upon position is to wait. The text then discusses the du'a for a child, stating that one should not ask forgiveness (since the child has no sins) but instead say the specific du'a reported from the Prophet. The commentary also covers the intention of the Imam for the deceased, and the ruling on raising hands, noting that the Zahir al-Riwayah says hands are not raised except for the opening takbir, but many Balkhi scholars chose to raise them. The commentator then delves into the principle of following the Imam in matters of ijtihad, using examples like Qunut in Witr and the extra takbirs in Eid, concluding that the follower must follow the Imam in matters that are subject to ijtihad and not clearly abrogated. Finally, it discusses the situation when the muballigh (announcer) makes an error in the number of takbirs, and a ruling about intending the opening takbir at each takbir for caution.

Key Terms
المنسوخ (al-mansukh): Abrogated; the fifth takbira in funeral prayer is considered abrogated, so it is not followed.
المجتهد فيه (al-mujtahad fih): Matters that are subject to ijtihad, i.e., not definitively established or abrogated, where different opinions are valid.
المخالفة (al-mukhalafah): Dissent; the act of showing opposition to the Imam's error by not following him in the abrogated act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what should a follower do if the Imam says five takbirs in the funeral prayer?
A) Say salam immediately to show dissent.
B) Wait until the Imam says salam and then say salam with him.
C) Say the fifth takbirah along with the Imam.
D) Leave the prayer and restart.

Key Takeaway
The follower must not follow the Imam in an abrogated act; the relied-upon position is to wait silently until the Imam salam, thereby maintaining the obligation of following in the essential parts of the prayer.

Following the Imam in the Fifth Takbir of Funeral Prayer
Explains the ruling when imam says five takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi ruling when the imam says five takbirs and explain the two narrations from Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
The fifth takbir is abrogated; follower must not follow it but wait for the imam's salam.

In the funeral prayer, the imam sometimes utters a fifth takbir. Does the follower follow? The Hanafi school teaches that the fifth takbir is abrogated, so following it is wrong. But what exactly should the follower do? This passage explores two narrations from Abu Hanifa and settles on the relied-upon practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The follower should not follow the fifth takbir because it is abrogated (mansukh). The matn does not specify the follower's action, so we need the two narrations.
2
Identify the two narrations
First narration: follower says salam immediately to complete opposition. Second narration: follower waits until imam says salam, maintaining the bond of following in the wajib parts.
3
Determine the mufta bihi
The second narration (wait) is preferred by later authorities like al-Karkhi and al-Marghinani because remaining in prayer after completion is not wrong; only following the fifth is wrong.
4
Note the exception via mubligh
If the follower only hears the takbirs through a mubligh (relayer) and the mubligh adds a fifth, the follower does follow that fifth, analogous to Eid takbirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو كبر الإمام خمساً لم يتبع لأنه منسوخ ولا متابعة فيه ولم يبين ماذا يصنع، وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان : في رواية يسلم للحال ولا ينتظر تحقيقاً للمخالفة، وفي رواية يمكث حتى يسلم معه إذا سلم ليكون متابعاً فيما تجب فيه المتابعة وبه يفتى. كذا في الواقعات. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن البقاء في حرمة الصلاة بعد فراغها ليس بخطأ مطلقاً إنما الخطأ في المتابعة في الخامسة، وفي بعض المواضع إنما لا يتابعه في الزوائد على الأربعة إذا سمع من الإمام أما إذا لم يسمع إلا من المبلغ فيتابعه وهذا حسن وهو قياس ما ذكروه في تكبيرات العيدين ا هـ.
If the imam says five takbirs, he is not to be followed because it is abrogated and there is no following in it, and it is not clarified what he should do. From Abu Hanifa there are two narrations: in one narration he says the salam immediately and does not wait to actualize the opposition; in another narration he remains until the imam says salam to be a follower in what must be followed, and this is what is given as fatwa. So in al-Waqi'at. And it was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because remaining in the sanctity of prayer after its completion is not absolutely wrong; the wrong is only in following in the fifth. And in some places he should not follow him in the extras beyond four if he heard from the imam, but if he only heard from the mubligh then he follows him, and this is good and is analogous to what they mentioned regarding the Eid takbirs.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author explains that if the imam says five takbirs in the funeral prayer, the follower should not follow in the fifth because it is abrogated (mansukh). The matn did not state what the follower should do, so two narrations from Abu Hanifa are given: 1) the follower says salam immediately to oppose the innovation; 2) the follower waits until the imam says salam to maintain following in what is obligatory. The mufta bihi is the second view, as preferred in Fath al-Qadir, because remaining in a state of prayer after completion is not intrinsically wrong—only following in the fifth is wrong. An exception: if the follower only hears through a mubligh (relayer) and the mubligh adds a fifth, the follower does follow in that fifth, analogous to the Eid takbirs where the follower follows the mubligh's relay.

Key Terms
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated: a ruling that was previously valid but later overturned by a stronger evidence.
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): Following the imam in actions of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam says five takbirs in the funeral prayer, what should the follower do according to the mufta bihi view?
A) Say the fifth takbir with the imam.
B) Say salam immediately after the fourth.
C) Wait until the imam says salam.
D) Leave the prayer and repeat it.

Key Takeaway
The fifth takbir in the funeral prayer is abrogated; the follower must not follow it but wait for the imam's salam.

Supplication for Deceased Child or Insane Person
Explains Hanafi funeral supplication for sinless deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi funeral supplication for a child or insane person and explain why istighfar is omitted.

Core Idea
For a sinless child, seek not forgiveness but that he be your forerunner and treasure.

In the funeral prayer, the supplication for a deceased adult includes seeking forgiveness. But for a child or an insane person, who are not accountable for sins, the Prophet taught a different prayer. This passage from Bahar al-Ra'iq explains that we do not say 'O Allah, forgive him' but rather ask Allah to make the deceased a means of reward and intercession for the family.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects of the ruling
The passage deals with two categories of deceased: a minor child (sabi) and an insane person (majnun). Both are not legally responsible (mukallaf) and thus sinless.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the child died before or after birth, as long as it was born alive.
2
Note the prohibition of istighfar
The text explicitly states 'do not seek forgiveness' for them. This is because istighfar is for sins, and they have none.
Some other schools allow seeking mercy (rahmah) but Hanafi reserves special du'a.
3
Learn the prescribed supplication
Memorize the du'a: 'Allahumma ij'alhu lana faratan, wa ij'alhu lana ajran wa dhukhran, wa ij'alhu lana shafi'an wa mushaffa'an.' Understand each term.
The terms are explained in the commentary: farat (forerunner), ajr (reward), dhukhr (stored treasure), shafi' mushaffa' (accepted intercessor).
4
Understand the reasoning behind the wording
The author discusses the meaning of 'farat' to avoid repetition with 'ajr'. The preferred interpretation is 'one who goes ahead to the watering place' symbolizing the child preceding the family to Paradise.
This also reflects the hadith where the Prophet says 'I am your forerunner at the Hawd'.
5
Apply the ruling to a related case: slave owner
The author adds that although not explicitly found, it is befitting to supplicate for the owner of a deceased slave during the funeral prayer, similar to supplicating for the parents of a free child.
This is an extension (qiyas) based on the idea that the owner loses property and may need reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يستغفر لصبي ولا لمجنون ويقول اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً واجعله لنا أجرا وذخرا واجعله لنا شافعاً ومشفعاً) كذا ورد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولأنه لا ذنب لهما . والفَرَط بفتحتين الذي يتقدم الإنسان من ولده، يقال اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً أي أجراً متقدماً ، والفرط الفارط وهو الذي يسبق الوراد إلى الماء، وفي الحديث أنا فرطكم على الحوض، أي أتقدكم إليه . كذا في ضياء الحلوم. والأنسب هو المعنى الثاني هنا كما اقتصر عليه في غاية البيان لئلا يلزم التكرار في قوله واجعله لنا أجراً» . والذخر بضم الذال وسكون الخاء الذخيرة، والمشفَع بفتح الفاء مقبول الشفاعة. وذكر اليمني في شرح الشهاب في بحث إنما الأعمال بالنيات أن الثواب هو الحاصل بأصول الشرع والحاصل بالمكملات يسمى أجراً لأن الثواب لغة بدل العين والأجر بدل المنفعة فالمنفعة تابعة للعين، وقد يطلق الأجر ويراد به الثواب وبالعكس اهـ. ولم أر من صرح بأنه يدعو لسيد العبد الميت وينبغي أن يدعو له فيها كما يدعو للميت .
His saying: (And do not seek forgiveness for a child or an insane person, and say: O Allah, make him for us a forerunner and make him for us a reward and a stored treasure and make him for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted) – thus it is reported from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and because they have no sin. Al-farat (with two fatha) is the one who precedes from one's children. It is said 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner' meaning an advanced reward. And al-farat is the one who precedes to the watering place. In the hadith: 'I am your forerunner at the Hawd' meaning I precede you to it. So in Diya' al-Hulum. The more appropriate is the second meaning here as was limited in Ghayat al-Bayan to avoid repetition in his saying 'and make him for us a reward'. And al-dhukhr (with damm on dhal and sukun on kha') is the stored treasure. And al-mushaffa' (with fatha on fa') is one whose intercession is accepted. Al-Yamani mentioned in his commentary on al-Shihab in the discussion on 'Actions are by intentions' that thawab is what is obtained by the foundations of sharia, and what is obtained by completions is called ajr (reward) because thawab linguistically is the exchange of the substance and ajr is the exchange of the benefit, so the benefit is a follower of the substance, and sometimes ajr is used to mean thawab and vice versa. And I have not seen anyone explicitly stating that the owner of a deceased slave should be supplicated for, but it is befitting to supplicate for him in it as one supplicates for the deceased.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This is a ruling about the specific supplication for a deceased child (sabi) or insane person (majnun) in the funeral prayer. The author states: do not seek forgiveness (istighfar) for them because they have no sins. Instead, say the supplication taught by the Prophet: 'O Allah, make him a forerunner (farat), a reward (ajr), a stored treasure (dhukhr), and an intercessor whose intercession is accepted (shafi'an mushaffa'an).' The word 'farat' is explained: it can mean 'advanced reward' or 'one who goes ahead to the watering place' (like the Prophet who precedes his ummah to the Hawd). The commentator prefers the second meaning to avoid repetition with 'ajr'. The term 'dhukhr' means something stored for future benefit. 'Mushaffa'' means one whose intercession is granted. The author adds a note: though not explicitly stated, one should also supplicate for the owner of a deceased slave if the slave is owned, just as one supplicates for the parents of a free child.

Key Terms
الفرط (al-faraṭ): A forerunner; one who goes ahead to a watering place; also an advanced reward.
الذخر (al-dhukhr): Stored treasure; something saved for future reward.
المشفع (al-mushaffa'): One whose intercession is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on saying 'Allahumma ighfir lahu' for a deceased child in the funeral prayer?
A) It is sunnah
B) It is wajib
C) It is not done; instead say the specific du'a
D) It is permissible but not recommended

Key Takeaway
For a sinless deceased (child or insane), omit istighfar and recite the prophetic du'a making them a forerunner, reward, treasure, and intercessor.

Latecomer in Funeral Prayer: Waiting or Starting Immediately?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on latecomer in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer in funeral prayer and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Wait for the imam's next takbir; each takbir is like a rak'ah.

In funeral prayer, each takbir is integral. What should a latecomer do when arriving after the imam has begun? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the authoritative Hanafi position and the objection of Abu Yusuf. The analogy (qiyas) to regular prayer's rak'ahs guides the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn and the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The latecomer must wait for the imam's next takbir and start with that.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that the latecomer can start immediately with his own takbir al-tahrima upon arrival.
Opponent within the same madhhab.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil: the first takbir is purely for opening (tahrima), so the latecomer can perform it independently.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: each takbir in funeral prayer stands in the place of a rak'ah. The latecomer cannot begin with what he missed because that would be performing an action not in sync with the imam, breaking the congregation.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to regular prayer where a latecomer joins with what the imam is currently doing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a latecomer starts immediately (per Abu Yusuf), his prayer is considered invalid by the majority, though some texts say it is not invalid but not valid? The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وينتظر المسبوق ليكبر معه من كان حاضراً في حالة التحريمة) أي وينتظر المسبوق في صلاة الجنازة تكبير الإمام ليكبر مع الإمام للافتتاح فلو كبر الإمام تكبيرة أو تكبيرتين لا يكبر الآتي حتى يكبر الأخرى بعد حضوره عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف : يكبر حين يحضر لأن الأولى للافتتاح والمسبوق يأتي به، ولهما : إن كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ركعة والمسبوق لا يبتدئ بما فاته إذ هو منسوخ كذا في الهداية. وهو مفيد لما ذكرناه أن التكبيرات الأربع أركان وليست الأولى شرطاً كما توهمه في فتح القدير، إلا أن يكون على قول أبي يوسف كما لا يخفى ولو كبر كما حضر ولم ينتظر لا تفسد عندهما لكن ما أداه غير في الخلاصة، وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو أدرك الإمام بعد ما كبر الرابعة فاتته الصلاة
His saying: (And the latecomer should wait to say takbir with those present in the state of the opening takbir) – meaning the latecomer in the funeral prayer should wait for the takbir of the imam so that he says takbir with the imam for the opening. So if the imam has already said one or two takbirs, the newcomer should not say takbir until he says the next one after his arrival, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He should say takbir upon arrival because the first is for opening and the latecomer performs it. Their proof: Each takbir is in place of a rak'ah, and the latecomer does not begin with what he missed because it is abrogated – so in al-Hidayah. And this benefits what we mentioned that the four takbirs are pillars and the first is not a condition as was imagined in Fath al-Qadir, unless it be on the saying of Abu Yusuf as is not hidden. And if he says takbir upon arrival and does not wait, it is not invalid according to them, but what he performed is not valid? – in al-Khulasa. And the author indicated that if he catches the imam after the fourth takbir, the prayer is missed.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage addresses the rule for a latecomer (masbuq) in the funeral prayer. The matn says: the latecomer should wait to say takbir with the imam who is already present in the state of the opening takbir (tahrima). The commentator explains: if the imam has already said one or two takbirs, the latecomer should not start his own prayer immediately; rather, he should wait until the imam says the next takbir and then start with that, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf disagrees, saying the latecomer should say the opening takbir immediately upon arrival because the first takbir is for opening and he can perform it now. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is based on qiyas: each takbir in the funeral prayer is like a rak'ah in regular prayer; the latecomer cannot begin with what he has missed (i.e., the earlier takbirs) because they are abrogated (i.e., they cannot be made up). This clarifies that the four takbirs are integral parts (arkan), not conditions. If the latecomer does not wait and says takbir immediately, the prayer is not invalid according to them, but what he performed is not considered valid? There is a note from al-Khulasa. Finally, if the imam has already said the fourth takbir, the latecomer misses the entire funeral prayer.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the prayer late, having missed one or more takbirs.
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a latecomer do in the funeral prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?
A) Start his prayer immediately with his own opening takbir.
B) Wait until the imam says the next takbir and start with that.
C) Leave the prayer and wait for the next funeral.
D) Join the imam's prayer but not say the opening takbir.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a latecomer to funeral prayer must wait for the imam's next takbir to start his prayer, as each takbir is analogous to a rak'ah.

Supplication for a Deceased Slave Child
Guidance on making du'a for a deceased slave child, suggesting du'a for the master instead of parents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended supplication for a deceased slave child and explain why the master is supplicated for instead of the parents, based on Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
For a deceased slave child, supplicate for the master, not the parents, because the master's right supersedes.

In the Hanafi school, the recommended du'a for a deceased child slave is directed to the master rather than the parents. This ruling is based on the master's primary right over the slave. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains this nuance, with an important difference of interpretation regarding adult slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
From the passage, state the recommended action (sunnah) for making du'a when a slave child dies. Who should be the focus of the supplication?
The text says one should supplicate for the master (sayyid) of the slave child.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is the master supplicated for instead of the parents? What principle from Hanafi fiqh supports this?
The master has more right (ahaqq) over the slave than the parents. Additionally, the parents of a slave child are often non-Muslims, so supplication for them may not be appropriate.
3
Analyze the interpretive expansion
Al-Ramli interprets the term 'abd (slave) in the matn as referring specifically to a child slave (al-sabi al-mamluk). Why does he restrict it? What is the apparent meaning of the matn?
The matn's apparent meaning includes adult slaves, but al-Ramli narrows it to minors based on the context of du'a for a child and the assumption of non-Muslim parents.
4
Note the disagreement
What is the difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding adult slaves? How does this affect the practice?
Some scholars hold that the ruling applies only to child slaves; for adult slaves, one should supplicate as for a free adult (i.e., not specifically for parents/master). Others maintain the general application.
5
Formulate the final position
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position according to later Hanafi authorities?
The relied-upon position is to supplicate for the master of a slave child, as stated by al-Ramli. For adult slaves, the ruling is not explicitly extended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وينبغي أن يدعو له فيها الخ) قال الرملي قال في شرح المنية وفي المفيد : ويدعو لوالدي الطفل، وقيل يقول اللهم ثقل به موازينهما وأعظم به أجرهما ولا تفتنهما بعده، اللهم اجعله في كفالة إبراهيم وألحقه بصالحي المؤمنين ا هـ . ثم قال الرملي : والمراد بالعبد في كلامه هنا الصبي. وقوله وينبغي أن يدعو له فيها كما يدعو للميت لعله كما يدعو لأبوي الميت يعني الصغير، ووجه كلامه أن السيد أحق به من أبويه فإذا دعا لأبويه المسلمين فبالأولى الدعاء لسيده المسلم، وأما الكبير مطلقاً فلم يصرح أحد بالدعاء لوالديه فكذلك السيده بل يدعو لا له كما يدعو للحر الكبير فتأمل ا.هـ. وحاصله أن المراد بالعبد في كلام المؤلف العبد الصغير لأن الحر الصغير يدعو لأبويه، وأما العبد الصغير فالغالب كون أبويه كافرين فينبغي أن يدعو لسيده بدل أبويه، ولا يخفى أن حمل كلام المؤلف على هذا بعيد لأنه لم يذكر الدعاء لأبوي الحر الصغير حتى يقيس عليه العبد الصغير ويجعل سيده بمنزلة الأبوين، بل المتبادر من كلامه العبد الكبير لكن الداعي للشيخ خير الدين حمله على ذلك ما ذكره بقوله وأما الكبير مطلقاً الخ
He said: 'And it is recommended that he supplicate for him in it, etc.' Al-Ramli said in Sharh al-Munyah and in al-Mufid: And he supplicates for the parents of the child, and it is said: O Allah, make him a weight in their scales, and magnify his reward for them, and do not tempt them after him. O Allah, place him in the care of Ibrahim and join him with the righteous believers. Then al-Ramli said: The meaning of 'slave' (al-'abd) in his statement here is the child (al-sabi). And his statement 'and it is recommended that he supplicate for him in it as he supplicates for the deceased' – perhaps it is as he supplicates for the parents of the deceased, meaning the child. The reasoning of his statement is that the master has more right to him than his parents, so if he supplicates for his Muslim parents, then more so for his Muslim master. As for the adult (al-kabir) absolutely, no one has explicitly stated supplication for his parents, so similarly for his master. Rather, he supplicates for him as he supplicates for the free adult. So reflect. The conclusion is that what is meant by 'slave' in the author's statement is the child slave, because for the free child, one supplicates for his parents. As for the child slave, most often his parents are disbelievers, so one should supplicate for his master instead of his parents. It is not hidden that interpreting the author's statement in this way is far-fetched, because he did not mention supplication for the parents of the free child so that he could analogize the child slave to it and make his master like the parents. Rather, the apparent meaning of his statement is the adult slave, but the caller (al-da'i) for Shaykh Khayr al-Din interpreted it in this way based on what he mentioned in his statement: 'As for the adult absolutely, etc.'
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommendation of making du'a for a deceased child who is a slave. The commentator, al-Ramli, explains that for a free child, one supplicates for the parents, but for a slave child, since the master has the right of ownership and guardianship, one should supplicate for the master instead, especially if the slave child's parents are likely disbelievers. However, the author of the matn seems to have intended the general rule for any slave, child or adult, but the later explanation narrows it to child slaves. The commentary shows a difference of interpretation: the more apparent reading is that the rule applies to adult slaves as well, but some scholars restrict it to minors. This reflects the Hanafi attention to detail in applying general principles of du'a and the rights of masters. The teacher should note that the recommended du'a includes asking Allah to make the child a source of reward for the master and to join him with the righteous.

Key Terms
العبد (al-'abd): In this context, interpreted by al-Ramli as a child slave (al-sabi al-mamluk), though the author's text might indicate an adult slave.
السيد (al-sayyid): The master of the slave, who has the right of ownership and guardianship over the slave child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, for whom should one primarily supplicate when a slave child dies?
A) The slave child's parents
B) The slave child's master
C) The slave child himself
D) The imam of the mosque

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends supplicating for the master of a deceased slave child, not the parents, based on the master's superior right, with a debated extension to adult slaves.

The Latecomer in Funeral Prayer: The Dispute on Waiting for the Takbir
Commentary on the ruling of the latecomer waiting for imam's takbir in funeral prayer, including intra-Hanafi dispute and fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the latecomer in funeral prayer, explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Each takbir in funeral prayer is like a rak'ah; the latecomer must wait for the imam's next takbir, but the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf in some cases.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) consists of four takbirs without bowing or prostration. When a worshipper arrives late, the question arises: should he wait for the imam to say the next takbir so he can join at that point, or should he say the opening takbir immediately upon joining? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule that he must wait, while Imam Abu Yusuf holds that he should begin at once. This lesson unpacks the proofs for each view, the practical impact of the difference, and the later fatwa position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the latecomer (mashuq) arriving during the funeral prayer. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he must wait for the imam to say his next takbir before reciting his own opening takbir.
This is the view of the majority of the early Hanafi masters.
2
Analyze the proof for waiting
The proof is qiyas: each takbir in funeral prayer is equivalent to a rak'ah in regular prayer. Just as a latecomer in regular prayer does not begin with the rakah he missed, the latecomer here does not begin with a missed takbir. Also, the rule that a latecomer can start with what he missed has been abrogated.
This analogy was stated in al-Hidayah.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that the first takbir is specifically for the opening (iftitah), and the latecomer should perform it upon arrival, just as he would say the opening takbir if he were starting fresh.
He does not accept the analogy to a rak'ah.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The majority responds that the first takbir is a pillar (rukn) like any other takbir, not a condition. The analogy to a rak'ah takes precedence because each takbir is a distinct unit of the prayer. The latecomer must join the imam in the same takbir, not start his own.
The opening takbir being a pillar is a key point.
5
Determine the practical consequence and fatwa
If the latecomer does not wait and says takbir immediately, his prayer is not invalidated (according to the majority) but what he performed is not considered valid (he must repeat after the imam's salam). According to Abu Yusuf, it is valid. The later fatwa leans toward Abu Yusuf's view in some scenarios, especially when the imam has already completed four takbirs.
The text says 'upon it is the fatwa' from al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وينتظر المسبوق ليكبر معه من كان حاضراً في حالة التحريمة) أي وينتظر المسبوق في صلاة الجنازة تكبير الإمام ليكبر مع الإمام للافتتاح فلو كبر الإمام تكبيرة أو تكبيرتين لا يكبر الآتي حتى يكبر الأخرى بعد حضوره عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف : يكبر حين يحضر لأن الأولى للافتتاح والمسبوق يأتي به، ولهما : إن كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ركعة والمسبوق لا يبتدئ بما فاته إذ هو منسوخ كذا في الهداية. وهو مفيد لما ذكرناه أن التكبيرات الأربع أركان وليست الأولى شرطاً كما توهمه في فتح القدير، إلا أن يكون على قول أبي يوسف كما لا يخفى ولو كبر كما حضر ولم ينتظر لا تفسد عندهما لكن ما أداه غير في الخلاصة، وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو أدرك الإمام بعد ما كبر الرابعة فاتته الصلاة قوله : (كذا) في (الخلاصة) قال في النهر : وتبعه في : على قولهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف وأفاد أنه لو جاء بعد التكبيرة الأولى فإنه يكبر بعد سلام الإمام عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف، ثم عندهما يقضي ما فاته بغير دعاء لأنه لو قضى الدعاء رفع الميت فيفوت له التكبير، وإذا رفع الميت قطع التكبير لأن الصلاة على الميت ولا ميت يتصور. وفي الظهيرية ولو رفعت بالأيدي ولم توضع على الأكتاف ذكر في ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يأتي وإنما لا ينتظر من كان حاضراً حالة التحريمة اتفاقاً لأنه بمنزلة المدرك، ألا ترى أنه لو كبر تكبيرة الافتتاح بعد الإمام يقع أداء لا قضاء. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كبر الإمام للثانية أو لم يكبر فإن لم يكبر الإمام الثانية كبر الحاضر للأولى للحال وإن لم يكبر الحاضر حتى كبر الإمام الثانية كبر معه الثانية وقضى الأولى للحال كذا في المجتبى. وكذا إن لم يكبر في الثانية والثالثة والرابعة يكبر ويقضي ما فاته للحال . قال في المحيط : ولو كبر الإمام أربعاً والرجل حاضر فإنه يكبر ما لم يسلم الإمام ويقضي الثلاث وهذا قول أبي يوسف وعليه الفتوى وقد روى الحسن أنه لا يكبر وقد فاتته ا هـ . فما في الحقائق من أن الفتوى على قول صدر فتح القدير وقضية عدم اعتبار ما أداه أنه لا يكون شارعاً في تلك الصلاة، وحينئذ فتفسد التكبيرة مع أن المسطور في القنية أنه يكون شارعاً، وعليه فيعتبر ما أداه وهذا لم أر من أفصح . عنه فتدبره ا هـ . وأجيب بأنه لا يلزم من عدم اعتباره عدم شروعه ولا من اعتبار شروعه اعتبار ما أداه، ألا ترى أن من أدرك الإمام في السجود صح شروعه مع أنه لا ما أداه . يعتبر من السجود مع الإمام، بل عليه إعادته إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به فلا مخالفة بين ما في الخلاصة والقنية ا.هـ. وهو حسن قوله: (من كان حاضراً حالة التحريمة) قيد الحضور في الدرر بكونه خلف الإمام والظاهر أنه اتفاقي لأن عبارة المجتبى الآتية : رجل واقف حيث يجزئه الدخول في صلاة الإمام قوله : (ذكر في ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يأتي) أي بالتكبير ويخالفه ما قاله في البزازية : فإن رفعت على الأيدي ولم توضع على الأكتاف كبر في الظاهر، وعن محمد لا إذا كان أقرب إلى الأكتاف وإن أقرب إلى الأرض كبر ا هـ . وينبغي أن يعول على ما في البزازية لأنه كما قال في الفتح لو رفعت قطع التكبير إذا رفعت على الأكتاف، وعن محمد إن كان الأرض أقرب يأتي بالتكبير لا إذا كان إلى الأكتاف أقرب وقيل لا يقطع حتى تباعد ولا يخالفه ما سنذكر من أنها لا تصح إذا كان الميت على أيدي الناس لأنه يغتفر في البقاء ما لا يغتفر في الابتداء. كذا في الشرنبلالية قوله : (كبر الحاضر للأولى للحال وكذا قوله وقضى الأولى للحال) أي قبل سلام الإمام وسينبه المؤلف على خلافه عن الواقعات وفي شرح الشيخ إسماعيل عن المنتقى بالقاف ثم يكبر ثلاثاً قبل أن ترفع الجنازة، وفي الولوالجية وعليه الفتوى، وفي النهر يكبر ما زاد على التحريمة بعد الفراغ نسقاً إن خشي رفع الميت على الأعناق حتى لو رفع على الأيدي كبر في ظاهر الرواية، لا فرق في ذلك بين المدرك واللاحق نص على ذلك غير واحد، فما في المجتبى أنه يكبر الكل للحال شاذ قوله: (ولو) كبر الإمام أربعاً والرجل حاضر) أي حاضر من أول التكبيرات كما هو المتبادر بقي ما لو حضر بعد التحريمة وكبر الإمام الثانية بعد حضوره هل ينتظر أو اهـ. من
He said: 'And the latecomer should wait so that he may say the takbir with him, meaning with the imam, at the time of the opening takbir. If the imam has said one or two takbirs, the latecomer should not say takbir until the imam says the next one after his arrival, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He should say takbir immediately upon arrival because the first takbir is for the opening and the latecomer should perform it. Their argument: Each takbir is equivalent to a rak'ah, and the latecomer does not begin with what he missed because that has been abrogated. This is in al-Hidayah. It is useful for what we mentioned: that the four takbirs are pillars (arkan) and the first is not a condition, as was imagined in Fath al-Qadir, except according to Abu Yusuf's opinion. And if he says takbir upon arrival without waiting, the prayer is not invalid according to them, but what he performed is not valid according to al-Khulasa. The author indicated that if he catches the imam after the fourth takbir, the prayer is missed. He said: 'Thus in al-Khulasa' – he said in al-Nahr: and he followed him in – according to their opinion, contrary to Abu Yusuf, and it indicates that if he comes after the first takbir, he should say takbir after the imam's salam according to them, contrary to Abu Yusuf. Then according to them, he should make up what he missed without du'a because if he makes up the du'a, the deceased would be lifted, and he would miss the takbir. When the deceased is lifted, the takbir is cut off because the prayer is upon the deceased and there is no deceased imaginable. In al-Zahiriyya: If the bier is raised on hands and not placed on shoulders, it is mentioned in the apparent narration that he does not come. And he does not wait for those present at the time of the opening takbir by agreement, because he is like one who catches up. Do you not see that if he says the opening takbir after the imam, it occurs as a performance (ada') not as a make-up (qada')? He left it general, so it includes whether the imam said the second takbir or not. If the imam did not say the second takbir, the one present says the first immediately. If he does not say it until the imam says the second, he says the second with him and makes up the first immediately. This is in al-Mujtaba. Similarly, if he does not say the second, third, and fourth, he says takbir and makes up what he missed immediately. He said in al-Muhit: If the imam said four takbirs and a man is present, he says takbir as long as the imam has not given salam, and he makes up three. This is the opinion of Abu Yusuf, and the fatwa is upon it. Al-Hasan narrated that he does not say takbir and has missed it. So what is in al-Haqa'iq that the fatwa is upon the opinion of the author of Fath al-Qadir and the implication of not considering what he performed is that he is not entering into that prayer, and then the takbir becomes invalid, whereas in al-Qunyah it is stated that he is entering, so what he performed is considered. I have not seen anyone explain this clearly, so reflect. And it was answered: It does not necessitate that not considering it means he did not enter, nor does considering that he entered necessitate that what he performed is considered. Do you not see that the one who catches the imam in prostration enters correctly even though what he performed is not considered from the prostration with the imam? Rather, he must repeat it when he stands to make up what preceded him. So there is no contradiction between what is in al-Khulasa and al-Qunyah. This is good. He said: 'Those present at the time of the opening takbir' – the condition of presence in al-Durar is that he is behind the imam, and apparently it is agreed upon because the phrase of al-Mujtaba later: a man standing where it is permissible for him to enter the imam's prayer. He said: 'It is mentioned in the apparent narration that he does not come' – meaning the takbir, and it contradicts what he said in al-Bazzaziyya: If it is raised on hands and not placed on shoulders, he says takbir in the apparent opinion, and from Muhammad, no, if it is closer to the shoulders, and if it is closer to the ground, he says takbir. It is better to rely on what is in al-Bazzaziyya because, as he said in al-Fath, if it is raised, the takbir is cut off when it is raised on the shoulders. From Muhammad: If the ground is closer, he says the takbir, not if it is closer to the shoulders. And it is said: It does not cut off until it is distant. This does not contradict what we will mention that it is not valid if the deceased is on the hands of people, because what is forgiven in continuity is not forgiven in initiation. This is in al-Shurnubulaliyya. He said: 'The one present says the first immediately' – and similarly his statement: 'and makes up the first immediately' – meaning before the imam's salam, and the author will later mention his disagreement with al-Waqi'at. In the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il from al-Muntaqa bi al-Qaf, then he says three takbirs before the bier is raised. In al-Wilwalijiyya, and the fatwa is upon it. In al-Nahr: He says what is additional to the opening takbir after finishing consecutively if he fears the bier will be raised on the necks, such that if it is raised on the hands, he says takbir in the apparent narration. There is no difference in that between the one who catches up and the latecomer; multiple scholars have stated this. So what is in al-Mujtaba that he says all immediately is anomalous. He said: 'And if the imam said four and the man is present' – meaning present from the beginning of the takbirs, as is apparent. It remains: if he came after the opening takbir and the imam says the second after his presence, does he wait or ...? End.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on the latecomer (mashuq) in the funeral prayer. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The core issue is whether the latecomer should wait for the imam's next takbir or immediately start with the opening takbir. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that the latecomer must wait for the imam to begin the next takbir so he can join with the imam in the same takbir. This is based on an analogy: each takbir in the funeral prayer is like a rak'ah in regular prayer, and the latecomer does not start with what he missed. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that the first takbir is for opening the prayer, and the latecomer should perform it upon arrival. The text also discusses various scenarios: if the imam has already done multiple takbirs, if the bier is lifted, and the fatwa position (which leans towards Abu Yusuf's view in some aspects). The passage then delves into the disagreement about whether the latecomer's takbir is considered valid if he does not wait, and whether he is considered to have entered the prayer. The commentary resolves apparent contradictions between al-Khulasa and al-Qunyah by explaining that entering the prayer and making up what was missed are two different matters. The later parts of the passage provide detailed rulings on when the latecomer should say his missed takbirs—whether immediately or after the imam's salam—and the effect of the bier being lifted. Throughout, the teacher should note that the Hanafi school has multiple views, and the mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) is often Abu Yusuf's view that the latecomer says takbir immediately upon arrival, though there is also a narration that he should wait.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-mashuq): The person who arrives late to the funeral prayer and misses some takbirs of the imam.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of the funeral prayer, which initiates the prayer.
الخلاصة (al-Khulasa): A fiqh work by Imam al-Tahawi? Actually, al-Khulasa is a famous Hanafi fiqh summary. Here, it is cited for the ruling that what the latecomer performs if he does not wait is not valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling when the imam has already completed four takbirs and a person arrives before salam?
A) He should not join because the prayer is missed.
B) He should say takbir immediately and then make up three takbirs.
C) He should wait for the imam to do a fifth takbir.
D) He should say takbir after the imam's salam.

Key Takeaway
The latecomer in funeral prayer faces an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require waiting for the next takbir, while Abu Yusuf permits immediate opening takbir; the later fatwa follows Abu Yusuf in certain scenarios.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Latecomer's Makeup of Takbirs in Janazah Prayer: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains how a latecomer to janazah prayer performs missed takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on how a latecomer (masbuq) makes up missed takbirs in janazah prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A latecomer to janazah prayer must not recite du'a between makeup takbirs; timing depends on whether he is a mudrik or masbuq.

Salat al-janazah consists of four takbirs with specific recitations. When someone joins late, he must make up missed takbirs, but the Hanafi school has multiple views on how and when. The two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rule that makeup occurs after the imam's salam without du'a, while Abu Yusuf holds that one should say remaining takbirs with the imam and then make up three after salam. A weak narration from al-Hasan says the prayer is lost. This lesson unpacks these positions and their resolution through the distinction between mudrik (present at tahrimah) and masbuq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The issue is how a person who misses one or more takbirs in janazah prayer should complete them. Specifically, whether he makes them up immediately or after the imam's salam, and whether he recites du'a between them.
2
State the Position of the Two Companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
According to the two companions, if a person arrives after the first takbir, he says the remaining takbirs after the imam's salam without supplication (du'a). Reason: if he made up du'a, the bier might be lifted, and then the takbir would be missed entirely.
This is the position in zahir al-riwayah.
3
State Abu Yusuf's Alternate Position (Mufta Bihi)
Abu Yusuf holds that if the imam says four takbirs and the person is present from the beginning, he should continue saying takbirs with the imam as long as the imam hasn't said salam, then make up the three missed takbirs after salam. This view is relied upon for fatwa.
Despite being a companion of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf differed on this specific issue.
4
Distinguish Mudrik vs Masbuq
The text resolves contradictions between earlier sources by distinguishing between a mudrik (one present at the opening takbir) and a masbuq (one who joins later). A mudrik may make up missed takbirs immediately during the prayer, while a masbuq waits until after the imam's salam.
This distinction explains why al-Mujtaba says immediate makeup (for a lahiq) and al-Waqi'at says after salam (for a masbuq).
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
In practice, a latecomer should not recite du'a between his makeup takbirs. If he is present from the beginning but delays his takbir, he becomes a masbuq for the missed ones and must make them up after the imam's salam, not immediately.

حالة التحريمة ويقوم للرجل والمرأة بحذاء الصدر ولم يصلوا ركباناً ولا في مسجد
أبي يوسف إنما هو في مسألة الحاضر لا في مسألة المسبوق. وقد يقال : إن الرجل إذا كان حاضراً ولم يكبر حتى كبر الإمام اثنين أو ثلاثاً فلا شك أنه مسبوق كما لو كان حاضراً وقد صلى الإمام ركعة أو ركعتين فإنه مسبوق، وحضوره من غير فعل لا يجعله مدركاً فينبغي يكون كالمسألة الأولى. وأن يكون الفرق بين الحاضر وغيره إنما هو في التكبيرة الأولى فقط
أن
كما لا يخفى. وفي الواقعات وإن لم يكبر الحاضر حتى كبر الإمام ثنتين كبر الثانية منهما ولم يكبر الأولى حتى يسلم الإمام لأن الأولى ذهب محلها فكان قضاء والمسبوق لا يشتغل بالقضاء قبل فراغ الإمام ا . هـ. وهو مخالف لما ذكرناه عن المجتبى من أنه يكبر الأولى للحال قضاء، وما في الواقعات أولى قيد بالمسبوق لأن اللاحق فيها كاللاحق في سائر الصلوات كذا في المجتبى. وذكر في الواقعات لو كبر مع الإمام التكبيرة الأولى ولم يكبر الثانية والثالثة يكبرهما أولاً ثم يكبر مع الإمام ما بقي ا هـ . وهو معنى ما في المجتبى في اللاحق .
لا؟ ظاهر تقييد المتن بقوله لا من كان حاضراً في حالة التحريمة أنه ينتظر لأنه ليس حاضراً وقتها فهو مسبوق تأمل قوله : (إنما هو في مسألة الحاضر ) قال في النهر : أنت خبير بأن مسألة الحاضر لا خلاف فيها فأنى ينسب إلى أبي يوسف وحده، ولذا ذكر المسألة في غاية البيان غير معزوة إليه ثم قال : وعن الحسن لا يدخل معه وعن أبي يوسف أنه يدخل ا هـ . وحاصله أن ما مر محل وفاق لا على قول الثاني فقط كما توهمه عبارة المحيط. ومحل الإيهام فيما لو حضر بعد الرابعة، وحينئذ فما في الحقائق في مسألة المسبوق لا الحاضر وقد نقل في الشرنبلالية عن التجنيس والولوالجية أن الفتوى في هذه المسألة على قول أبي يوسف ا هـ. وفي البدائع والدرر وشرح المقدسي أن الصحيح قولهما فقد اختلف التصحيح وظهر أن ما ذكره المؤلف غير ظاهر قوله : ( فينبغي أن يكون كالمسألة الأولى) أي أنه تفوته الصلاة إذا كبر الإمام الرابعة وهو حاضر كما إذا حضر بعدما كبرها الإمام فإنها تفوته عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف كما مر ، وحينئذ فلا فرف بين الحاضر وبين الغائب الذي حضر بعد الرابعة. وعليه فقول المحيط والرجل حاضر ليس احترازاً عن الغائب إذ لا فرق بينهما إلا في التكبيرة الأولى فإن . من حاضراً وقتها لا يكون مسبوقاً إذا كبر الثانية مع الإمام، أما إذا لم يكبرها معه فإنه يكون مسبوقاً بالأولى وحاضراً في الثانية فيتابعه فيها ويقضي الأولى كما دل عليه كلام الواقعات. هذا حاصل كلامه وفيه نظر، لأن الظاهر أن من حضر تكبير الإمام له أن يكبر بلا انتظار إلى تكبير الإمام بعده، سواء كان ذلك في التكبيرة الأولى أو غيرها، فلو كبر الإمام الأولى ثم حضر رجل وكبر الإمام الثانية والرجل حاضر كان مدركاً لهذه التكبيرة الثانية فله أن يكبرها قبل أن يكبر الإمام الثالثة ويكون مسبوقاً بواحدة ويقضيها بعد سلام الإمام، فكذا إذا كبر الإمام ثنتين أو ثلاثاً وهو حاضر يكون مدركاً لأخراها فيكبرها ومسبوقاً بما قبلها فيقضيها، وكذا إذا كبر الإمام الأربع وهو حاضر يكون مدركاً للرابعة فيكبرها ويقضي الثلاث لأنه فات محلها فيكون مسبوقاً بها. ولا يلزم من ذلك كونه مسبوقاً بالرابعة أيضاً لأن محلها باقي ما لم يسلم الإمام، وكلام الواقعات مشير إلى ما ذكرنا، وحينئذ فالفرق ظاهر بين الحاضر والمسبوق لأن
كان
Book of Funerals: Chapter: The ruler has more right to lead its prayer. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf [alone], and it benefits that if he came after the first takbir, then he says takbir after the imam's salam according to them, contrary to Abu Yusuf. Then according to them, he makes up what he missed without supplication, because if he were to make up the supplication, the deceased would be lifted and the takbir would be missed for him, and when the deceased is lifted, the takbir is cut off because the prayer is over the deceased and there is no deceased [to pray over]. In al-Zahira: and if it is lifted on hands and not placed on shoulders, it is mentioned in the apparent narration that he does not come [with takbir]. And he only waits for one who was present at the time of the takbirat-ul-ihram by agreement, because he is like one who catches up. Do you not see that if he says the opening takbir after the imam, it falls as performance, not makeup? He released it, so it includes whether the imam says the second or not. If the imam does not say the second, the present person says the first immediately, and if the present person does not say it until the imam says the second, he says the second with him and makes up the first immediately. Likewise in al-Mujtaba. And likewise if he does not say the second, third, and fourth, he says takbir and makes up what he missed immediately. He said in al-Muhit: and if the imam says four [takbirs] and the man is present, then he says takbir as long as the imam has not said salam and makes up the three. This is the saying of Abu Yusuf and upon it is the fatwa. And al-Hasan narrated that he does not say takbir and that it is lost for him. Thus what is in al-Haqa'iq that the fatwa is upon the saying of [the two companions?] [text unclear]...
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the rulings for a latecomer (masbuq) to the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The author begins by stating the ruling according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that if a person arrives after the first takbir, he should say the remaining takbirs after the imam's salam, but without reciting the supplication (du'a) between them. This is contrary to a separate view of Abu Yusuf. The reasoning is that if he were to recite the du'a, the bier would be lifted before he completes his takbirs, thereby invalidating his prayer. The text then discusses the case where the bier is raised on hands but not yet on shoulders: in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), the latecomer does not say takbir. However, a distinction is made for one who was present at the opening takbir (tahrimah) – by consensus, such a person is like one who caught the prayer (mudrik) and should not wait. The commentary clarifies that if a person present at the first takbir delays his own first takbir until the imam says the second, he says the second with the imam and makes up the first afterwards. The same applies for subsequent takbirs. A key dispute is recorded: according to Abu Yusuf, if the imam says four takbirs and a person is present from the beginning, he should say takbir as long as the imam has not said salam and then make up three. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, though al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that he does not say takbir and misses the prayer. Later, the text addresses the difference between one who is 'present' (hader) and one who is a 'latecomer' (masbuq). The author argues that if a person is present but does not say takbir until after the imam has said two or three, he is considered a masbuq, just like one who misses rak'ahs in regular prayer. Thus, he should follow the imam's current takbir and make up the missed ones only after the imam's salam, contrary to some earlier statements that he should make up immediately. The passage concludes by affirming the distinction: a person present at the moment of the imam's takbir can either say takbir immediately or wait for the next takbir, but if he delays, he becomes a masbuq for the earlier takbirs.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the janazah prayer after the imam has already started, missing one or more takbirs.
حاضر (hader): A person who is present at the beginning of the janazah prayer but may not have said the opening takbir yet.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who started the prayer with the imam but missed some takbirs due to a prolonged rukn or other reason.
مدرك (mudrik): A person who catches a particular part of the prayer with the imam.
قضاء (qada): Makeup of a missed obligatory part of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the two companions rule that the latecomer should not recite du'a between his makeup takbirs?
A) Because du'a is only allowed after the fourth takbir.
B) Because the bier might be lifted, causing the takbir to be missed.
C) Because the latecomer is not obligated to recite du'a.
D) Because the imam already recited du'a on behalf of all.

Key Takeaway
A latecomer to janazah prayer must make up missed takbirs after the imam's salam without du'a, and the mufta bihi position (Abu Yusuf) allows saying remaining takbirs with the imam before salam if present from the start.

Standing Position of the Imam in Funeral Prayer
Explains the preferred standing position for the imam in funeral prayer for men and women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended standing position for the imam in funeral prayer and explain why standing elsewhere does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Standing opposite the chest is recommended; the prayer is valid even if the imam stands elsewhere.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on where the imam should stand when leading funeral prayer. While it is a recommended practice (mustahabb) to stand opposite the chest, the prayer remains valid if the imam stands elsewhere. The text also addresses a potential misunderstanding from a hadith about the Prophet standing 'in the middle' of a deceased woman, showing how Hanafi scholars reconcile apparent contradictions through careful interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The imam's standing position in funeral prayer. What is the hukm level? Mustahabb (recommended), not wajib or fard. The text explicitly says 'بيان الاستحباب' (statement of recommendation).
The prayer is valid even if the imam stands elsewhere ('أجزأه').
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim: the Prophet stood in the middle of a deceased woman who died in postpartum.
This is a Sunnah ahad, but its authenticity is accepted (thubut qati). The Hanafis use this as evidence for the recommended position.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith support the chest position? The Hanafis interpret 'middle' (وسط) as the chest because the chest is the middle of the body considering the limbs: above it are the head and hands, below it are the stomach and thighs.
An alternative explanation is that the Prophet leaned slightly toward the private parts out of modesty, so the narrator thought it was the exact middle.
4
Note the potential objection
Some might think 'middle' contradicts the chest position. The author directly addresses this objection by offering two plausible interpretations.
This shows the importance of understanding how Hanafi scholars reconcile apparent differences between texts.
5
Evaluate the legal consequence
What is the practical effect? Since it is only a recommendation, if the imam stands elsewhere (e.g., at the head or feet), the prayer is still valid. No compensation is required.
This distinction between mustahabb and fard/wajib is crucial in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم من الرجل والمرأة بحذاء الصدر لأنه موضع القلب وفيه نور الإيمان فيكون القيام عنده إشارة إلى الشفاعة لإيمانه، وهذا ظاهر الرواية وهو بيان الاستحباب حتى لو وقف في غيره أجزأه . كذا في كافي الحاكم وما في الصحيحين أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى على امرأة ماتت في نفاسها فقام وسطها لا ينافي كونه الصدر بل الصدر وسط باعتبار توسط الأعضاء إذا فوقه يداه ورأسه وتحته بطنه وفخذاه ويحتمل أنه وقف كما قلنا إلا أنه مال إلى العورة في حقها فظن الراوي ذلك لتقارب المحلين. كذا في فتح القدير
And he stands from the man and the woman opposite the chest because it is the place of the heart and in it is the light of faith, so standing there is an indication of intercession for his faith. This is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is a statement of recommendation (istihbab), so that if he stands elsewhere it suffices him. Thus in Kafi al-Hakim. And what is in the two Sahihs that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed over a woman who died in her postpartum period and he stood in the middle of her does not contradict that it is the chest; rather the chest is middle considering the middle of the limbs since above it are his hands and head, and below it are his stomach and thighs. And it is possible that he stood as we said except that he inclined toward the private parts in her case, so the narrator thought that due to the proximity of the two places. Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the preferred standing position for the imam in funeral prayer. The author states that the imam should stand opposite the chest of the deceased, whether the deceased is a man or a woman. The reason given is that the chest contains the heart, which is the seat of the light of faith, so standing there symbolizes intercession for the deceased's faith. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is a matter of recommendation (istihbab), not obligation; if the imam stands elsewhere, the prayer is still valid. The author then addresses a potential objection from the authentic hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed over a woman and stood in the middle of her body. He clarifies that 'middle' here refers to the chest, which is the middle of the body in terms of the limbs. Alternatively, the Prophet may have moved slightly toward the private parts out of modesty, leading the narrator to think he was in the middle. Thus, there is no contradiction.

Key Terms
بحذاء الصدر (bihadha' al-sadr): Standing opposite the chest of the deceased, i.e., the area over the chest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the imam stands at the feet instead of the chest in funeral prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid but disliked.
C) The prayer is valid, and there is no dislike.
D) The prayer must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The imam standing opposite the chest in funeral prayer is recommended; the prayer is valid even if he stands elsewhere.

The Requirement of Standing in Funeral Prayer
States that funeral prayer is not valid while riding without an excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing the funeral prayer while riding and explain the legal reasoning that standing is a required element (wajib/rukn) due to the presence of the opening takbir (tahrimah).

Core Idea
The funeral prayer requires standing because the opening takbir makes it a prayer in some respects.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Bahr al-Raiq regarding the funeral prayer performed while riding. The author argues that even though the funeral prayer is not a full prayer, the presence of the tahrimah (opening takbir) imposes the requirement of standing. We will trace the reasoning, note the exception for unavoidable excuses, and explore an internal Hanafi disagreement about a sick imam leading while sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage: what is the ruling on praying the funeral prayer while riding without an excuse? Determine the hukm level (valid/invalid, permissible/impermissible).
2
Understand the Reasoning (Ta'lil)
The author gives a reason: because it is a prayer 'in some respect' due to the tahrimah. How does this lead to the requirement of standing? Consider the precautionary principle.
The tahrimah marks the start of prayer and imposes prohibitions, making it akin to a full prayer in that aspect.
3
Critique of an Alternative View
The author refutes the claim in Ghayat al-Bayan that the funeral prayer is 'nothing more than standing.' Why does he reject this? What flaw does he identify?
Reducing the prayer to standing alone would make standing the only pillar, which is incorrect.
4
Note the Exception
Identify the exception to the ruling: when is riding permitted? What counts as a valid excuse according to the text?
Excuses like mud or rain that make dismounting difficult are mentioned.
5
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
The passage ends with a disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a sick imam leading while sitting. State each position and identify the relied-upon view.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the followers' prayer is invalid. Muhammad: the imam's prayer is valid but not the followers'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يصلوا ركباناً) لأنها صلاة من وجه لوجود التحريمة فلا يجوز تركه القيام من غير عذر احتياطاً. وما في غاية البيان من أنها ليست بأكثر من القيام فإذا ترك القيام انعدمت أصلاً فلم يجز تركه فيه نظر، لأنه يقتضي أن ركنها القيام فقط وهو غير صحيح، قيدنا بكونه بغير عذر لأنه لو تعذر النزول لطين ومطر جاز الركوب فيها، وأشار إلى أنها لا تجوز قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام. ولو كان ولي الميت مريضاً فصلى قاعداً وصلى الناس خلفه قياماً ما أجزأهم في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد: يجزيء الإمام ولا يجزيء المأموم بناء على اقتداء القائم بالقاعد
His saying: (And they do not pray while riding) because it is a prayer in some respect due to the presence of the opening takbir (tahrimah), so it is not permissible to abandon standing without an excuse as a precaution. And what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is nothing more than standing, so if standing is abandoned, it is completely nonexistent, so it is not permissible to abandon it – there is consideration in this, because it implies that its pillar is only standing, which is incorrect. We restricted it to being without an excuse because if descent is difficult due to mud or rain, riding in it is permissible. And it indicates that it is not permissible while sitting if able to stand. And if the guardian of the deceased is sick and prays sitting, and the people pray behind him standing, it does not suffice them in the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: It suffices the imam but does not suffice the follower, based on the following of a standing person behind a sitting one.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on performing funeral prayer while riding. The text states that it is not permissible (la yajuz) to pray the funeral prayer while riding without a valid excuse. The reason given is that the funeral prayer has the status of a prayer in some respects because it includes the opening takbir (tahrimah), so standing is required out of precaution. The author critiques the view in Ghayat al-Bayan that the funeral prayer is nothing more than standing, arguing that this would make standing the only pillar, which is incorrect. The exception is made for excuses such as rain or mud that make dismounting difficult. The text also addresses the case of a sick guardian leading the prayer while sitting: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the prayer of the followers (who stand) is not valid, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the imam's prayer is valid but the followers' is not.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer and renders normal actions prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a sick imam prays the funeral prayer sitting and the followers stand, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer of both is valid.
B) The prayer of neither is valid.
C) The imam's prayer is valid but not the followers'.
D) The followers' prayer is valid but not the imam's.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer requires standing due to the tahrimah, and riding without excuse invalidates it, but an excuse like heavy rain permits riding.
