The Hanafi Ruling on Funeral Prayer in a Mosque
Inter-madhhab dispute on funeral prayer in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers funeral prayer in a mosque makruh (disliked) and distinguish between the tahrimi and tanzihi views, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer in a mosque is makruh—negation of reward implies dislike, and caution demands avoidance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq delves into a well-known issue: is it permissible to perform the funeral prayer inside a mosque? The Hanafi school, based on a hadith from Abu Dawood, holds it is disliked (makruh), but scholars differ on whether the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitive) or tanzihi (discommendable). We will examine the evidence, the scenarios, and how the Hanafi position compares to the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary evidence
Start with the hadith: 'Whoever prays over a dead person in the mosque has no reward.' Note its absolute wording and the variant 'has no prayer'.
The hadith is mursal, so its thubut is zanni, but it is accepted in practice.
2
Analyze grammatical interpretations
The phrase 'in the mosque' could modify the prayer, the deceased, or both. Each yields conditions for the dislike. The chosen view is that if either the deceased or the prayer is in the mosque, dislike applies.
This is the opinion in al-Mujtaba.
3
Understand the two degrees of karahah
Makruh tahrimi is close to prohibition and sinful; makruh tanzihi is light dislike. The hadith's negation of reward does not automatically imply tahrimi, but the variant 'no prayer' supports it.
Fath al-Qadir prefers tanzihi; al-Fatawa al-Qasimiyya prefer tahrimi.
4
Examine the intra and inter-madhhab disputes
Within Hanafi, a weak narration from Abu Yusuf allows it. Externally, Shafi'is permit it in spacious mosques, though the best is outside.
The practical difference: Hanafis avoid the mosque; Shafi'is may pray inside.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is makruh, with caution leaning toward tahrimi. The fatwa should follow the apparent madhhab unless necessity dictates otherwise.
Historical examples, like the Umayyad Mosque incident, reinforce caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولا في مسجد) الحديث أبي داود مرفوعاً من صلى على ميت في المسجد فلا أجر له» وفي رواية فلا شيء له أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الميت والقوم في المسجد، أو كان الإمام مع بعض القوم خارج المسجد والقوم الباقون في المسجد، أو الميت في المسجد والإمام والقوم خارج المسجد وهو المختار خلافاً لما أولاده النسفي . كذا في الخلاصة. وهذا الإطلاق في الكراهة بناء على أن المسجد إنما بني للصلاة المكتوبة وتوابعها من النوافل والذكر وتدريس العلم . وقيل : لا يكره إذا كان الميت خارج المسجد وهو مبني على أن الكراهة لاحتمال تلويث المسجد والأول هو الأوفق لإطلاق الحديث كذا في فتح القدير فما في غاية البيان والعناية من أن الميت وبعض القوم إذا كانا خارج المسجد والباقون فيه لا كراهة اتفاقاً ممنوع. وقد يقال : إن الحديث يحتم ثلاثة أشياء : أن يكون الظرف وهو قوله في مسجد ظرفاً للصلاة والميت وحينئذ فللكراهة شرطان: كون الصلاة في المسجد وكون الميت فيه، فإذا فقد أحدهما فلا كراهة . الثاني أن يكون ظرفاً للصلاة فقط فلا يكره إذا كان الميت في المسجد والقوم كلهم خارجه الثالث أن يكون ظرفاً للميت فقط وحينئذ حيث كان خارجه فلا كراهة، وما اختاروه كما نقلناه لم يوافق واحداً من الاحتمالات الثلاثة لأنهم قالوا بالكراهة إذا وجد أحدهما في المسجد المصلي أو الميت كما قال في المجتبى وتكره سواء كان الميت والقوم في المسجد أو أحدهما ولعل وجهه أنه لما لم يكن دليل على بعينه قالوا بالكراهة بوجود أحدهما أياً كان، وظاهر كلام المصنف أن من الاحتمالات الكراهة تحريمية لأنه عطفه على ما لا يجوز من الصلاة راكباً وهي إحدى الروايتين مع أن فيه إيهاماً لأن في المعطوف عليه لم تصح الصلاة أصلاً وفي المعطوف هي صحيحة، والأخرى أنها تنزيهية ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن الحديث ليس نهياً غير مصروف ولا قرن الفعل بوعيد بظني بل سلب الأجر وسلب الأجر لا يستلزم ثبوت استحقاق العقاب لجواز الإباحة. ثم قرر تقريراً حاصله أنه لا خلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي على هذه الرواية لأنه يقول بالجواز في توسعة المسجد لكن الأفضل خارجه وهو معنى كراهة التنزيه وبه يحصل الجمع بين الأحاديث اهـ. لكن تترجح كراهة التحريم بالرواية الأخرى التي رواها الطيالسي كما في الفتاوى القاسمية : من صلى على ميت في المسجد فلا صلاة له . ولم يقيد المصنف كصاحب المجمع المسجد بالجماعة كما قيده في الهداية لعدم الحاجة إليه لأنهم يحترزون به عن المسجد المبني لصلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تكره فيه مع أن الصحيح أنه ليس بمسجد لأنه ما أعد للصلاة حقيقة لأن صلاة الجنازة ليست بصلاة حقيقة وحاجة الناس ماسة إلى أنه لم يكن مسجداً : للأمر عليهم. واختلفوا أيضاً في مصلى العيدين أنه هل هو مسجد، والصحيح أنه مسجد في حق جواز الاقتداء وإن لم تتصل الصفوف لأنه أعد للصلاة حقيقة لا في حرمة دخول الجنب والحائض. كذا في المحيط وغيره واعلم أن ظاهر الحديث وكلامهم أنه لا أجر أصلاً لمن صلى عليها في المسجد ولا يلزم منه عدم سقوط الفرض لعدم الملازمة بينهما. ولم يذكر المصنف رحمه الله ما إذا اجتمعت الجنائز للصلاة قالوا : الإمام بالخيار إن شاء صلى عليهم دفعة واحدة وإن شاء صلى على كل جنازة صلاة على حدة، فإن أراد الثاني فالأفضل أن يقدم يبن له نعم يظهر التوفيق على التعليل الثاني فتدبر قوله : (لكن) ترجح كراهة التحريم الخ) قال الشيخ إسماعيل : فيه نظر لجواز كونه مثل لا صلاة لجار المسجد، ثم نقل عن مفتي الحنفية بمكة المشرفة قطب الدين في تاريخ مكة أنه أفتى بالجواز وعدم الكراهة كما هو رواية عن أبي يوسف، ذكرها في المحيط لتظافر أهل الحرمين سلفاً وخلفاً على ذلك دليلاً يؤدي إلى تأثيم السلف، وقد رأيت رسالة للمنلا علي القاريء مؤداها ذلك أيضاً، لكن رد الشيخ إسماعيل على قطب الدين بأنه لا يفتى بخلاف ظاهر المذهب على أنه جدير بالترجيح لما شاهدنا في عصرنا من نفساء ماتت فوضعت في باب الجامع الأموي فخرج منها دم ضمخ العتبة فالاحتياط عدم الإدخال ولعل أهل الحرمين على مذهب غيرنا ا وللعلامة قاسم رسالة خاصة نقل فيها الكراهة عن أئمتنا الثلاثة وحقق أنها تحريمية والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقة الحال
His saying: (And not in a mosque) – the hadith of Abu Dawood, raised: 'Whoever prays over a dead person in the mosque has no reward.' And in another narration: 'has nothing.' It is absolute, so it includes when the deceased and the people are in the mosque, or when the imam and some of the people are outside and the rest are inside, or when the deceased is in the mosque and the imam and people are outside – and this is the chosen view contrary to what al-Nasafi transmitted. Thus in al-Khulasa. And this absoluteness in dislike is based on the fact that the mosque was built only for the obligatory prayers and their supplements of supererogatory prayers, remembrance, and teaching knowledge. It is said: it is not disliked if the deceased is outside the mosque, and this is based on the opinion that the dislike is due to the possibility of soiling the mosque. The first is more in line with the absoluteness of the hadith, as in Fath al-Qadir. So what is in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-‘Inaya that if the deceased and some of the people are outside the mosque and the rest inside, there is no dislike by agreement – is rejected. It may be said that the hadith admits three possibilities: that the adverb 'in a mosque' is a circumstantial clause for the prayer and the deceased – then there are two conditions for dislike: that the prayer is in the mosque and the deceased is in it; if one is missing, then no dislike. Second: it is a circumstance for the prayer only, then it is not disliked if the deceased is in the mosque and all the people are outside. Third: it is a circumstance only for the deceased, then when he is outside there is no dislike. And what they chose as we transmitted does not agree with any of the three possibilities because they said there is dislike if either the prayer or the deceased is in the mosque, as stated in al-Mujtaba: it is disliked whether the deceased and the people are in the mosque or one of them. Perhaps the reason is that since there is no specific evidence, they said dislike with the presence of either. The apparent speech of the author (al-Marghinani) indicates that among the possibilities is that the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitive) because he coupled it with what is not permissible of prayer while riding, which is one of the two narrations, even though there is an illusion because in the first the prayer is invalid and in the second it is valid. The other view is that it is tanzihi (discommendable), and he preferred it in Fath al-Qadir because the hadith is not a prohibitive command not diverted, nor is the action coupled with a threat of punishment, but rather negation of reward, and negation of reward does not necessitate punishment – abatement (ibaha) is possible. Then he established a point: there is no disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i in this narration because he permits it in a spacious mosque, but the better is outside, which is the meaning of tanzihi dislike, and by this reconciliation of hadiths is achieved. However, the dislike of tahrimi is preferred by the other narration of al-Tayalisi as in al-Fatawa al-Qasimiyya: 'Whoever prays over a dead person in the mosque has no prayer.' The author did not restrict the mosque by congregation as al-Asl did in al-Hidaya, because there is no need since they avoid by it the mosque built for funeral prayer, for it is not disliked in it, even though the correct view is that it is not a mosque because it is not prepared for prayer in reality – funeral prayer is not a real prayer, and people's need is pressing that it was not a mosque for their situation. They also differed about the ‘Id prayer ground: is it a mosque? The correct view is that it is a mosque regarding the validity of following even if rows are not connected, because it is prepared for prayer in reality, but not for the prohibition of entry for the junub and menstruating woman. Thus in al-Muhit and others. Know that the apparent meaning of the hadith and their statements is that there is no reward at all for one who prays over it in the mosque, but it does not necessitate the non-fulfillment of the obligation due to lack of correlation. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention when funerals gather for prayer. They said: the imam has the choice: if he wishes, he prays over them all at once, and if he wishes, he prays over each funeral separately. If he chooses the second, then it is better that he presents a son to him? Yes, the reconciliation appears on the second explanation. So ponder. His saying: (But) the dislike of tahrimi is preferred... Sheikh Ismail said: There is consideration in it because it could be like 'no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque'. Then he quoted from the Mufti of the Hanafis in Mecca, Qutb al-Din in his history of Mecca, that he gave a fatwa of permissibility and no dislike, as a narration from Abu Yusuf mentioned in al-Muhit, due to the widespread practice of the people of the Two Sanctuaries past and present as evidence leading to implicating the predecessors. And I saw a treatise by Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari to that effect. But Sheikh Ismail replied to Qutb al-Din that a fatwa contrary to the apparent madhhab is not given, but it is worthy of being preferred because we have seen in our time a woman in postpartum died and was placed at the door of the Umayyad Mosque, and blood came out from her and stained the threshold – so caution is to not bring her in. Perhaps the people of the Two Sanctuaries follow other than our madhhab. And the scholar Qasim has a special treatise in which he transmitted the dislike from our three imams and confirmed it is tahrimi. And Allah knows the reality of the situation.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This extensive passage deals with the ruling on performing funeral prayer inside a mosque. It begins by citing the hadith narrated by Abu Dawood that whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque has no reward. The author discusses various scenarios based on whether the deceased, the imam, or the congregation are inside or outside the mosque. There is disagreement over whether the dislike (karahah) is tahrimi (prohibitive) or tanzihi (discommendable). The author notes that some scholars, like those in Fath al-Qadir, consider it tanzihi, as the hadith only negates reward, not imposes punishment. However, another narration from al-Tayalisi says 'no prayer', which supports tahrimi. The text also discusses exceptions: a mosque built specifically for funeral prayers (not a real mosque) and the ‘Id prayer ground (which is a mosque for some rulings but not for removing restrictions on junub and menstruating women). The passage concludes with a practical issue: if multiple funerals are present, the imam may pray over them all at once or separately. The general caution is to avoid funeral prayers inside the mosque, especially due to potential impurity, as seen in the historical example of the Umayyad Mosque.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A category of dislike that is close to prohibition; the action is sinful if done without valid reason.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A light dislike; the action is not sinful but avoiding it is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing funeral prayer in a mosque?
A) It is permissible without any dislike.
B) It is makruh, but some say tahrimi and others tanzihi.
C) It is haram and the prayer is invalid.
D) It is mustahabb to do so.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that funeral prayer in a mosque is makruh, with the stronger view being tahrimi due to caution and the hadith, though a minority considers it tanzihi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Funeral Prayer in a Mosque: Hanafi Ruling and Inter-Madhhab Differences
Explains the disliked nature of funeral prayer inside a mosque and resolves conflicting hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer in a mosque, distinguish between prohibitive and offensive dislike, and evaluate the Shafi'i position on the matter.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer inside a mosque is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school, not absolutely forbidden.

In this lesson, we delve into the Hanafi ruling on performing funeral prayer inside a mosque. The source text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the degree of dislike and reconciles conflicting hadiths. You will learn the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) and understand why the Shafi'i school differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its degree of dislike
Determine whether the ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitive dislike) or makruh tanzihi (offensive dislike). The text presents both views and weighs them.
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicates karahah, but the degree is debated.
2
Examine the evidence: the hadith of al-Tayalisi
The hadith 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque, his prayer is not valid' is a strong proof. In Hanafi usul, negation of validity indicates strong prohibition.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and al-dalala.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi authorities (e.g., in Fath al-Qadir) prefer tanzihi, while the text favors tahrimi based on the stronger narration.
Abu Yusuf reportedly had a view of no dislike, but the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on dislike.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Al-Shafi'i allows funeral prayer in a spacious mosque but prefers outside. This is compatible with the Hanafi tanzihi view.
The text reconciles by saying there is no disagreement on that level.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis avoid praying inside mosques, considering it makruh tahrimi; Shafi'is allow it in spacious mosques without dislike.
The difference affects community practice and fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته واحد وحينئذ حيث كان خارجه فلا كراهة، وما اختاروه كما نقلناه لم يوافق واحداً من الاحتمالات الثلاثة لأنهم قالوا بالكراهة إذا وجد أحدهما في المسجد المصلي أو الميت كما قال في المجتبى وتكره سواء كان الميت والقوم في المسجد أو أحدهما ولعل وجهه أنه لما لم يكن دليل على بعينه قالوا بالكراهة بوجود أحدهما أياً كان، وظاهر كلام المصنف أن من الاحتمالات الكراهة تحريمية لأنه عطفه على ما لا يجوز من الصلاة راكباً وهي إحدى الروايتين مع أن فيه إيهاماً لأن في المعطوف عليه لم تصح الصلاة أصلاً وفي المعطوف هي صحيحة، والأخرى أنها تنزيهية ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن الحديث ليس نهياً غير مصروف ولا قرن الفعل بوعيد بظني بل سلب الأجر وسلب الأجر لا يستلزم ثبوت استحقاق العقاب لجواز الإباحة. ثم قرر تقريراً حاصله أنه لا خلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي على هذه الرواية لأنه يقول بالجواز في توسعة المسجد لكن الأفضل خارجه وهو معنى كراهة التنزيه وبه يحصل الجمع بين الأحاديث اهـ. لكن تترجح كراهة التحريم بالرواية الأخرى التي رواها الطيالسي كما في الفتاوى القاسمية : من صلى على ميت في المسجد فلا صلاة له . ولم يقيد المصنف كصاحب المجمع المسجد بالجماعة كما قيده في الهداية لعدم الحاجة إليه لأنهم يحترزون به عن المسجد المبني لصلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تكره فيه مع أن الصحيح أنه ليس بمسجد لأنه ما أعد للصلاة حقيقة لأن صلاة الجنازة ليست بصلاة حقيقة وحاجة الناس ماسة إلى أنه لم يكن مسجداً : للأمر عليهم. واختلفوا أيضاً في مصلى العيدين أنه هل هو مسجد، والصحيح أنه مسجد في حق جواز الاقتداء وإن لم تتصل الصفوف لأنه أعد للصلاة حقيقة لا في حرمة دخول الجنب والحائض. كذا في المحيط وغيره واعلم أن ظاهر الحديث وكلامهم أنه لا أجر أصلاً لمن صلى عليها في المسجد ولا يلزم منه عدم سقوط الفرض لعدم الملازمة بينهما.
Book of Funerals: Chapter: The Sultan has most right to his prayer. One: And when it is outside [the mosque], there is no dislike. What they chose as we transmitted does not agree with any of the three probabilities because they said there is dislike if either the one praying or the deceased is in the mosque, as stated in al-Mujtaba: it is disliked whether the deceased and the people are in the mosque or one of them. Perhaps its reasoning is that since there is no specific proof, they said dislike with the presence of either, whichever it may be. The apparent wording of the author (al-Marghinani) suggests that among the probabilities is that the dislike is prohibitive (tahrimi) because he juxtaposes it with what is not permissible, like praying while riding, which is one of two narrations, although this is misleading because in the conjoined item the prayer is not valid at all, while in this case it is valid. The other view is that it is merely offensiveness (tanzihi), and this was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because the hadith is not an unrestricted prohibition nor is the action accompanied by a threat of punishment, but rather a deprivation of reward, and deprivation of reward does not entail deserving punishment, since permissibility is possible. Then he established that there is no disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i according to this narration because he allows it in a spacious mosque, though it is better outside, which is the meaning of tanzih dislike, and this reconciles the hadiths. However, the view of prohibitive dislike is strengthened by the other narration transmitted by al-Tayalisi, as in al-Fatawa al-Qasimiyya: 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque, his prayer is not valid.' The author (al-Marghinani) did not restrict the mosque to the congregational mosque as the author of al-Majma' did, nor as it was restricted in al-Hidayah, because there is no need, since they thereby avoid the mosque built specifically for funeral prayer, for it is not disliked therein, although the correct view is that it is not a mosque because it was not prepared for prayer properly, since funeral prayer is not actually prayer, and people's need is urgent that it not be a mosque. They also differed about the 'id prayer ground whether it is a mosque. The correct view is that it is a mosque regarding the permissibility of following an imam even if the rows are not connected, because it was prepared for actual prayer, but not regarding the prohibition of entry for a junub or a menstruating woman. This is in al-Muhit and others. Know that the apparent meaning of the hadith and their statements is that there is absolutely no reward for the one who prays over it in the mosque, but it does not necessarily follow that the obligation is not fulfilled, because there is no necessary connection between them.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of performing funeral prayer inside a mosque. The text begins by stating that if the prayer is outside the mosque, there is no dislike. The author then critiques an earlier view that dislike applies if either the deceased or the congregation is inside the mosque, noting that this does not align with any of the three possible interpretations. The discussion then moves to the nature of the dislike: some hold it to be prohibitive (tahrimi) because the matn author juxtaposed it with an invalid action, while others consider it merely offensiveness (tanzihi), a view preferred in Fath al-Qadir based on a hadith that only deprives of reward without threat. The text then reconciles the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view regarding spacious mosques, stating there is no essential difference—both allow it in a spacious mosque but prefer outside. A stronger proof for prohibitive dislike is mentioned from the narration of al-Tayalisi. The passage also clarifies that a mosque built specifically for funeral prayers is not considered a true mosque for this ruling, and the 'id prayer ground is considered a mosque only for following an imam, not for purity rules. The conclusion is that the hadith denies reward but does not necessarily negate fulfillment of the obligation.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an action that is close to haram and entails sin in the Hanafi school.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Offensive dislike; an action that is better to avoid but not sinful.
مسجد الجنازة (masjid al-janazah): A mosque built specifically for funeral prayers; considered not a true mosque in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this text, what is the ruling on performing funeral prayer inside a mosque?
A) Permissible without any dislike
B) Prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer inside a mosque is prohibitively disliked in the Hanafi school, but the prayer remains valid; the obligation is fulfilled even though reward is diminished.

Arrangement of Multiple Funeral Biers in Hanafi Jurisprudence
Ruling on placement of multiple funeral biers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi preferred order for placing multiple funeral biers (men, boys, hermaphrodites, women, girls) and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Funeral biers are arranged like living prayer rows: men closest, then boys, hermaphrodites, women, girls.

When multiple funerals are prayed over together, the Hanafi school prescribes a recommended order based on the analogy of rows in congregational prayer (qiyas). This order is sunnah muakkadah; the prayer remains valid even if the arrangement is different. The following passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq details the placement from the imam outward, along with the permissibility of praying over all at once or individually.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's options
First, note that the imam may pray over all funerals together or separately. The passage gives this choice before detailing the order when praying together.
The imam's choice is a rukhsah (concession).
2
Recognise the default arrangement for same gender
If all funerals are of the same gender, they may be placed side by side in one row or one behind another towards the qiblah. The passage cites al-Halabi's Sharh al-Munya for this.
Al-Tatarkhaniyya also permits either.
3
Learn the order for mixed genders
The preferred order from the imam outward is: men (free and slave equal), then boys, then hermaphrodites (khuntha), then women, then girls. This is based on the order of living rows in prayer.
Zahir al-riwayah (apparent narration) supports this order.
4
Apply the order to a concrete example
The passage gives an example: a man, a boy, a hermaphrodite, a woman, and a girl. The man is placed nearest the imam, then the boy, then the hermaphrodite, then the woman, then the girl.
This order mirrors the standing in life: men, then women, but boys precede women because they are male minors.
5
Understand the ruling level and implications
The arrangement is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib. The prayer is valid even if the order is different. The proof is the Prophet's action at Uhud and analogy to prayer rows.
The dalil is ahad (single-narrator hadith), giving zanni certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف رحمه الله ما إذا اجتمعت الجنائز للصلاة قالوا : الإمام بالخيار إن شاء صلى عليهم دفعة واحدة وإن شاء صلى على كل جنازة صلاة على حدة، فإن أراد الثاني فالأفضل أن يقدم يبن له نعم يظهر التوفيق على التعليل الثاني فتدبر قوله : (لكن) ترجح كراهة التحريم الخ) قال الشيخ إسماعيل : فيه نظر لجواز كونه مثل لا صلاة لجار المسجد، ثم نقل عن مفتي الحنفية بمكة المشرفة قطب الدين في تاريخ مكة أنه أفتى بالجواز وعدم الكراهة كما هو رواية عن أبي يوسف، ذكرها في المحيط لتظافر أهل الحرمين سلفاً وخلفاً على ذلك دليلاً يؤدي إلى تأثيم السلف، وقد رأيت رسالة للمنلا علي القاريء مؤداها ذلك أيضاً، لكن رد الشيخ إسماعيل على قطب الدين بأنه لا يفتى بخلاف ظاهر المذهب على أنه جدير بالترجيح لما شاهدنا في عصرنا من نفساء ماتت فوضعت في باب الجامع الأموي فخرج منها دم ضمخ العتبة فالاحتياط عدم الإدخال ولعل أهل الحرمين على مذهب غيرنا ا وللعلامة قاسم رسالة خاصة نقل فيها الكراهة عن أئمتنا الثلاثة وحقق أنها تحريمية والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقة الحال قوله : (فإن كان الجنس متحداً الخ) قال الرملي : هذا : يوهـم. كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته ۳۲۹ ومن استهل صلى عليه وإلا لا كصبي سبي مع أحد أبويه إلا أن يسلم أحدهما أو هو الفحوى أولى وتقدم أن بعضهم توهم انحصار جواز الصف الواحد في متحد الجنس، وما في التتارخانية يخالفه وفي شرح المنية للحلبي : ولو اجتمعت الجنائز جاز أن يصلي عليهم صلاة واحدة ويجعلون واحداً خلف واحد، ويجعل الرجال مما يلي الإمام ويستوي فيه الحر والعبد في ظاهر الرواية، ثم الصبيان ثم الخناثى ثم النساء، وإن شاؤوا جعلوهم صفاً واحداً ا ففيه كما ترى جواز الشيئين تأمل وقوله : (وهو سهو الخ) أقول : هو قول لبعض العلماء فقد ذكر في البدائع ما نقله المؤلف عنه هنا في فصل الدفن وذكر قبله في فصل الصلاة أنه يوضع الرجال مما يلي الإمام والنساء خلف الرجال مما يلي القبلة لأنهم هكذا يصطفون خلف الإمام في حالة الحياة، ثم إن الرجال يكونون أقرب إلى الإمام من النساء فكذا بعد النساء مما يلي الإمام والرجال خلفهن لأن في الصلاة بالجماعة من قال : يوضع في حال الحياة صف النساء خلف صف الرجال إلى القبلة فكذا في وضع الجنائز، ولو اجتمع جنازة رجل وصبي وخنثى وامرأته وصبية وضع الرجل مما يلي الإمام والصبي وراءه ثم الخنثى ثم المرأة ثم الصبية لأنهم هكذا يقومون في الصف خلف الإمام حال الحياة فيوضعون كذلك اهـ.
The author (al-Marghinani) did not mention the case when funerals gather for prayer. They said: the imam has a choice: if he wishes he may pray over them all at once, or if he wishes he may pray over each funeral separately. If he wishes the second, it is better to present... then he is shown, yes, reconciliation appears upon the second rationale, so ponder. His statement: (but the view of prohibitive dislike is preponderant, etc.) Shaykh Ismail said: there is room for consideration because it may be like 'no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque'. Then he reported from the Mufti of the Hanafis in Mecca, Qutb al-Din, in his history of Mecca, that he gave a fatwa of permissibility and no dislike, as is a narration from Abu Yusuf, mentioned in al-Muhit, due to the continuous practice of the people of the two sanctuaries (Makkah and Madinah) both early and late, as a proof that would lead to accusing the predecessors of sin. And I have seen a treatise by Mulla Ali al-Qari to the same effect. However, Shaykh Ismail responded to Qutb al-Din that one should not give fatwa contrary to the apparent madhhab, and that it is worthy of preponderance because we have seen in our time a woman who died postpartum and was placed at the door of the Umayyad Mosque, and blood came out from her, staining the threshold, so caution is by not entering. Perhaps the people of the two sanctuaries follow another madhhab. And Allama Qasim has a special treatise in which he reports dislike from our three imams and established that it is prohibitive. And Allah knows best the reality of the matter. His statement: (If the gender is the same, etc.) al-Ramli said: this is misleading. Book of Funerals: Chapter: The Sultan has most right to his prayer. 329: And whoever cries at birth, prayer is performed over him, otherwise not, like a child captured with one of his parents unless one of them accepts Islam or he himself... The meaning [that some] imagined the confinement of permissibility of a single row to the case of same gender, and what is in al-Tatarkhaniyya contradicts it. In Sharh al-Munya by al-Halabi: If funerals gather, it is permissible to pray over them with one prayer, and they place them one behind the other, and they place the men closest to the imam, and the free and slave are equal in the apparent narration, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women. And if they wish, they make them a single row. So there is, as you see, permissibility of two things, so ponder. His statement: (And it is a mistake, etc.) I say: it is a statement of some scholars. It was mentioned in al-Bada'i' what the author transmitted from him here in the chapter on burial, and before that in the chapter on prayer, that he places the men closest to the imam and the women behind the men towards the qiblah because they line up behind the imam in life. Then men are closer to the imam than women, so likewise after the women closest to the imam and the men behind them, because in congregational prayer some said: in life the row of women is placed behind the row of men towards the qiblah, so likewise in the placement of funerals. If the funeral of a man, a boy, a hermaphrodite, his wife, and a girl gather, the man is placed closest to the imam, the boy behind him, then the hermaphrodite, then the woman, then the girl, because they stand in the row behind the imam in life, so they are placed likewise. End.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage addresses the arrangement of multiple funeral biers when praying over them collectively. It begins by noting that the matn author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not mention this situation. The imam has the choice to pray over all at once or individually. The discussion then details the placement of bodies when praying together: if the gender is the same, they can be placed in a single row side by side or one after another towards the qiblah, with the imam standing facing them all. The text then presents the preferred order when genders differ: men closest to the imam, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women, then girls. Free persons are prioritized over slaves. The author also cites a view from al-Tatarkhaniyya and Sharh al-Munya that permits either arrangement. The commentary on the phrase 'وهو سهو' (it is a mistake) clarifies that some scholars hold a different view regarding placement in the grave, but the text maintains that the funeral prayer arrangement follows the order of living rows. The passage concludes with an example: for a man, boy, hermaphrodite, woman, and girl, the man is placed nearest the imam, followed by the boy, then the hermaphrodite, then the woman, then the girl, based on the analogy of standing in rows behind the imam in life.

Key Terms
الجنائز (al-jana'iz): Plural of janazah; funeral biers or the deceased persons.
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite; a person with ambiguous gender.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Funeral biers are arranged like living prayer rows: men (free/slave) closest, then boys, hermaphrodites, women, girls — this is sunnah, not fard.

Same-Gender Funeral Bier Arrangement
Explaining the two permissible arrangements for same-gender funeral biers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two permissible arrangements for same-gender funeral biers and identify the primary ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
For same-gender biers, a single row is the primary sunnah; one behind the other is also permissible.

When several deceased are all of the same gender, the Hanafi school offers two valid arrangements for their biers. This lesson explains those options and the preferred method according to the primary transmissions of the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's scope
This ruling applies only when all deceased are of the same gender. Gender uniformity is the key condition for these two options.
If genders differ, a different order applies.
2
Recognize the two options
The text gives two options: a single row parallel to the qibla (like living congregants), or one bier behind the other facing the qibla with the imam standing opposite all.
Both are sunnah muakkadah.
3
Determine the preferred method
Zahir al-Riwayah presents the single row as the primary answer, while a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad considers the stacked method better. The mufta bihi accepts both.
The single row is more commonly practiced.
4
Understand alignment when stacked
When placing biers one behind the other, the most virtuous should be nearest the imam. Alignment of the biers can be heads aligned or head-to-shoulder of the preceding bier.
Both alignments are equally good.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما كيفية وضعها فإن كان الجنس متحداً فإن شاؤوا جعلوها صفاً واحداً كما يصطفون في حال حياتهم عند الصلاة وإن شاؤوا وضعوا واحداً بعد واحد مما يلي القبلة ليقوم الإمام بحذاء الكل. هذا جواب ظاهر الرواية، وفي رواية الحسن أن الثاني أولى من الأول. وإذا وضعوا واحداً بعد واحد ينبغي أن يكون الأفضل مما يلي الإمام، ثم إن وضع رأس كل واحد بحذاء رأس صاحبه فحسن وإن وضع رأس كل واحد عند منكب الأول فحسن، وإن اختلف الجنس وضع الرجل بين يدي الإمام، ثم الصبي وراءه ثم الخنثى ثم المرأة ثم الصبية. والأفضل أن يجعل الحر مما يلي الإمام ويقدم على العبد ولو كان الحر صبياً كما في الظهيرية وإن كان عبداً وامرأة حرة فالعبد يوضع مما يلي الإمام والمرأة خلفه. وفي فتح القدير : ولو اجتمعوا في قبر واحد فوضعهم على عكس هذا فيقدم الأفضل فالأفضل إلى القبلة، وفي الرجلين يقدم أكبرهما سناً وقرآناً وعلماً كما فعله عليه السلام في قتلى أحد من المسلمين اهـ. وفي البدائع : ولو كان رجل وامرأة قدم الرجل مما يلي القبلة ثم الصبي خلفه اعتباراً بحال الحياة، ولو اجتمع رجل وامرأة وصبي وخنثى وصبية دفن الرجل مما يلي القبلة ثم الصبي خلفه ثم الخنثى ثم الأنثى ثم الصبية لأنهم هكذا يصطفون خلف الإمام حالة الحياة وهكذا توضع جنائزهم عند الصلاة فكذا في القبر اهـ. وهو سهو وفي قوله وهكذا توضع جنائزهم لما ذكرنا أنه على عكسه.
And as for the manner of placing them: if the gender is uniform, if they wish they make them a single row just as they line up in their lives during prayer, and if they wish they place them one after another facing the qibla so that the imam stands opposite all. This is the answer of the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), and in a narration of al-Hasan the second is better than the first. When they place them one after another, the most virtuous should be next to the imam. Then if they place the head of each level with the head of his companion, that is good; and if they place the head of each at the shoulder of the first, that is good. If the genders differ, they place the man before the imam, then the boy behind him, then the hermaphrodite, then the woman, then the girl. It is better to place the free one next to the imam and give him precedence over the slave, even if the free one is a boy, as in al-Zahiriyyah. If there is a slave and a free woman, the slave is placed next to the imam and the woman behind him. In Fath al-Qadir: if they are gathered in one grave, their placement is the reverse of this: the most virtuous are placed first towards the qibla. For two men, the older in age, Quran, and knowledge is given precedence, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did with the martyrs of Uhud. In al-Bada'i': if there is a man and a woman, the man is placed first towards the qibla, then the boy behind him, considering the state of life. If a man, woman, boy, hermaphrodite, and girl are gathered, the man is buried first towards the qibla, then the boy behind him, then the hermaphrodite, then the female, then the girl, because they line up like this behind the imam during life, and thus their funeral biers are placed during prayer, so likewise in the grave. But this is a mistake, and his statement 'and thus their funeral biers are placed' is contrary to what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage details the proper placement of multiple funeral biers for a collective funeral prayer. The author presents rulings from the Hanafi school. If all deceased are the same gender, they may be placed in a single row (like living worshippers) or one behind the other facing the qibla, with the imam standing opposite them all. The preferred method in Zahir al-Riwayah is the single row; a narration from al-Hasan holds the second method better. When placing one behind another, the most meritorious should be nearest the imam. If genders differ, men come first in front of the imam, then boys, hermaphrodites, women, and girls. Free persons are placed closer to the imam than slaves, even if the free person is a child. The author notes a disputed point: some scholars, like in al-Bada'i', claimed that the arrangement in the grave mirrors the arrangement during prayer (men closest to the imam), but the author corrects this, stating it is the opposite. The passage includes references from various Hanafi sources such as al-Zahiriyyah, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the core Hanafi texts (the six books of Imam Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They must be placed in a single row.
B) They must be placed one behind the other.
C) Both methods are equally permissible, but the single row is the primary answer.

Key Takeaway
Same-gender biers may be arranged in a single row or one behind the other; the single row is the primary sunnah.

Mixed-Gender Funeral Bier Arrangement and Burial Correction
Explaining the order of precedence for mixed-gender biers and a correction about burial arrangement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to arrange funeral biers of mixed genders according to the Hanafi sunnah order and identify the correction regarding burial arrangement.

Core Idea
Men, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women, then girls: the order of precedence for mixed-gender biers.

When multiple deceased include different genders and statuses, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific order to honor the most virtuous. This lesson covers the placement order, priority of free over slave, and a correction about burial arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gender categories
The text lists men, boys, khuntha (hermaphrodite), women, and girls. Khuntha is placed between the two genders.
The imam stands by the head of the foremost bier.
2
Learn the order
Man before the imam, then boy, khuntha, woman, girl.
This order is based on virtue and precedence in life.
3
Understand free/slave priority
Free persons are placed closer to imam than slaves, even if the free is a child. Exception: a free woman is placed behind a slave man.
This exception shows that male status can outweigh freedom.
4
Clarify the burial correction
The author corrects a mistaken view that burial arrangement mirrors bier arrangement; they are opposite. In burial, the most virtuous are placed closest to the qibla.
The correction is based on Fath al-Qadir and practice of the Prophet (PBUH) at Uhud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما كيفية وضعها فإن كان الجنس متحداً فإن شاؤوا جعلوها صفاً واحداً كما يصطفون في حال حياتهم عند الصلاة وإن شاؤوا وضعوا واحداً بعد واحد مما يلي القبلة ليقوم الإمام بحذاء الكل. هذا جواب ظاهر الرواية، وفي رواية الحسن أن الثاني أولى من الأول. وإذا وضعوا واحداً بعد واحد ينبغي أن يكون الأفضل مما يلي الإمام، ثم إن وضع رأس كل واحد بحذاء رأس صاحبه فحسن وإن وضع رأس كل واحد عند منكب الأول فحسن، وإن اختلف الجنس وضع الرجل بين يدي الإمام، ثم الصبي وراءه ثم الخنثى ثم المرأة ثم الصبية. والأفضل أن يجعل الحر مما يلي الإمام ويقدم على العبد ولو كان الحر صبياً كما في الظهيرية وإن كان عبداً وامرأة حرة فالعبد يوضع مما يلي الإمام والمرأة خلفه. وفي فتح القدير : ولو اجتمعوا في قبر واحد فوضعهم على عكس هذا فيقدم الأفضل فالأفضل إلى القبلة، وفي الرجلين يقدم أكبرهما سناً وقرآناً وعلماً كما فعله عليه السلام في قتلى أحد من المسلمين اهـ. وفي البدائع : ولو كان رجل وامرأة قدم الرجل مما يلي القبلة ثم الصبي خلفه اعتباراً بحال الحياة، ولو اجتمع رجل وامرأة وصبي وخنثى وصبية دفن الرجل مما يلي القبلة ثم الصبي خلفه ثم الخنثى ثم الأنثى ثم الصبية لأنهم هكذا يصطفون خلف الإمام حالة الحياة وهكذا توضع جنائزهم عند الصلاة فكذا في القبر اهـ. وهو سهو وفي قوله وهكذا توضع جنائزهم لما ذكرنا أنه على عكسه.
And as for the manner of placing them: if the gender is uniform, if they wish they make them a single row just as they line up in their lives during prayer, and if they wish they place them one after another facing the qibla so that the imam stands opposite all. This is the answer of the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), and in a narration of al-Hasan the second is better than the first. When they place them one after another, the most virtuous should be next to the imam. Then if they place the head of each level with the head of his companion, that is good; and if they place the head of each at the shoulder of the first, that is good. If the genders differ, they place the man before the imam, then the boy behind him, then the hermaphrodite, then the woman, then the girl. It is better to place the free one next to the imam and give him precedence over the slave, even if the free one is a boy, as in al-Zahiriyyah. If there is a slave and a free woman, the slave is placed next to the imam and the woman behind him. In Fath al-Qadir: if they are gathered in one grave, their placement is the reverse of this: the most virtuous are placed first towards the qibla. For two men, the older in age, Quran, and knowledge is given precedence, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did with the martyrs of Uhud. In al-Bada'i': if there is a man and a woman, the man is placed first towards the qibla, then the boy behind him, considering the state of life. If a man, woman, boy, hermaphrodite, and girl are gathered, the man is buried first towards the qibla, then the boy behind him, then the hermaphrodite, then the female, then the girl, because they line up like this behind the imam during life, and thus their funeral biers are placed during prayer, so likewise in the grave. But this is a mistake, and his statement 'and thus their funeral biers are placed' is contrary to what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage details the proper placement of multiple funeral biers for a collective funeral prayer. The author presents rulings from the Hanafi school. If all deceased are the same gender, they may be placed in a single row (like living worshippers) or one behind the other facing the qibla, with the imam standing opposite them all. The preferred method in Zahir al-Riwayah is the single row; a narration from al-Hasan holds the second method better. When placing one behind another, the most meritorious should be nearest the imam. If genders differ, men come first in front of the imam, then boys, hermaphrodites, women, and girls. Free persons are placed closer to the imam than slaves, even if the free person is a child. The author notes a disputed point: some scholars, like in al-Bada'i', claimed that the arrangement in the grave mirrors the arrangement during prayer (men closest to the imam), but the author corrects this, stating it is the opposite. The passage includes references from various Hanafi sources such as al-Zahiriyyah, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): Hermaphrodite; a person with ambiguous gender who is treated as a separate category in arrangement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mixed-gender funeral, what is the correct order of biers from closest to furthest from the imam?
A) Man, woman, boy, khuntha, girl.
B) Man, boy, khuntha, woman, girl.
C) Woman, man, boy, girl, khuntha.
D) Boy, man, khuntha, woman, girl.

Key Takeaway
Mixed-gender biers are ordered by virtue: men, boys, hermaphrodites, women, girls; and burial arrangement is the reverse.

Ruling on Funeral Prayer for a Child with One Muslim Parent or Who Converts
Defines when a child receives funeral prayer if with one Muslim parent or if the child converts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criteria for a child to be considered Muslim for funeral prayer in the Hanafi school and apply the distinction between external and internal Islam.

Core Idea
A child follows the better parent in religion; conversion requires understanding ('aql), not mere utterance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies when a minor child is considered Muslim for the purpose of funeral prayer. Building on the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitra,' the Hanafi school determines the child's religious status by parental religion or, if the child converts, by his level of understanding. The discussion also distinguishes between the external ruling (zahir al-shar') and inner reality, a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The child is a follower of his parents. If both are non-Muslim, no funeral prayer is performed over him. The hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitra...' is cited as the basis.
This applies only when both parents are alive and non-Muslim.
2
Recognize the exception for a Muslim parent
If one parent converts to Islam, the child becomes Muslim by following the better parent (i.e., the Muslim). Funeral prayer is performed.
The child does not need to personally convert; the parent's Islam suffices.
3
Analyze the child's own conversion
If both parents remain non-Muslim but the child converts, his Islam is valid provided he has understanding ('aql). The passage discusses differing interpretations of 'aql: some require basic discrimination (mumayyiz, age 7+), others require understanding the tenets of faith.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is age 7 or the ability to independently eat, drink, and clean oneself.
4
Distinguish external vs. inner Islam
The passage notes that merely uttering the shahada is sufficient for the external ruling (zahir al-shar'), but inner conviction is required for the reality of Islam. This distinction prevents confusion when dealing with children or hypocrites.
In practice, a child who says the shahada is treated as a Muslim externally, even if his inner state is uncertain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (كصبي سيء مع أحد أبويه) أي لا يصلى عليه لأنه تبع لهما للحديث كل مولود يولد على الفطرة فأبواه يهودانه إلى آخره» (۱) . وتقدم في غسل الجنابة معنى الفطرة وأفاد بقوله (إلا أن يسلم أحدهما أنه يصلي عليه لإسلامه تبعاً للمسلم منهما لأنه يتبع خيرهما ديناً وأفاد بقوله (أو هو أنه يصلى عليه إذا أسلم وأبواه كافران لصحة إسلامه عندنا. وأطلقه وقيده في الهداية بأن يعقل الإسلام واختلف في تفسيره ؛ فقيل أن يعقل المنافع والمضار وأن الإسلام هدى واتباعه خير له ذكره في العناية وفسره في فتح القدير بأن يعقل صفة الإسلام وهو ما في الحديث أن تؤمن بالله أي بوجوده و بربوبيته لكل شيء «وملائكته» أي بوجود ملائكته وكتبه» أي إنزالها «ورسله» أي إرسالهم إليهم عليهم السلام واليوم الآخر» أي البعث بعد الموت والقدر خيره وشر من الله تعالى». وهذا دليل أن مجرد قوله «لا إله إلا الله» ا هـ. لكن في الشرنبلالية يمكن التوفيق بأن من نفى غسله أراد الغسل المراعي فيه وجه السنة، ومن أثبته أراد الغسل في الجملة كصب الماء عليه من غير وضوئه وترتيب لفعله كغسله ابتداء بحرض وسدر قوله : (واختلف في تفسيره قال في النهر وفي فتاوى قارئ الهداية المراد بالعاقل المميز وهو من بلغ سبع سنين فما فوقها، فلو ادعى أبوه أنه ابن خمس وأمه أنه ابن سبع عرض على أهل الخبرة ورجع إليهم في ذلك ا.هـ. وكان ينبغي أن يقال ما قيل في الحضانة عند اختلاف الأبوين في سنة إذا كان يأكل وحده ويشرب وحده ويستنجي وحده فابن سبع وإلا فلا قوله : (وهذا دليل أن مجرد قول لا إله إلا الله لا يوجب الحكم (الخ الظاهر أن المراد لا يوجب الحكم بالإسلام في نفس الأمر وإلا ففي ظاهر الشرع يكتفى بالإقرار بالشهادتين كما كان يفعل صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم لأنه دليل على ما في الباطن، وإن لم يكن مقراً باطناً كالمنافق فهو مسلم حكماً
His statement: (Like a child who is with one of his parents) i.e., no prayer is performed over him because he is a follower of them due to the hadith: 'Every child is born upon the fitra, then his parents make him a Jew, Christian, or Magian.' And the meaning of fitra was previously discussed in the section on washing from janabah. And he indicated by his statement (Except if one of them becomes Muslim) that prayer is performed over him because of his Islam following the Muslim parent, because he follows the better of them in religion. And he indicated by his statement (Or if he himself [becomes Muslim]) that prayer is performed over him if he becomes Muslim while both parents are disbelievers, because his Islam is valid in our school. And he made it absolute but restricted it in al-Hidaya by his understanding of Islam, and they differed regarding its interpretation. It was said: He understands benefits and harms, and that Islam is guidance and following it is good for him. Mentioned in al-Inaya. And it was explained in Fath al-Qadir as: He understands the description of Islam, which is what is in the hadith: to believe in Allah (i.e., in His existence and His lordship over everything), in His angels (i.e., their existence), in His books (i.e., their revelation), in His messengers (i.e., their sending to them, peace be upon them), in the Last Day (i.e., resurrection after death), and in fate, good and evil from Allah. This proves that mere saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' (does not suffice). etc. However, in al-Sharnaballaliyya, one can reconcile that whoever denies washing him intended the washing that observes the sunnah method, and whoever affirms it intended washing in general, like pouring water on him without wudu and order, like washing him initially with lotus leaves and sidr. His statement: (And they differed regarding its interpretation) He said in al-Nahr and in Fatawa Qari' al-Hidaya: The intended meaning of 'one of sound mind' is the discerning child, i.e., one who has reached seven years or more. So if his father claims he is five and his mother claims he is seven, the matter is referred to experts, and they rely on them in that. etc. And one should say what was said in custody regarding the parents' dispute about his age: if he eats alone, drinks alone, and cleans himself alone, then he is seven; otherwise not. His statement: (And this is evidence that mere saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' does not necessitate the ruling) etc. Apparently what is meant is that it does not necessitate the ruling of Islam in reality, otherwise in the external ruling of the Shari'ah, affirmation of the two shahadahs is sufficient, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do, because it is evidence of what is in the inner self, even if the person is not inwardly affirming, like the hypocrite, he is ruled as a Muslim.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage discusses the funeral prayer for a child who has one Muslim parent or who converts to Islam. The author states that normally a child with both parents disbelievers is not prayed over because he follows them in religion, based on the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitra, then his parents make him a Jew...' However, if one parent becomes Muslim, the child is considered a Muslim by following the better parent, and funeral prayer is performed over him. If the child himself becomes Muslim while both parents are disbelievers, his Islam is valid according to the Hanafi school, provided he has understanding ('aql). The author notes that al-Hidaya restricts this by requiring that the child understands Islam. There is a difference of opinion on what constitutes understanding: some say he understands benefits and harms, others require understanding of the basic tenets of Islam as mentioned in the hadith of Jibril. The passage clarifies that mere utterance of the shahada is not sufficient for the inner reality of Islam, but in external Shari'ah rulings, it is sufficient, as was the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who accepted the shahada as evidence of faith, even from hypocrites. Thus, a child who says the shahada is ruled as a Muslim externally. Regarding the age of discernment, the relied-upon view is seven years or the ability to independently eat, drink, and clean oneself.

Key Terms
الفطرة (al-fitrah): The innate disposition to believe in monotheism; every child is born upon it.
المميز (al-mumayyiz): A discerning child, typically age seven or able to independently perform basic tasks.
العاقل (al-'aql): One of sound mind; for a child, it means having understanding of Islam's basic beliefs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The child must have understanding ('aql) of Islam
C) The child must be accompanied by a Muslim guardian
D) The child must fast before conversion

Key Takeaway
A child's Islam for funeral prayer is determined by having a Muslim parent or converting with understanding; externally, the shahada is accepted.

Funeral Prayer for a Captive Child with Muslim Parent
Ruling on funeral prayer for a captive child with one parent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios where a captive child's funeral prayer is performed and explain the condition of understanding required for a child's valid conversion.

Core Idea
A captive child follows his parents; prayer is only performed if a parent becomes Muslim, child converts with understanding, or child enters Dar al-Islam alone.

This lesson unpacks a detailed ruling from the funerals chapter: when is funeral prayer performed for a captive child (sabi) who has one parent with him? The default is no prayer because the child follows his disbelieving parents. But three exceptions shift the ruling. We will examine each exception, especially the child's own conversion, which requires a specific level of understanding (aql). The text also provides guidance on how to ascertain that understanding without demanding eloquent expression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling and its proof
The passage states: no funeral prayer is performed for a captive child with his parents, because the child follows them in religion, citing the hadith 'Every child is born upon fitrah, then his parents make him a Jew, etc.' This default applies unless one of the listed exceptions occurs.
The hadith of fitrah establishes that a child's religion is initially determined by his parents.
2
First exception: one parent becomes Muslim
If one of the child's parents converts to Islam, the child is considered Muslim by following the Muslim parent, because the child follows the better of the two in religion. Consequently, funeral prayer is performed for the child.
This is a simple application of the principle that a minor follows the better religion of his parents.
3
Second exception: child converts with understanding
If the child himself embraces Islam while both parents remain disbelievers, funeral prayer is performed, provided the child has understanding (ya'qil al-Islam). The text clarifies that mere utterance of the shahada is insufficient; the child must genuinely believe in the six articles of faith (God, angels, books, messengers, Last Day, destiny).
Al-Hidayah restricts the absolute statement of the matn to this condition. There is ikhtilaf on the definition of 'aql; the relied-upon view is understanding the basic tenets.
4
Practical test for understanding
The passage advises that one should not ask a common person 'What is faith?' expecting a technical answer. Instead, the judge should explain the articles of faith and then ask for affirmation (e.g., 'Do you believe this?'). If the person says yes, it suffices. This avoids rejecting sincere converts who lack eloquence.
This is a practical adaptation to avoid judging by appearance only.
5
Third exception: child enters Dar al-Islam without parents
If neither parent is captured with the child and the child enters Dar al-Islam, he is considered Muslim following the land (or the captor), and funeral prayer is performed for him.
This is based on the principle that a child without parents in Dar al-Islam takes the ruling of the land.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (كصبي سيء مع أحد أبويه) أي لا يصلى عليه لأنه تبع لهما للحديث كل مولود يولد على الفطرة فأبواه يهودانه إلى آخره» (۱) . وتقدم في غسل الجنابة معنى الفطرة وأفاد بقوله (إلا أن يسلم أحدهما أنه يصلي عليه لإسلامه تبعاً للمسلم منهما لأنه يتبع خيرهما ديناً وأفاد بقوله (أو هو أنه يصلى عليه إذا أسلم وأبواه كافران لصحة إسلامه عندنا. وأطلقه وقيده في الهداية بأن يعقل الإسلام واختلف في تفسيره ؛ فقيل أن يعقل المنافع والمضار وأن الإسلام هدى واتباعه خير له ذكره في العناية وفسره في فتح القدير بأن يعقل صفة الإسلام وهو ما في الحديث أن تؤمن بالله أي بوجوده و بربوبيته لكل شيء «وملائكته» أي بوجود ملائكته وكتبه» أي إنزالها «ورسله» أي إرسالهم إليهم عليهم السلام واليوم الآخر» أي البعث بعد الموت والقدر خيره وشر من الله تعالى». وهذا دليل أن مجرد قوله «لا إله إلا الله» لا يوجب الحكم بالإسلام ما لم يؤمن بما ذكرنا وعلى هذا قالوا لو اشترى جارية أو تزوّج امرأة فاستوصفها صفة الإسلام فلم تعرفه لا تكون مسلمة. والمراد من عدم المعرفة ليس ما يظهر من التوقف في جواب ما الأيمان ما الإسلام كما يكون من بعض العوام لقصورهم في التعبير بل قيام الجهل بذلك بالباطن مثلاً بأن البعث هل يوجد أو لا، وأن الرسل وإنزال الكتب عليهم كان أو لا، لا يكون في اعتقاده اعتقاد طرف الإثبات للجهل البسيط فعن ذلك قالت لا أعرفه، وقل ما يكون ذلك لمن نشأ في دار الإسلام فإنا نسمع ممن قد يقول في جواب ما قلنا لا أعرف وهو من التوحيد والإقرار والخوف من النار وطلب الجنة بمكان، بل وذكر ما يصلح استدلالاً في أثناء أحوالهم وتكلمهم على التصريح ما يصرح باعتقاد هذه الأمور وكانوا يظنون أن جواب هذه الأشياء إنما يكون بكلام خاص منظوم وعبارة عالية حاجة فيحجمون عن الجواب .اهـ. فعلى هذا فينبغي أن لا يسأل العامي والمرأة على هذا الوجه بأن يقال ما الأيمان، وإنما يذكر حقيقة الإيمان وما يجب الإيمان به بحضرتهما، ثم يقال له هل أنت مصدق بهذا فإذا قال نعم كان ذلك كافياً. وأفاد بقوله . (أو لم يسب أحدهما معه أنه يصلي عليه إذا دخل دار الإسلام ولم يكن معه أحد أبويه تبعاً لدار الإسلام وفي التبيين أي إذا لم يسب مع الصبي أحد أبويه فحينئذ يصلى عليه تبعاً للسابي أو الدار اهـ. فجعل كلام المصنف شاملاً لتبعية السابي ولتبعية الدار
His statement: (like a captive child with one of his parents) i.e., funeral prayer is not performed for him because he follows them due to the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitrah, then his parents make him a Jew, etc.' And the meaning of fitrah preceded in washing of janabah. And he benefited by his statement (except if one of them becomes Muslim) that prayer is performed for him due to his Islam following the Muslim parent, because he follows the better of them in religion. And he benefited by his statement (or he himself) that prayer is performed for him if he becomes Muslim while his parents are disbelievers, because his Islam is valid with us. He made it absolute and al-Hidayah restricted it to the condition that he understands Islam, and there is difference in its interpretation. It is said: he understands benefits and harms and that Islam is guidance and following it is good for him, mentioned in al-Inayah. And it is explained in Fath al-Qadir: he understands the description of Islam, which is what is in the hadith: to believe in Allah (i.e., His existence and Lordship over everything) and His angels (i.e., the existence of His angels) and His books (i.e., their revelation) and His messengers (i.e., their sending to them, peace be upon them) and the Last Day (i.e., resurrection after death) and destiny, its good and evil from Allah. And this is evidence that merely saying 'There is no god but Allah' does not necessitate the ruling of Islam unless he believes what we have mentioned. And on this basis they said: if a person buys a slave-girl or marries a woman and asks her to describe the quality of Islam and she does not know it, she is not a Muslim. And the meaning of 'lack of knowledge' is not the apparent hesitation in answering 'What is faith? What is Islam?' as occurs from some common people due to their deficiency in expression, but rather inner ignorance of that, for example whether resurrection exists or not, and whether the messengers and revelation of books occurred or not. So that is from simple ignorance. Thus she says: 'I do not know it.' And rarely is that in one who grew up in Dar al-Islam, for we hear from someone who might say in answer to what we said 'I do not know' while he is [well-versed] in tawhid and affirmation and fear of hellfire and seeking paradise, and indeed he mentions what suffices as evidence in his circumstances and his speech explicitly expresses belief in these matters. They thought that answering these things requires special arranged speech and high expression, so they refrain from answering. So on this basis, one should not ask the common person and the woman in this manner by saying 'What is faith?' Rather, the reality of faith and what must be believed should be mentioned in their presence, then asked 'Do you believe this?' If he says yes, that is sufficient. And he benefited by his statement (or if neither parent was captured with him) that prayer is performed for him if he enters Dar al-Islam and neither parent is with him, due to following Dar al-Islam. And in al-Tabyin: if neither parent was captured with the boy, then he is prayed upon following the captor or the land. So he made the author's statement inclusive of following the captor and following the land.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling within the chapter of funerals. It addresses the funeral prayer for a child who is a captive (sabi) and has one parent with him. The default ruling: no prayer is performed for such a child because he follows the religion of his disbelieving parents, based on the hadith of fitrah. However, if one of the parents converts to Islam, the child is considered Muslim by following the Muslim parent, and prayer is performed. If the child himself converts to Islam while both parents remain disbelievers, his conversion is valid according to the Hanafi school, but only if he has understanding (ya'qil al-Islam). There is ikhtilaf on the definition of 'aql: some say he understands benefits and harms; al-Hidayah explains it as understanding the basic articles of faith as mentioned in the famous hadith of Jibril. The text then deduces that merely uttering the shahada without inner belief does not make one a Muslim in the sight of Allah, though outwardly it suffices for legal purposes. However, for a child's conversion to be valid, he must have true understanding. The passage also discusses the practical test: if a person asks a potential convert about faith and they hesitate due to lack of eloquence, judges should not take that as rejection. Instead, the judge should explain faith and then ask for affirmation. Finally, the ruling for a child who enters Dar al-Islam without his parents: he is considered Muslim following Dar al-Islam (or following the captor), and funeral prayer is performed for him.

Key Terms
السبي (al-sabiyy): A child taken captive from Dar al-Harb. In this context, a child captured with his parents who are presumably non-Muslim.
العاقل (al-'aqil): One who has understanding of Islam, specifically the basic tenets: belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, Last Day, and destiny.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is a captive child who has both parents disbelievers still prayed over?
A) If the child is above 7 years old.
B) If the child himself converts to Islam with understanding.
C) If the child was born in Dar al-Islam.
D) If the child was purchased by a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer is performed for a captive child if one parent converts, or if the child converts with understanding of the six articles, or if he enters Dar al-Islam without parents.

Determining the Status of a Captive Child: Taba'iyyah to Dar, Yad, or Parents?
Internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on taba'iyyah of a captive child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three bases of taba'iyyah for a captive child's religion and apply the Hanafi tarjih to determine whether dar or possession takes precedence.

Core Idea
A captive child's religion follows the parent, the abode, or the captor; the Hanafi preferred view gives precedence to the abode over possession.

This lesson examines a nuanced discussion from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq about the legal status of a child captured in dar al-harb. The Hanafi school has multiple positions on whether the child is considered Muslim by following the abode (dar), the captor's possession (yad), or the parents. We will work through the sources and the tarjih mechanism that leads to the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three avenues of taba'iyyah
Extract from the text the three factors that can determine a child's religion: following the parents, following the abode (dar al-Islam or dar al-harb), and following the captor (or possessor, yad).
The text mentions 'تبعية الولاد' (lineage), 'تبعية الدار' (abode), and 'تبعية اليد' (possession).
2
Locate the point of disagreement
The Hanafi school agrees that all three apply, but differs on which takes precedence when they conflict. The main conflict is between dar and yad.
The author of al-Hidayah and Qadikhan give precedence to dar; al-Muhit gives precedence to yad.
3
Examine the proof for the preferred view
The text cites a case from Kashf al-Asrar: a dhimmī steals a child and brings him to dar al-Islam; the child becomes Muslim by following the dar, and no disagreement is reported.
This is used as evidence that dar takes priority over the captor's yad.
4
Analyze the opposing view and its rebuttal
Al-Muhit argues that yad takes precedence, but the author notes that yad is only agreed upon when not in dar al-Islam, so it cannot serve as a preference in this context.
The text states: 'فإن تبعية اليد عند عدم الكون في دار الإسلام متفق عليه فلا يصلح مرجحاً'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The author leans towards al-Hidayah: dar over yad. The practical thamarah: if a captive child dies in dar al-harb, he is prayed over as Muslim because he follows the captor's yad (or possibly dar, depending on context).
The main impact is whether the child is given a Muslim funeral or not.

Book of Funerals, Section: The Sultan is most entitled to lead his funeral prayer. The four [rulings]: hasten with it without brisk walking, sitting before placing it [the bier], walking in front of it, placing its front on [the shoulder]... As in Diya' al-Hulum. The benefit of following the captor is evident only in dar al-harb: if a child falls into the share of a man and dies in dar al-harb, he is prayed over following the captor. The apparent meaning of what is in Diya' al-Hulum is that it is necessary to transport from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam to be called a captive. In Fath al-Qadir: 'There is disagreement about following lineage. According to al-Hidayah, it is following the dar; according to al-Muhit, in the absence of one parent, possession (yad) applies, and in the absence of the possessor, it follows the dar, and perhaps that is better. If a child falls into someone's share of booty in dar al-harb and dies, he is prayed over and considered Muslim following the possessor.' End. There is consideration in this because following possession in the absence of being in dar al-Islam is agreed upon, so it cannot serve as a preference for what is in al-Muhit regarding the precedence of following possession over the dar. The conclusion is that there is agreement on following by the three avenues, and the only point of disagreement is priority of dar over possession. The author of al-Hidayah, Qadikhan, and a group give precedence to dar over possession, and that is more appropriate due to what is transmitted in Kashf al-Asrar: 'If a dhimmī steals a child and takes him out to dar al-Islam and the child dies, he is prayed over and becomes Muslim by following the dar, and the taking is not considered; he must be rescued from his hand.' End. No disagreement is mentioned. This is a refutation of what is in al-Muhit, because its implication is that he would not be prayed over, giving precedence to possession over the dar, unless there is disagreement. The author (of Kanz) gave absolute statement regarding the child and did not restrict it to the non-rational. The muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in his Tahrir restricted it to the non-rational, saying: 'If he is rational, he is independent in his Islam and does not apostatize by the apostasy of one of his parents.' End. The apparent meaning of al-Zayla'i's statement is that he used to justify following possession by saying the young child who cannot express himself is akin to property, and he attributed that to Sharh al-Ziyadat. So their apparent meaning is that even if one of his parents is a disbeliever, a rational child does not become a disbeliever in following his father, but becomes Muslim following the dar, and needs explicit transmission. Their statements indicate otherwise, for they made 'sabi' and zakat on camels or adhan... [unclear]. His statement: 'And the apparent meaning of what is in Diya' al-Hulum is that it is necessary...' i.e., and in that case it is not what we are discussing because the discussion is about the captive, and as long as he is in dar al-harb, there is no benefit in mentioning the so-called captor. I said: What appears is that what is in Diya' al-Hulum is not meant apparently because it contradicts what is in al-Sihah and al-Qamus, since they mentioned that it is said 'the enemy captured prisoners' and 'captured him' meaning he took him as a prisoner, so he is a captive and she is a captive, and the plural is 'subaba'. So they indicated that 'sabi' applies to the act of capturing and to the captured, i.e., the source and the passive participle, without observing the condition of transportation from land to land. Yes, they mentioned that condition in the context of 'sabi al-khamra' (transporting wine), for it is said 'I transported the wine' if you carried it from a land, so it is a transport. His statement: 'And their statements indicate otherwise.' Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Hajj said in Sharh al-Tahrir in the section on the judge after mentioning taba'iyyah to parents, then to dar, then to the captor, the text: 'What is in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam: it is the same in what we said whether he is rational or not. This is indicated in this book and stated in al-Jami' al-Kabir. Consequently, he said in his commentary: if one of his parents becomes Muslim, he is made Muslim by following, whether the child is rational or not because the child follows the better religion of the parents.' End quote. I say: And I also saw it in Sharh al-Siyar.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the funeral prayer etiquettes and then delves into a major juristic discussion about the legal status of a captive child. The main point is determining whether a child who is captured or born in dar al-harb is considered Muslim or not. Three factors are considered: following the parents (taba'iyyah li al-abawayn), following the abode (taba'iyyah li al-dar), and following the captor (taba'iyyah li al-sabi). The Hanafi school has ikhtilaf on which takes precedence. The text reports that al-Hidayah and Qadikhan favor the dar, while al-Muhit favors possession (yad). Ibn al-Humam restricts the rulings to non-rational children, as a rational child can independently choose Islam. The commentary also includes a linguistic discussion about the word 'sabi' (captive) and references to linguistic sources like al-Sihah and al-Qamus.

Key Terms
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Following the status of another (parent, captor, or abode)

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi preferred view is that a non-rational captive child's status follows the abode (dar al-Islam) over the captor's possession, making him Muslim.
