Walking Behind the Funeral Bier: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling on walking position with inter-madhhab dispute and subsidiary rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on walking position in a funeral procession and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In a funeral procession, the follower walks behind, not in front—the shaf'i (intercessor) analogy does not apply.

The proper position of participants in a funeral procession is a matter of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While the Shafi'is analogize the follower to an intercessor (shaf'i) who advances to prepare, the Hanafis insist that the follower is a 'mushayyi' (follower) who must remain behind. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the disputed question: what is the preferred walking position for participants in a funeral procession?
The dispute is about afdaliyya (which is better), not permissibility.
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds walking behind the bier is better. Their proof includes hadiths about following funerals and a rational argument: participants are followers (mushayyi'un), so they should be behind.
The hadiths are general but the rational argument distinguishes the follower from an intercessor.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and its analogy
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the participant is like a shaf'i (intercessor) who should advance to prepare the objective, thus walking in front is better.
This is a qiyas (analogy) based on the role of the imam in funeral prayer as intercessor.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and the thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy: the intercessor in prayer is specifically advanced by Shari'ah, but this does not extend to the walking procession. The practical difference is that Hanafis walk behind, Shafi'is walk in front.
The Hanafi view is supported by the practice of the Salaf and is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ومشى قدامها) أي بلا مشي لمتبعها أمامها لأن المشي خلفها أفضل عندنا للأحاديث الواردة باتباع الجنائز، وقد نقل فعل السلف على الوجهين والترجيح بالمعنى، فالشافعي يقول والشفيع يتقدم ليمهد المقصود، ونحن نقول هم مشيعون فيتأخرون والشفيع المتقدم هو الذي لا يستصحب المشفوع له في الشفاعة وما نحن فيه بخلافه، بل قد ثبت شرعاً إلزام تقديمه حالة الشفاعة له أعني حالة الصلاة فثبت شرعاً عدم اعتبار ما اعتبره. قالوا: ويجوز المشي أمامها إلا أن يتباعد عنها أو يتقدم الكل فيكره ولا يمشي عن يمينها ولا عن شمالها. وذكر الأسبيجابي: ولا بأس بأن يذهب إلى صلاة الجنازة راكباً غير أنه يكره له التقدم أمام الجنازة بخلاف الماشي. اهـ. وبهذا يضعف ما نقله ابن الملك في شرح المجمع معزياً إلى أبي يوسف فقال: رأيت أبا حنيفة يتقدم الجنازة وهو راكب ثم قعد حتى تأتيه. كذا في النوادر اهـ. وفي الظهيرية والمشي فيها أفضل من الركوب كصلاة الجمعة. وفي الغاية: اتباع الجنائز أفضل من النوافل إذا كان الجوار أو قرابة أو صلاح مشهور وإلا فالنوافل أفضل. وينبغي لمن تبع جنازة أن يطيل الصمت ويكره رفع الصوت بالذكر وقراءة القرآن وغيرهما في الجنازة، والكراهة فيها كراهة تحريم في فتاوى العصر وعند مجد الأئمة التركماني. وقال علاء الدين الناصري: ترك الأولى. اهـ. وفي الظهيرية: فإن أراد أن يذكر الله يذكره في نفسه لقوله تعالى {أنه لا يحب المعتدين} [الأعراف: ٥٥] أي الجاهرين بالدعاء وعن إبراهيم أنه كان يكره أن يقول الرجل وهو يمشي معها استغفروا له غفر الله لكم. وفي البدائع: ولا ينبغي أن يرجع من الرملي: وهو مقيد بعدم الحاجة والضرورة ذكر الحلبي في شرح منية المصلي وهو ظاهر ومقتضى الدليل الآتي أنها كراهة تحريم تأمل قوله: فلذا كره يفيد أن قول البدائع «فلا بأس بالجلوس» ليس جارياً. ما الغالب في استعماله فيما تركه أولى قوله: قالوا ويجوز المشي أمامها إلا أن يتباعد الخ) قال الرملي: الظاهر أنها كراهة تنزيه وكذا بعده.
His statement: (And he walks in front of it) meaning: no walking for the follower in front of it, because walking behind it is better according to us due to the hadiths reported about following funerals. And the practice of the Salaf has been transmitted on both sides, and the preponderance is by meaning. So al-Shafi'i says: The intercessor advances to prepare the objective. And we say: They are followers, so they should be behind. The intercessor who advances is one who does not bring the one for whom he intercedes in the intercession, and our case is different. Rather, the Shari'ah has established the necessity of advancing him in the state of intercession for him, meaning the state of prayer, so the Shari'ah has established the disregard for what he considered. They said: It is permissible to walk in front of it unless one moves away from it or all advance, then it is disliked, and one should not walk to its right or left. And al-Asbijabi mentioned: There is no harm in going to the funeral prayer riding, except that it is disliked for him to advance ahead of the funeral, unlike the pedestrian. End quote. And by this, that which Ibn al-Malik narrated in Sharh al-Majma' attributing to Abu Yusuf is weakened: 'I saw Abu Hanifah advance ahead of the funeral while riding, then he sat until it came to him.' Thus in al-Nawadir. End quote. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Walking in it is better than riding, like the Friday prayer. And in al-Ghayah: Following funerals is better than supererogatory prayers if there is neighborliness, kinship, or well-known righteousness; otherwise, supererogatory prayers are better. It is befitting for whoever follows a funeral to prolong silence, and it is disliked to raise the voice with remembrance, recitation of Quran, or other things in the funeral. The dislike therein is proscribed (karahah tahrim) according to the fatwas of the age and according to Majd al-A'immah al-Turkmani. And 'Ala' al-Din al-Nasiri said: It is abandoning the preferable. End quote. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he wants to remember Allah, he remembers in himself due to His statement: 'He does not love the transgressors' [al-A'raf: 55] i.e., those who are loud in supplication. And from Ibrahim that he used to dislike that a man say while walking with her: 'Ask forgiveness for him, may Allah forgive you.' And in al-Bada'i': One should not return from the... al-Ramli: It is conditioned by lack of need and necessity. Al-Halabi mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, and it is apparent, and the implication of the evidence below is that it is a proscribed dislike (karahah tahrim). Consider his statement: 'Therefore it is disliked' indicates that the statement of al-Bada'i' 'there is no harm in sitting' is not operative. What is most used in it is leaving the preferable. His statement: 'They said: It is permissible to walk in front of it unless he moves away etc.' Al-Ramli said: Apparently it is a permissible dislike (karahah tanzih), and likewise what follows.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the proper position of participants in a funeral procession. The commentator explains the Hanafi position that walking behind the bier is superior, contrary to the Shafi'i view. He provides both textual evidence (hadiths about following funerals) and rational arguments: the participants are followers (mushayyi'un), so they should be behind, while the Shafi'i view analogizes the participant to an intercessor who advances. The Hanafi response emphasizes that the Shafi'i analogy is invalid because in the case of funeral prayer, the intercessor (the imam) is indeed advanced, but that is a specific ritual requirement. The passage then addresses subsidiary rulings: it is permissible to walk in front but disliked if one becomes distant or if all walk in front; one should not walk to the right or left. Riding to the funeral is permitted but disliked if one advances ahead of the bier, and walking is superior to riding. The text also includes rulings on silence during the funeral: it is recommended to remain silent and avoid raising the voice with dhikr or Quran. According to later fatwas, this is a proscribed dislike (karahah tahrim), but some scholars say it is merely leaving the preferable (tark al-ula). The commentary further discusses the ruling on sitting after the bier is placed, reconciling different reports.

Key Terms
الشفيع (al-shafī‘): The intercessor: here refers to the one who follows the funeral, analogized to an intercessor by Shafi'i.
المشيعون (al-mushayyi‘ūn): Followers of the funeral; those who accompany the bier.
كراهة تحريم (karāhah taḥrīm): Proscribed dislike: an act that is close to haram based on a speculative proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the preferred position for a follower when walking in a funeral procession?
A) Walking in front of the bier
B) Walking behind the bier
C) Walking to the right of the bier
D) Riding ahead of the bier

Key Takeaway
Hanafis walk behind the bier; Shafi'is walk in front; the difference stems from whether the follower is a shaf'i (intercessor) or a mushayyi' (follower).

Salah — Prayer

The General Ruling for the Martyr: No Washing, Prayer Obligatory
Explains the default treatment of the martyr: no wash, prayer, and burial clothes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the martyr regarding washing, shrouding, and prayer, and identify the primary proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The martyr is not washed but is buried in his bloody clothes, and prayer over him is wajib.

When a person dies a martyr in battle, a specific set of rules applies that differs from the ordinary deceased. The Hanafi school derives these rules primarily from the actions of the Prophet ﷺ after the Battle of Uhud. This lesson covers the core ruling: the martyr is not washed, but is shrouded in his own clothes (with some adjustments) and the funeral prayer is performed over him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Determine what is stated about washing, shrouding, and praying for the martyr. The text says: 'فيكفن ويصلى عليه بلا غسل' – He is shrouded and prayed over without washing.
2
Locate the dalil for no washing
Find the hadith cited as proof. The Prophet ﷺ ordered the martyrs of Uhud to be buried with their blood and clothes, indicating they should not be washed.
The hadith is from Sunan and Bukhari.
3
Locate the dalil for prayer
The proof is that the Prophet ﷺ prayed over Hamza and other martyrs at Uhud, and also prayed over them eight years later (as per Bukhari).
4
Understand the refutation of objections
The text refutes two objections: (1) Martyrs are alive, so prayer is invalid – responded by noting their life is otherworldly, worldly death applies. (2) Prayer is for forgiveness, but martyrs are forgiven – refuted by the example of the Prophet and children.
5
Note the ruling on clothing and shroud adjustment
The martyr is buried in his clothes, but items not part of the shroud (fur, weapons, cap, etc.) are removed. The shroud may be increased or decreased to match the sunnah standard of three pieces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن قوله : ( فيكفن ويصلى عليه بلا غسل بيان لحكمه . أما عدم الغسل فلحديث السنن أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بقتلى أحد أن ينزع عنهم الحديد والجلود وأن يدفنوا بدمائهم وثيابهم. وما علل به الحسن البصري لعدم الغسل بأنهم كانوا جرحى فقد قال السرخسي : إنه ليس بصحيح لأنه لو كان عدم الغسل باعتبار الجراحة لكان التيمم مشروعاً. وأما الصلاة فلصلاته عليه السلام على حمزة وغيره يوم أحد ولحديث البخاري أنه صلى على قتلى أحد بعد ثماني سنين. وما قيل من أنهم أحياء والحي لا يصلى عليه فمدفوع بأنه حكم أخروي لا دينوي بدليل ثبوت أحكام الموتى لهم من قسمة تركاتهم وبينونة نسائهم إلى غير ذلك. وما قيل من أنها للاستغفار وهم مغفور لهم فمنتقض بالنبي والصبي كما في الهداية وما في فتح القدير من أنه لو اقتصر على النبي لكان أولى فإن الدعاء في الصلاة على الصبي لأبويه فمدفوع من أن كلامه في نفس الصلاة لا في المدعو له، ولأن الصبي ليس بمستغن عن الرحمة فنفس الصلاة عليه رحمة له ونفس الدعاء الوارد لأبويه دعاء له لأنه إذا كان فرطاً لأبويه فقد تقدمهما في الخير لا سيما وقد قالوا: إن حسنات الصبي له لا لأبويه ولهما ثواب التعليم قوله : ( ويدفن بدمه وثيابه إلا ما ليس من الكفن ويزاد وينقص) بيان الحكم آخر له. وأشار إلى أنه يكره أن ينزع عنه جميع ثيابه ويجدد الكفن ذكره الأسبيجابي. وقالوا ما ليس من جنس الكفن الفرو والحشو والقلنسوة والسلاح والخف وقدمنا فيه كلاماً. واختلفوا في معنى قولهم يزاد وينقص ففي غاية البيان وغيرها : يزاد إن كان ما عليه ناقصاً عن كفن السنة، وينقص إن كان ما عليه زائداً على كفن السنة. وفي معراج الدراية : وبه استدل المشايخ على جواز الزيادة في الكفن على الثلاث. وفيه : ويجعل الحنوط للشهيد كالميت قوله : ( ويغسل إن قتل جنباً أو صبياً) بيان لشرطين آخرين للشهادة الأول الطهارة من الجنابة الثاني التكليف. أما الأول فهو قوله :وقالا : الجنب شهيد لأن ما . بالجنابة سقط بالموت. وله : إن الشهادة عرفت مانعة غير رافعة فلا ترفع الجنابة وقد صح أن حنظلة لما استشهد جنباً غسلته الملائكة. وعلى هذا الخلاف الحائض والنفساء إذا طهرتا وكذا قبل الانقطاع في الصحيح من الرواية كذا في الهداية. وفي معراج الدراية : وإنما لم يعد النبي صلى عليه وسلم غسل حنظلة لأن الواجب تأدى بدليل قصة آدم عليه السلام ولم تعد أولاده وهو الجواب عن قولهما لو كان واجباً لوجب على بني آدم ولما اكتفى به إذ الواجب نفس الغسل، فأما الغاسل يجوز من كان كما في قصة آدم ا هـ . وفيه أن هذا الغسل عنده للجنابة لا غسله وجب فهو شهيد ولا إشكال تدبر قوله : (فمدفوع من أن كلامه من نفس الصلاة لا في المدعو له) ذكر في النهر أن هذا الجواب ممنوع واقتصر على الثاني قوله : (وفي معراج الدراية وبه استدل المشايخ الخ) قال في النهر : هذا يفيد أن المراد يزاد على الثلاث وقد مر عن الغاية. قوله: (وفيه إن هذا الغسل (الخ تنظير فيما قاله في المعراج من الاستدلال بقصة آدم عليه السلام لأن هذا الغسل عند أبي حنيفة للجنابة لا للموت وما في القصة غيره. واعلم أن هذا الغسل لا يخلو إما أن يكون للجنابة أو للموت، فإن كان للجنابة فهو يتأدى من أي غاسل كان والجواب عن قولهما حينئذ ظاهر، وإن كان للموت وهو ظاهر كلام المعراج كما هو قضية تنظيره يفصة آدم عليه السلام فالجواب مشكل لما أنه لا مر من بد في إسقاط الفرض من فعل المكلفين حتى لو وجد في البحر لا بد من تغسيله، فقوله إذا لواجب نفس الغسل الخ ) غير ظاهر، ويجاب عن قصة آدم بأن
Regarding his statement: (He is shrouded and prayed over without washing) is an explanation of his ruling. As for not washing, it is due to the hadith in the Sunan that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered regarding the martyrs of Uhud to remove the iron and leather from them and to bury them with their blood and clothes. And what al-Hasan al-Basri reasoned for not washing, that they were wounded, al-Sarakhsi said: it is not correct, because if not washing were due to wounds, then tayammum would be legislated. As for prayer, it is due to his prayer (peace be upon him) upon Hamza and others on the day of Uhud, and the hadith of Bukhari that he prayed upon the martyrs of Uhud after eight years. And what is said that they are alive and the living is not prayed upon is refuted because it is an otherworldly ruling, not worldly, as evidenced by the application of rulings of the dead to them, such as division of estates and separation of wives, etc. And what is said that prayer is for seeking forgiveness and they are forgiven, is refuted by the Prophet and the child, as in al-Hidayah. And what is in Fath al-Qadir that if he limited it to the Prophet it would be better, because the supplication in prayer for the child is for his parents, is refuted because his speech is about the prayer itself, not the one prayed for, and because the child is not independent of mercy; the prayer itself is a mercy for him, and the supplication for his parents is a supplication for him because if he is a forerunner for his parents, he precedes them in good, especially since they said: the good deeds of the child are for him, and his parents have the reward of teaching. His statement: (And he is buried with his blood and clothes except what is not from the shroud, and it is increased and decreased) is an explanation of another ruling for him. And he indicated that it is disliked to remove all his clothes and renew the shroud, as mentioned by al-Asbiji. And they said: what is not of the type of shroud is the fur, stuffing, cap, weapon, and khuff, and we have mentioned discussion on it. And they differed on the meaning of their saying 'increase and decrease': in Ghayat al-Bayan and others: it is increased if what he has on is less than the sunnah shroud, and decreased if what he has on is more than the sunnah shroud. And in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: and by it the mashayikh used as evidence for the permissibility of increasing the shroud beyond three. And in it: and hanut is made for the martyr like the deceased. His statement: (And he is washed if he is killed in a state of janabah or is a child) is an explanation of two other conditions for martyrdom: first, purity from janabah; second, legal capacity. As for the first, it is his saying: and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the one in janabah is a martyr because what is [due] due to janabah falls with death. And he (Abu Hanifa) said: martyrdom is known as preventative, not remover, so it does not remove janabah, and it is authentically reported that when Hanzala was martyred in janabah, the angels washed him. And on this difference, the menstruating woman and postpartum if they become pure, and likewise before cessation in the correct narration, as in al-Hidayah. And in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not count the washing of Hanzala because the obligation was fulfilled, as evidenced by the story of Adam, and he did not count his children, and it is the answer to their statement that if it were obligatory, it would be obligatory upon the children of Adam and they would not be content with it, for the obligation is the washing itself; as for the washer, it is permissible to be whoever, as in the story of Adam. And in it: this washing for him is for janabah, not for death, so it is incumbent and he is a martyr, no problem. Ponder his statement: (it is refuted because his speech is about the prayer itself, not the one prayed for) it is mentioned in al-Nahr that this answer is rejected, and he limited to the second. His statement: (and in Mi'raj al-Dirayah, by it the mashayikh used as evidence) said in al-Nahr: this indicates that the intended meaning is increase beyond three, and it has passed from al-Ghayah. His statement: (and in it, this washing (etc.) is a refutation of what was said in al-Mi'raj from using the story of Adam as evidence, because this washing according to Abu Hanifa is for janabah, not for death, and what is in the story is other than it. And know that this washing is either for janabah or for death; if for janabah, it is performed by any washer, and the answer to their statement then is clear; and if for death, which is apparent from the wording of al-Mi'raj as the inference of the story of Adam, then the answer is problematic because there is no alternative to dropping the obligation from the actions of the obligated, even if he were found in the sea, he must be washed, so his statement 'if the obligation is the washing itself' etc. is not apparent, and the story of Adam is answered by...
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive commentary on the rulings for the martyr. It covers three main areas: (1) The martyr is not washed but is shrouded and prayed over. Proofs are given from the hadith of Uhud (washing removed, prayer established). Objections are refuted: that martyrs are alive, so prayer is invalid, is countered by noting it is an otherworldly life; that prayer seeks forgiveness while martyrs are forgiven is refuted by the example of the Prophet and children. (2) The martyr is buried in his clothes, but items not part of the shroud (e.g., fur, weapons) are removed. The shroud may be increased or decreased to meet the sunnah standard. (3) Exceptions to not washing: a martyr in a state of janabah or a child who is killed is washed. There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: the latter consider a person in janabah martyred without washing, citing the incident of Hanzala who was washed by angels. Abu Hanifa argues that martyrdom prevents but does not remove janabah, so washing is still due, but the obligation was fulfilled by angels. The text delves into the nuances of this dispute and attempts to reconcile using the story of Adam.

Key Terms
حنوط (hanut): Perfume applied to the shroud of the deceased, including the martyr.
كفن السنة (kafan al-sunnah): The standard shroud for a deceased, consisting of three garments for men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for not washing the martyr?
A) The Prophet said martyrs are pure.
B) The Prophet ordered the martyrs of Uhud to be buried with their blood and clothes.
C) The angels wash the martyrs.
D) The martyr is alive and does not need washing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the martyr is not washed, is buried in his own clothes (with adjustments), and the funeral prayer is wajib.

intermediate

Washing the Martyr in Janabah or When a Child
Explains the exception for janabah and child, and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on washing a martyr in a state of janabah, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The martyr killed in janabah is not washed; the child martyr is washed. Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn.

While the general rule is that the martyr is not washed, two exceptions are mentioned: the martyr in a state of janabah (major impurity) and a child. However, even the janabah case is disputed within the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether the martyr in janabah should be washed, and how the story of Hanzala is used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception in the text
The text states: 'ويغسل إن قتل جنباً أو صبياً' – he is washed if killed in a state of janabah or if a child. But a dispute follows.
2
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the one in janabah is still a martyr and not washed, because the obligation of janabah falls with death.
3
State the position of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa says martyrdom prevents but does not remove janabah; washing is still due, but the obligation was fulfilled by angels in the case of Hanzala.
4
Understand the evidence for each side
Sahibayn: the Prophet did not order washing Hanzala. Abu Hanifa: Hanzala was washed by angels, proving washing was still required.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its practical impact
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view: a martyr in janabah is not washed. The text indicates this is the preferred view.

His statement: (And he is washed if he is killed in a state of janabah or is a child) is an explanation of two other conditions for martyrdom: first, purity from janabah; second, legal capacity. As for the first, it is his saying: and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the one in janabah is a martyr because what is [due] due to janabah falls with death. And he (Abu Hanifa) said: martyrdom is known as preventative, not remover, so it does not remove janabah, and it is authentically reported that when Hanzala was martyred in janabah, the angels washed him. And on this difference, the menstruating woman and postpartum if they become pure, and likewise before cessation in the correct narration, as in al-Hidayah. And in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not count the washing of Hanzala because the obligation was fulfilled, as evidenced by the story of Adam, and he did not count his children, and it is the answer to their statement that if it were obligatory, it would be obligatory upon the children of Adam and they would not be content with it, for the obligation is the washing itself; as for the washer, it is permissible to be whoever, as in the story of Adam. And in it: this washing for him is for janabah, not for death, so it is incumbent and he is a martyr, no problem. Ponder his statement: (it is refuted because his speech is about the prayer itself, not the one prayed for) it is mentioned in al-Nahr that this answer is rejected, and he limited to the second. His statement: (and in Mi'raj al-Dirayah, by it the mashayikh used as evidence) said in al-Nahr: this indicates that the intended meaning is increase beyond three, and it has passed from al-Ghayah. His statement: (and in it, this washing (etc.) is a refutation of what was said in al-Mi'raj from using the story of Adam as evidence, because this washing according to Abu Hanifa is for janabah, not for death, and what is in the story is other than it. And know that this washing is either for janabah or for death; if for janabah, it is performed by any washer, and the answer to their statement then is clear; and if for death, which is apparent from the wording of al-Mi'raj as the inference of the story of Adam, then the answer is problematic because there is no alternative to dropping the obligation from the actions of the obligated, even if he were found in the sea, he must be washed, so his statement 'if the obligation is the washing itself' etc. is not apparent, and the story of Adam is answered by...
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive commentary on the rulings for the martyr. It covers three main areas: (1) The martyr is not washed but is shrouded and prayed over. Proofs are given from the hadith of Uhud (washing removed, prayer established). Objections are refuted: that martyrs are alive, so prayer is invalid, is countered by noting it is an otherworldly life; that prayer seeks forgiveness while martyrs are forgiven is refuted by the example of the Prophet and children. (2) The martyr is buried in his clothes, but items not part of the shroud (e.g., fur, weapons) are removed. The shroud may be increased or decreased to meet the sunnah standard. (3) Exceptions to not washing: a martyr in a state of janabah or a child who is killed is washed. There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: the latter consider a person in janabah martyred without washing, citing the incident of Hanzala who was washed by angels. Abu Hanifa argues that martyrdom prevents but does not remove janabah, so washing is still due, but the obligation was fulfilled by angels. The text delves into the nuances of this dispute and attempts to reconcile using the story of Adam.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): Person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
حنظلة (Hanzala): Companion who was martyred in a state of janabah and washed by angels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, how is a martyr who was in a state of janabah treated?
A) He is not washed because martyrdom removes the obligation.
B) He is washed by the community because of the janabah.
C) He is buried without any special treatment.
D) He is washed only if he was an adult.

Key Takeaway
The martyr in janabah is not washed according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, while a child martyr is washed.

Salah — Prayer

Validity of Prayer Inside and Atop the Kaaba
Commentary on matn stating validity of prayer inside and atop the Kaaba, with evidence and expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and atop the Kaaba and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the definition of qibla.

Core Idea
Prayer inside and atop the Kaaba is valid for both fard and nafl because the entire building is the qibla.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq that comments on the ruling for prayer inside and atop the Kaaba. The core ruling is that both obligatory and voluntary prayers are valid in these locations. The commentator provides evidence from the Prophet's action during the Conquest of Mecca and explains the underlying legal principles regarding facing the qibla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Locate the exact phrase stating the ruling: 'صح فرض ونفل فيها وفوقها' – 'Obligatory and voluntary prayer are valid inside it and atop it.'
This is the matn statement that the commentary expands.
2
Recognize the Evidence (Dalil)
The commentary cites the Prophet's practice: 'لأنه في جوف الكعبة يوم الفتح' – because he prayed inside the Kaaba on the day of the Conquest. This is a dalil from Sunnah mutawatirah (the attested practice).
The Prophet's action is a source of legislation according to Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the Condition of Facing Qibla
The validity depends on facing the qibla. The commentary clarifies that 'استيعابها ليس بشرط' – encompassing the entire qibla is not a condition. Thus, facing any part of the Kaaba suffices.
This is why prayer inside is valid: one is automatically facing the qibla.
4
Analyze the Ruling for Atop the Kaaba
The commentary extends the ruling to the roof because 'الكعبة هي العرصة والهواء إلى عنان السماء' – the Kaaba's area extends upward to the sky. An analogy (qiyas) is made to praying on Mount Abu Qubays, which is valid if no building obstructs.
This shows the Hanafi view that the direction (jihah) of the Kaaba includes the airspace above it.
5
Note the Ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i School
The commentary does not mention the ikhtilaf explicitly, but it is known that Shafi'is only validate nafl inside the Kaaba due to doubt about facing the exact qibla during fard. The Hanafi position is more permissive.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is important for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلاة في الكعبة
ختم كتاب الصلاة بما يتبرك به حالاً ومكاناً وأولاده للشهيد لأنه معدول به عن سائر الصلوات لجواز جعل الظهر فيها إلى ظهر الإمام قوله : (صح فرض ونفل فيها وفوقها) لأنه في جوف الكعبة يوم الفتح ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها لوجود استقبال القبلة لأن استيعابها ليس بشرط، وإنما جازت فوقها لأن الكعبة هي العرصة والهواء إلى عنان السماء عندنا دون البناء لأنه ينقل ألا ترى أنه لو صلى علي أبي قبيس جاز ولا بناء بين يديه
،
قوله : (فوافق في الأول) وهو ما إذا قتلوا في حال الحرب والمراد بالثاني ما إذا قتلوا بعدها.
باب الصلاة في الكعبة
(لأنه متوجه إلى القبلة زاد في النهر غير متقدم على إمامه قال : وحذفه في البحر ولا بد منه
Chapter on Prayer in the Kaaba. He concluded the Book of Prayer with what is blessed in state and place, and his children for the martyr because it is diverted from other prayers due to the permissibility of making the zuhr prayer with one's back to the imam's back inside it. His statement: (Obligatory and voluntary prayer are valid inside it and atop it) because it was in the interior of the Kaaba on the day of the Conquest, and because it is a prayer that has gathered its conditions due to the existence of facing the qibla, because encompassing the entire qibla is not a condition. And it is permitted atop it because the Kaaba is the area and the air up to the sky according to us, not the building, because it moves. Do you not see that if one prays on Mount Abu Qubays it is permissible with no building in front of him? His statement: (So he agreed in the first) which is when they were killed during war, and by the second is meant when they were killed after it. Chapter on Prayer in the Kaaba. (Because he is facing the qibla. In al-Nahr he added: not advancing ahead of his imam. He said: And he omitted it in al-Bahr, and it is necessary.)
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on prayer inside the Kaaba. It states that both fard and nafl prayers are valid when performed inside the Kaaba or on its roof. The reason given is that on the day of the Conquest of Mecca, the Prophet prayed inside the Kaaba. The validity depends on facing the qibla, but facing the exact direction is not a strict condition; facing the general direction suffices. Prayer on the roof is also valid because the Kaaba's area (al-'arsa) extends to the sky in the Hanafi school, not just the building itself. The text analogizes to prayer on Mount Abu Qubays, which is valid if no building obstructs the direction. The final lines are textual notes: Al-Nahr adds that one should not advance ahead of the imam, but Al-Bahr omits it, though it is necessary.

Key Terms
كعبة (ka'bah): The sacred house in Mecca; prayer inside or atop it is valid.
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qiblah): Facing the qibla; for prayer inside Kaaba, facing any part of the building suffices.
العرصة (al-'arsa): The area or courtyard of the Kaaba; used to extend the qibla direction to the airspace above.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it valid to perform an obligatory (fard) prayer inside the Kaaba?
A) No, only nafl prayer is valid inside.
B) Yes, both fard and nafl are valid.
C) Yes, but only if the imam leads from outside.
D) No, because the qibla cannot be determined.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates fard and nafl prayer inside and atop the Kaaba based on the Prophet's practice and the principle that facing the general direction of the qibla suffices.

Validity of Prayer Inside and On Top of the Ka'bah and Follower Positioning
Explains validity of prayer inside and atop the Ka'bah and follower positioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah, identify the four follower positions inside, and apply the condition that the follower must not be ahead of the imam.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Ka'bah and on its roof is valid; the follower must never be ahead of the imam.

This lesson examines the unique rulings for prayer in and atop the Ka'bah. The Hanafi school permits both based on the principle that facing the qibla is achieved even if not directly facing a wall. It then details the precise positioning of followers relative to the imam inside the sacred structure, with specific valid and invalid configurations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What two locations are being considered? What is the general ruling for each?
The text states that both farḍ and nafl prayers are valid inside and on top.
2
Locate the dalīl
What proof is cited for prayer inside? For atop?
Inside: the Prophet prayed inside on the day of conquest. Atop: the Ka'bah's 'arsah includes the air above.
3
Examine the follower positions inside
How many scenarios are given? What are the key conditions for validity?
Four scenarios: valid (back to back), invalid (back to face), valid but disliked (face to face), valid without dislike (face to side).
4
Analyze the circle formation (taḥlīq)
When is forming a circle around the Ka'bah valid? What determines if a follower is ahead?
Valid if the follower is not in the imam's side and not closer to the wall than the imam.
5
Note cross-madhhab insight
What do al-Ramlī and al-Durr al-Mukhtār add regarding the imam facing a corner?
They confirm the Hanafi principle: whoever is closer to the wall than the imam has an invalid prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلاة في الكعبة
صح فرض ونفل فيها وفوقها ومن جعل ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه فيها صح وإلى وجهه لا وإن تحلقوا حولها صح لمن هو أقرب إليها من أمامه إن لم يكن في جانبه. قال الشارح: لأنه في جوف الكعبة يوم الفتح ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها لوجود استقبال القبلة لأن استيعابها ليس بشرط، وإنما جازت فوقها لأن الكعبة هي العرصة والهواء إلى عنان السماء عندنا دون البناء لأنه ينقل ألا ترى أنه لو صلى على أبي قبيس جاز ولا بناء بين يديه. قوله: (ومن جعل ظهره إلى ظهر الإمام فيها صح لأنه متوجه إلى القبلة ولا يعتقد إمامه على الخطأ بخلاف مسألة التحري. قوله: (وإلى وجهه لا) أي لو جعل ظهره إلى وجه إمامه لا يصح لتقدمه على إمامه. وسكت ما إذا جعل وجهه إلى وجه الإمام لأنه صحيح لما قدمناه لكنه مكروه بلا حائل لأنه يشبه عبادة الصورة. وعما إذا جعل وجهه إلى جوانب الإمام وهو جائز بلا كراهة فهي أربعة: تصح بلا كراهة في صورتين ومعها في صورة ولا تصح في أخرى. قوله: (وإن تحلقوا حولها صح لمن هو أقرب إليها إن لم يكن في جانبه) لأنه متأخر حكماً لأن التقدم والتأخر لا يظهر إلا عند اتحاد الجهة. فمن كان وجهه إلى الجهة التي توجه الإمام إليها وهو عن يمينه أو يساره وتقدم عليه بأن كان أقرب إلى الحائط من الإمام فهو غير صحيح لتقدمه فهو في معنى من جعل ظهره إلى وجه الإمام. ولو قام الإمام في الكعبة وتحلق المقتدون حولها جاز إذا كان الباب مفتوحاً لأنه كقيامه في المحراب في غيرها من المساجد. والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
قال الرملي: رأيت في كتب الشافعية: لو توجه الإمام أو المأموم إلى الركن فكل من جانبيه جهته. وأقول: ولا شيء من قواعدنا يأباه. فلو صلى الإمام إلى الركن فكل من جانبيه جانبه فينظر إلى من عن يمينه وشماله من المقتدين فمن كان الإمام أقرب منه إلى الحائط أو بمساواته له فيحكم بصحة صلاته، وأما الذي هو أقرب منه إلى الحائط فصلاته فاسدة. وبه يتضح الحال في التحلق حول الكعبة المشرفة مع الإمام في سائر الأحوال. ونحوه في الدر المختار حيث قال: ولو وقف مسامتاً لركن في جانب الإمام وكان أقرب لم أره وينبغي الفساد احتياطاً لترجيح جهة الإمام. وهذه صورته مؤتم إمام.
Chapter: Prayer in the Ka'bah
It is valid to pray obligatory and supererogatory prayers in it and on top of it. Whoever places his back to the back of his imam inside it, his prayer is valid, but (if he places his back) to his face, it is not valid. If they form a circle around it, it is valid for the one who is closest to it if he is not in his (the imam's) direction. The commentator said: Because he (the Prophet) prayed inside the Ka'bah on the day of conquest, and because it is a prayer that fulfills all conditions due to facing the qibla, since encompassing it is not a condition. It is permitted on top because the Ka'bah is the courtyard and the air up to the sky according to us, not the building, because it moves. Do you not see that if one prays on Abu Qubais it is valid even without a building in front of him. His statement: (Whoever places his back to the back of his imam inside it is valid) because he is facing the qibla and does not consider his imam to be in error, unlike the case of taharri. His statement: (And to his face no) means if he places his back to the face of his imam, it is not valid due to being ahead of his imam. He did not mention if he places his face to the face of the imam, for it is valid as we mentioned, but disliked without a barrier because it resembles image worship. As for placing his face to the sides of the imam, it is permissible without dislike. There are four cases: valid without dislike in two, with dislike in one, and not valid in one. His statement: (If they form a circle around, it is valid for the one who is closest to it if he is not in his side) because he is virtually behind, since ahead and behind only appear when direction is unified. So whoever faces the direction the imam faces and is to his right or left and is ahead of him by being closer to the wall, his prayer is invalid due to being ahead, and he is like one who places his back to the imam's face. If the imam stands in the Ka'bah and the followers form a circle around, it is valid if the door is open, because it is like his standing in the mihrab in other mosques. And Allah knows best. Al-Ramli said: I saw in Shafi'i books: if the imam or follower faces the corner, then each side is his direction. I say: nothing in our principles forbids it. So if the imam prays towards the corner, each side is his side. He looks at those to his right and left among the followers: whoever the imam is closer to the wall than or equal, his prayer is judged valid; but whoever is closer to the wall than the imam, his prayer is invalid. This clarifies the situation of forming a circle around the Ka'bah with the imam in all conditions. Similar is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: if he stands aligned with a corner in the side of the imam and is closer, I have not seen it, and it should be invalid as a precaution to prioritize the imam's direction. This is its picture: a follower is imam?
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of prayer in the Ka'bah from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It opens with the ruling that both obligatory and supererogatory prayers are valid inside the Ka'bah and on its roof. The proof for inside is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed inside the Ka'bah on the day of conquest. For the roof, the reasoning is that the Ka'bah itself is considered the 'arsah (courtyard) and the air above it up to the sky is the same as the building, so facing the qibla is achieved. The author then addresses the follower's position relative to the imam inside the Ka'bah. There are four scenarios: (1) follower's back to imam's back: valid because both face the qibla without assuming imam is in error, unlike the case of taharri (when qibla direction is uncertain). (2) follower's back to imam's face: invalid because the follower is ahead of the imam. (3) follower's face to imam's face: valid but disliked without a barrier as it resembles image worship. (4) follower's face to imam's sides: valid without dislike. Then the ruling on forming a circle around the Ka'bah: it is valid for those who are closer to the imam if not in his side, meaning not directly facing him. The commentary explains that being behind or ahead is determined by the direction; if the follower faces the same direction as the imam but is to his side, and is closer to the wall (i.e., ahead), the prayer is invalid. The passage ends with a quotation from al-Ramli discussing a scenario where imam faces a corner of the Ka'bah, applying similar principles. Al-Ramli states that this does not contradict Hanafi principles, and the rule is that whoever is closer to the wall than the imam has an invalid prayer, while those at equal distance or behind have valid prayer. This is also supported by al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
عرصة (arsah): The courtyard or open area of the Ka'bah, considered as the qibla itself in Hanafi view.
تحلق (tahliq): Forming a circle around the Ka'bah for prayer.
تقدم (taqaddum): The follower being physically ahead of the imam in the direction of prayer, which invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a follower stands inside the Ka'bah facing the same direction as the imam but is closer to the wall (ahead), what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid because both face the qibla.
B) The prayer is invalid because the follower is ahead of the imam.
C) The prayer is valid but disliked.
D) The follower must repeat the prayer but it is valid.

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside and atop the Ka'bah is sahih; followers must not be ahead of the imam, and forming a circle is valid only if each follower is not closer to the wall than the imam.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on Prayer Inside and Around the Kaaba
Explaining validity conditions of prayer when imam is inside Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four possible positions of a follower relative to the imam inside the Kaaba and classify each as valid, invalid, or disliked.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid, but the follower's position relative to the imam determines validity: back-to-back valid, back-to-face invalid, face-to-face valid but disliked, face-to-side valid without dislike.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the detailed rulings when the imam leads prayer from inside the Kaaba. The key is understanding the concept of 'precedence' (taqaddum) and how it affects the follower's prayer. We will analyze the four scenarios and the condition of forming a circle around the Kaaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Positions
Enumerate the four combinations of the follower's body orientation relative to the imam: back-to-back, back-to-face, face-to-face, face-to-side.
The text directly names these possibilities.
2
Apply the Rule of Direction
Determine when the follower is considered 'ahead' (taqaddum) based on unified direction (jihah). The follower is ahead if closer to the qibla wall than the imam.
This invalidates the prayer.
3
Classify Each Case
Check the ruling for each position: back-to-back is valid, back-to-face is invalid due to taqaddum, face-to-face is valid but disliked without a barrier, face-to-side is valid without dislike.
The ruling is given explicitly.
4
Handle Circling Around the Kaaba
When followers form a circle, validity depends on proximity to the wall. Only those not ahead (imam closer or equal) have valid prayer.
The imam's direction unifies the circle.
5
Consider the Corner Exception
If the imam stands at a corner, Hanafis consider both sides as his direction, so followers on both sides can be behind if not closer to the wall.
Al-Ramli and al-Durr al-Mukhtar support this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز باب الصلاة في الكعبة وجهه جانبه. يصح وإن تحلقوا حولها صح لمن هو أقرب إليها من أمامه إن لم يكن في [؟] إلا أنه يكره لما فيه من ترك التعظيم وقد ورد النهي عنه وفي الغاية الكعبة هي البناء المرتفع مأخوذ من الارتفاع والنتو ومنه الكاعب فكيف يقال الكعبة هي العرصة والصواب القبلة العرصة كما ذكره صاحب المحيط والوبري وفي المجتبى وقد رفع البناء في عهد ابن الزبير ليبني على قواعد الخليل وفي عهد الحجاج كذلك ليعيدها إلى الحالة الأولى والناس هي يصلون والأحرار والعبيد والرجال والنساء في ذلك سواء قوله : (ومن جعل ظهره إلى ظهر الإمام فيها صح لأنه متوجه إلى القبلة ولا يعتقد إمامه على الخطأ بخلاف مسألة التحري قوله : (وإلى وجهه (لا أي لو جعل ظهره إلى وجه إمامه لا يصح لتقدمه على إمامه، وسكت ما إذا جعل وجهه إلى وجه الإمام لأنه صحيح لما قدمناه لكنه مكروه بلا حائل لأنه يشبه عبادة الصورة، وعما إذا جعل وجهه إلى جوانب الإمام وهو جائز بلا كراهة فهي أربعة، تصح بلا كراهة في صورتين ومعها في صورة ولا تصح في أخرى قوله : (وإن حلقوا حولها صح لمن هو أقرب إليها إن لم يكن في جانبه لأنه متأخر حكماً لأن التقدم والتأخر لا يظهر إلا عند اتحاد الجهة، فمن كان وجهه إلى الجهة التي توجه الإمام إليها وهو عن يمينة أو يساره وتقدم عليه بأن كان أقرب إلى الحائط من الإمام فهو غير صحيح لتقدمه فهو في معنى من جعل ظهره إلى وجه الإمام، ولو قام الإمام في الكعبة وتحلق المقتدون حولها جاز إذا كان الباب مفتوحاً لأنه كقيامه في المحراب في غيرها من المساجد والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب. أنه لقوله «وإلى وجهه لا» أي لا أنه تقدم عليه فالمؤثر إنما هو التقدم متوجه إلى القبلة غير يصح مع وعدمه قول المصنف : ( إن لم يكن في جانبه قال الرملي : رأيت في كتب الشافعية : لو توجه الإمام أو المأموم إلى الركن فكل من جانبيه جهته وأقول : ولا شيء من قواعدنا يأباه، فلو صلى الإمام إلى الركن فكل من جانبيه جانبه فينظر إلى من عن يمينه وشماله من المقتدين فمن كان الإمام أقرب منه إلى الحائط أو بمساواته له فيحكم بصحة صلاته، وأما الذي هو أقرب منه إلى الحائط فصلاته فاسدة وبه يتضح الحال في التحلق حول الكعبة المشرفة مع الإمام في سائر الأحوال ا هـ. ونحوه في الدار المختار حيث قال : ولو وقف مسامتاً لركن في جانب الإمام وكان أقرب لم أره وينبغي الفساد احتياطاً لترجيح جهة الإمام وهذه صورته مؤتم إمام .
Book of Funerals, Chapter of Prayer in the Kaaba. Its side. It is valid. If they form a circle around it, it is valid for the one closest to it from his front if not in [his direction?], except that it is disliked because it involves lack of reverence and the prohibition has been reported. In al-Ghayah: the Kaaba is the elevated building, derived from height and protrusion, and from it comes al-ka'ab (breast). So how can it be said the Kaaba is the courtyard? The correct is that the qibla is the courtyard as mentioned by the author of al-Muhit and al-Webari. In al-Mujtaba: the building was raised in the time of Ibn al-Zubayr to build on the foundations of al-Khalil, and in the time of al-Hajjaj as well to return it to the first state, and people pray there; free men and slaves, men and women are equal in that. His statement: (And whoever places his back to the imam's back inside it, it is valid because he is facing the qibla and does not consider his imam to be in error, unlike the case of ijtihad. His statement: (And to his face (no) means if he places his back to his imam's face, it is not valid because he is ahead of his imam. He remained silent about when he places his face to his imam's face because it is valid as we have stated, but it is disliked without a barrier because it resembles worshipping an image. As for when he places his face to the sides of the imam, it is permissible without dislike. So there are four cases: valid without dislike in two, with dislike in one, and not valid in another. His statement: (And if they form a circle around it, it is valid for the one closest to it if he is not on his side because he is legally behind, since precedence and being behind only become apparent when the direction is unified. So whoever faces the direction the imam is facing and is on his right or left and is ahead of him by being closer to the wall than the imam, his prayer is invalid due to his precedence, and he is in the same case as one who places his back to the imam's face. And if the imam stands inside the Kaaba and the followers form a circle around it, it is permissible if the door is open, because it is like his standing in the mihrab in other mosques. And Allah knows best and to Him is the return. That is because of his saying 'and to his face no' meaning not that he is ahead of him; the effective factor is only being ahead facing the qibla, not valid with or without it. The author's statement: (if he is not on his side). Al-Ramli said: I saw in the books of the Shafi'is: if the imam or the follower faces the corner, then each of his sides is his direction. I say: nothing in our principles prevents it. So if the imam prays facing the corner, then each of his sides is his side, so we look at those to his right and left among the followers: the one whom the imam is closer to the wall than or equal to, we rule the validity of his prayer. As for the one who is closer to the wall than the imam, his prayer is invalid. And by this the situation becomes clear regarding forming a circle around the noble Kaaba with the imam in all circumstances. And similar is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar where he said: If he stands aligned to a corner on the imam's side and is closer, I have not seen it, and it should be invalid as a precaution to give weight to the imam's direction. And this is its form: a follower with an imam.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the rulings of prayer when the imam is inside the Kaaba. The commentary expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It first clarifies that the Kaaba is the building itself, not the courtyard, and that praying inside it is valid for all people equally. The core ruling: if a follower places his back to the imam's back, his prayer is valid because he is facing the qibla. If he places his back to the imam's face, it is invalid due to being ahead. Facing the imam's face is valid but disliked without a barrier; facing his sides is valid without dislike. When followers form a circle around the Kaaba, validity depends on proximity: if a follower is closer to the wall than the imam, his prayer is invalid because he is effectively ahead. The commentator then quotes al-Ramli and al-Durr al-Mukhtar to handle the case when the imam stands at a corner, explaining that followers on both sides are considered behind if the imam is closer to the wall or equal.

Key Terms
التحليق (al-tahalluq): Forming a circle around the Kaaba by the followers.
التقدم (al-taqaddum): The follower being physically closer to the qibla wall than the imam, which invalidates prayer.
الجهة (al-jihah): The direction the imam is facing; when unified, precedence can be determined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower inside the Kaaba places his back to the imam's back, what is the ruling?
A) Valid because he is facing the qibla
B) Invalid because he is ahead of the imam
C) Valid but disliked
D) Invalid unless there is a barrier

Key Takeaway
When praying inside the Kaaba, the follower's prayer is valid unless he is physically ahead of the imam relative to the qibla wall.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling and Conditions of I'tikaf in the Hanafi School
Explains the legal classification, elements, and conditions of i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'tikaf (Sunnah mu'akkadah in last ten days, mustahabb otherwise, wajib by vow) and identify its conditions (place, intention, fasting conditionality).

Core Idea
I'tikaf is Sunnah mu'akkadah in Ramadan's last ten days; fasting is a condition only for vowed i'tikaf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the legal classification and conditions of i'tikaf (spiritual retreat) according to the Hanafi school. It clarifies the three levels of ruling—Sunnah mu'akkadah, mustahabb, and wajib—and addresses the disputed issue of fasting as a condition. The commentator resolves the apparent tension between the Prophet's continuous practice and his one abandonment, establishing the preferred view that fasting is required only for vowed i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of i'tikaf
The passage divides i'tikaf into wajib (by vow), Sunnah mu'akkadah (last ten days of Ramadan), and mustahabb (other times). Note the evidence from the Prophet's continuous practice and lack of disapproval.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is stronger than mustahabb; the dispute with al-Quduri is about this classification.
2
Determine the condition of fasting
Fasting is a condition only for vowed i'tikaf. For nafl (including Sunnah i'tikaf of last ten days), it is customary but not a strict condition; if performed without fasting due to excuse, some consider it valid. The minimum for nafl is one hour.
This resolves the apparent contradiction in the passage mentioning fasting alongside the ruling.
3
Recognize the pillar and other conditions
The pillar (rukn) is staying (lubth) in the mosque. Conditions include intention (niyyah) and place: men in a mosque, women in a designated prayer space at home. The passage also implies that menstruation and postnatal bleeding are preventers for vowed i'tikaf.
Intention is distinct from the general fasting intention; it must be specifically for i'tikaf.
4
Analyze the evidence for the ruling
The Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) in the last ten days, never leaving it without excuse, proves it is Sunnah mu'akkadah. His one abandonment was due to anger and was later made up, so it does not lower the rank.
This dalil is from the Sahihayn, establishing strong transmission.
5
Apply the ruling to vow scenarios
The passage discusses examples: vowing i'tikaf for a night alone is invalid because fasting is a condition (night is not for fasting). Vowing for a night and day together is valid because the day is primary. Also, if one vows i'tikaf of a day after already eating, it is invalid.
These applications show the practical implications of the fasting condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم/ باب الاعتكاف
سن لبث في مسجد بصوم ونية وأقله نفلاً ساعة والمرأة تعتكف في مسجد بيتها
صفته فالسنية كما ذكره على كلام فيه يأتي، وأما سببه فالنذر إن كان واجباً والنشاط الداعي إلى طلب الثواب إن كان تطوعاً، وأما حكمه فسقوط الواجب ونيل الثواب إن كان واجباً، والثاني فقط إن كان نفلاً وسيأتي ما يفسده ويكره فيه ويحرم ويندب ومحاسنه كثيرة لأن فيه تفريغ القلب عن أمور الدنيا وتسليم النفس إلى المولى والتحصن بحصن حصين وملازمة بيت رب كريم فهو كمن احتاج إلى عظيم فلازمه حتى قضى مآربه فهو يلازم بيت ربه ليغفر له . كذا في الكافي. وفي الاختيار : وهو من أشرف الأعمال إذا كان عن إخلاص.
قوله : (سن لبث في مسجد بصوم ونية أي ونية اللبث الذي هو الاعتكاف . وقد أشار المصنف إلى صفته وركنه وشرائطه. أما الأول فهو السنية وهكذا في كثير من الكتب، وهي القدوري الاعتكاف مستحب، وصحح في الهداية أنه سنة مؤكدة، وذكر الشارح أن الحق انتسامه إلى ثلاثة أقسام: واجب وهو المنذور، وسنة وهو في العشر الأخير من رمضان، ومستحب وهو في غيره من الأزمنة. وتبعه المحقق في فتح القدير، والأظهر أنه سنة في الأصل كما اقتصر عليه في المتن تبعاً لما صرح به في البدائع وهي مؤكدة وغير مؤكدة. وأطلق عليها الاستحباب لأنها بمعناه، وأما الواجب فهو بعارض النذر. وفي البدائع إنه يجب بالشروع أيضاً، ولا يخفى أنه مفرع على ضعيف وهو اشتراط زمن للتطوع، وأما على المذهب من أن أقل النفل ساعة ،فلا والدليل على تأكده في العشر الأخير مواظبته عليه السلام عليه فيه كما في الصحيحين ولهذا قال الزهري : عجباً للناس كيف تركوا الاعتكاف وقد كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعل الشيء ويتركه ولم يترك الاعتكاف منذ دخل المدينة إلى أن مات. فهذه المواظبة المقرونة بعدم الترك مرة لما اقترنت بعدم الإنكار على من لم يفعله من الصحابة كانت دليل السنية وإلا كانت دليل الوجوب كذا في فتح القدير ولا يخفى أن المواظبة قد اقترنت فيه عن الحيض والنفاس على رواية اشتراط الصوم في نفله، أما على عدمه فينبغي أن يكون من شرائط الحل فقط كالطهارة عن الجنابة قال : ولم أر من تعرض لهذا ا هـ. والحاصل أنه ينبغي أن تشترط للصحة الطهارة عن الحيض والنفاس في المنذور لأن الصوم لا يكون معهما، وكذلك في النفل على رواية اشتراط الصوم فيه وأما على عدمه فينبغي اشتراطها للحل لا للصحة كما لا تشترط الطهارة من الجنابة لشيء من المنذور وغيره كما في الإمداد أي للصحة أما للحل فينبغي اشتراطها كما ذكره المؤلف قوله : (كالصوم) فيه أن الصوم شرط للصحة لا الحل وهذا في المنذور والنفل عل رواية، أما على ظاهر الرواية فليس بشرط أصلاً وإن أراد أن الطهارة من الجنابة شرط لحل الصوم ففيه نظر تأمل قوله : (وأطلق عليه الاستحباب الخ) قال في النهر : هو ظاهر في أن القدوري أطلق اسم الاستحباب على المؤيدة وغيرها لأنها بمعناه لكن لا يخفى ما في إطلاق المستحب على المؤكدة من المؤاخذة فالأقرب أن يقال : إنه اقتصر على نوع منه وهو غير المؤكدة وكلام المصنف لا غبار عليه
بالترك وهو ما يفيده الحديث من أنه اعتكف العشر الأخير من رمضان فرأى خياماً وقباباً مضروبة فقال : لمن هذا؟ قال : لعائشة وهذا الحفصة وهذا السودة فغضب وقال : أترون البر بهذا فأمر بأن تنزع قبته فنزعت ولم يعتكف فيه ثم قضي في شوال. وقد يقال: إن الترك هنا لعذر كما صرح به في الفتاوى الظهيرية، وقد قدمنا في المواظبة كلاماً حسناً في سنن الوضوء فارجع إليه. ولا فرق في المنذور بين المنجز والمعلق. وأشار باللبث إلى ركنه، وبالمسجد والصوم والنية إلى شرائطه لكن ذكره الصوم معها لا ينبغي لأنه لا يمكن حمله على المنذور لتصريحه بالسنية، ولا على غيره لتصريحه بعد أن أقله نفلاً ساعة فلزم أن الصوم ليس من شرطه. فإن قلت يمكن حمله على الاعتكاف المسنون سنة مؤكدة وهو العشر الأخير من رمضان فإن الصوم من شرطه حتى لو اعتكفه من غير صوم لمرض أو سفر ينبغي أن لا يصح . قلت : لا يمكن لتصريحهم بأن الصوم إنما هو شرط في المنذور فقط دون غيره، وفرعوا عليه بأنه لو نذر اعتكاف ليلة لم يصح لأن الصوم من شرطه والليل ليس بمحل له، ولو نوى اليوم معها لم يصح . كذا في الظهيرية عن أبي يوسف : إن نوى ليلة بيومها لزمه ولم يذكر محمد هذا التفصيل. ولو قال الله علي أن أعتكف ليلاً ونهاراً لزمه أن يعتكف ليلاً ونهاراً وإن لم يكن الليل محلاً للصوم لأن الليل يدخل فيه تبعاً، ولا يشترط للتبع ما يشترط للأصل ولو نذر اعتكاف يوم قد أكل فيه لم يصح ولم يلزمه شيء لأنه لا يصح بدون الصوم، وسيأتي بقية تفاريع النذر. ومن تفريعاته هنا أنه لو أصبح صائماً متطوعاً أو غيرنا وللصوم ثم قال الله علي أن أعتكف هذا اليوم لا يصح وإن كان في وقت تصح فيه نية الصوم لعدم استيفاء النهار، وتمامه في فتح القدير : وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية ولو قال لله علي أن أعتكف لأن المشكك حقيقة في أفراده ا هـ . وقد يقال : ما جعله الأقرب هو مراد المؤلف بإرجاع ضمير عليها لأقرب مذكور هو غير المؤكدة كما أفاده الشيخ إسماعيل .
بالنسبة
قوله : (التصريحهم بأن الصوم إنما هو شرط في المنذور) قلت : تصريحهم بذلك إنما هو : إلى النفل يعني أنه ليس بشرط في النفل لأنه المحتاج إلى البيان أما المسنون فلا يكون إلا بالصوم عادة فلا حاجة إلى التنبيه عليه وإمكان تصور عدم الصوم فيه لمرض أو سفر نادر جداً، ويدل على ما قلنا أنه في متن الدرر قسم الاعتكاف إلى الأقسام الثلاثة ثم قال : والصوم شرط لصحة الأول يعني الواجب لا الثالث يعني المستحب ولم يتعرض للثاني، وهو المسنون بنفي ولا إثبات للعلم بأنه لا يكون بدون صوم عادة، وسيأتي قريباً بيان اختلاف الرواية في وجوب الصوم في الاعتكاف النفل بناء على اختلاف الرواية في أنه مقدر بيوم أم لا، ومقتضاه أن التقدير مستلزم لإيجاب الصوم فيه، ولا يخفى أن اعتكاف العشر الأخير مقدر فيكون الصوم شرطاً فيه فتأمل قوله : (ولو نوى اليوم معها لم يصح) قال الرملي : سيأتي الكلام على ذلك في شرح قوله وليلتان بنذر يومين» فراجعه تأمل
Book of Fasting / Chapter of I'tikaf. It is Sunnah to stay in a mosque with fasting and intention, and its minimum as Nafl is one hour, and a woman performs I'tikaf in the mosque of her house. Its description: it is Sunnah as he mentioned, with some discussion to come. As for its cause, it is a vow if obligatory, and the enthusiasm leading to seeking reward if voluntary. And as for its ruling, it is the dropping of obligation and attainment of reward if obligatory, and only the second if nafl. And what invalidates it, what is disliked in it, what is forbidden, and what is recommended will come. And its merits are many because it empties the heart from worldly matters and surrenders the soul to the Lord and fortifies with a strong fortress and adhering to the house of a generous Lord. So it is like one who needs a great person and stays with him until he fulfills his needs, so he adheres to his Lord's house so that He may forgive him. Thus in al-Kafi. And in al-Ikhtiyar: It is among the noblest deeds if done with sincerity. His statement: (Sunnah is staying in a mosque with fasting and intention), meaning intention of staying which is i'tikaf. The author has indicated its description, its pillar, and its conditions. As for the first, it is the Sunnah and thus in many books, and al-Quduri said i'tikaf is mustahabb, and it is corrected in al-Hidayah that it is Sunnah mu'akkadah. The commentator mentioned that the correct view is that it divides into three categories: obligatory (vowed), Sunnah (in the last ten days of Ramadan), and mustahabb (at other times). The investigator in Fath al-Qadir followed him, and the most apparent is that it is Sunnah in principle as confined in the matn following what was stated in al-Bada'i'—it is mu'akkadah and non-mu'akkadah. And he applied the term 'mustahabb' to it because it is in its meaning. As for obligatory, it is due to the contingency of a vow. In al-Bada'i': It becomes obligatory also by commencing, and it is not hidden that this is based on a weak view which requires a specific time for voluntary i'tikaf; whereas according to the established school that the minimum of nafl is one hour, it is not. And the evidence for its emphasis in the last ten days is his continuous practice عليه السلام upon it in them as in the Sahihayn. Hence al-Zuhri said: I marvel at people how they abandoned i'tikaf while the Messenger of Allah صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ used to do a thing and leave it, but he never left i'tikaf from the time he entered Medina until he died. This continuous practice combined with never leaving it, when coupled with the lack of disapproval of those who did not do it among the Companions, is evidence of it being Sunnah; otherwise it would be evidence of obligation. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, and it is not hidden that the continuous practice was combined with leaving it in what the hadith conveys: that he observed i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan and saw tents and domes erected and asked: 'Whose are these?' They said: 'Aisha's, Hafsah's, and Sawdah's.' He became angry and said: 'Do you consider piety this?' He ordered that his tent be pulled down, so it was pulled down, and he did not perform i'tikaf then, but later made it up in Shawwal. It may be said that the abandonment here was due to an excuse, as stated in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah. And we have previously presented good discussion on continuous practice in the Sunnah of Wudu', so refer to it. And there is no difference in the vowed i'tikaf between the absolute and conditional. And he indicated by 'staying' its pillar, and by 'mosque', 'fasting', and 'intention' its conditions. But his mentioning fasting with them is not appropriate because it cannot be construed as referring to the vowed, due to his explicit statement of Sunnah, nor to others due to his explicit statement that its minimum as nafl is one hour, so it necessarily follows that fasting is not a condition for it. If you say: It can be construed as referring to the Sunnah i'tikaf which is Sunnah mu'akkadah, namely the last ten days of Ramadan, for fasting is a condition of it such that if one performs i'tikaf without fasting due to illness or travel, it should not be valid. I say: It cannot, because of their explicit statements that fasting is only a condition in the vowed i'tikaf, not others. And they derived from this that if one vows to observe i'tikaf for a night, it is not valid because fasting is a condition and the night is not a place for it. And if he intends the day with it, it is not valid. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah from Abu Yusuf: If he intends a night with its day, it becomes binding; Muhammad did not mention this detail. And if he says: 'By Allah I must observe i'tikaf for a night and a day,' it becomes binding on him to observe i'tikaf for a night and a day, even though the night is not a place for fasting, because the night is included subordinately, and what is required for the subordinate is not required for the principal. And if he vows i'tikaf of a day in which he has eaten, it is not valid and nothing is binding on him, because it is not valid without fasting. The rest of the derivations of vows will come. Among the derivations here: If he wakes up fasting voluntarily or otherwise and then says: 'By Allah I must observe i'tikaf this day,' it is not valid even if it is a time when the intention of fasting is valid, due to not completing the day. Its completion is in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If he says 'By Allah I must observe i'tikaf' because the doubted thing is reality in its individuals. It may be said that what he considered closest is the intention of the author by referring the pronoun to the nearest mentioned, which is the non-mu'akkadah, as indicated by Shaykh Isma'il. With respect to his statement: (Their explicit statement that fasting is only a condition in the vowed) I say: Their explicit statement of that is only regarding nafl, meaning it is not a condition in nafl because it is that which requires clarification; as for the Sunnah, it only occurs with fasting customarily, so there is no need to draw attention to it, and the possibility of imagining i'tikaf without fasting due to illness or travel is very rare. And what indicates what we say is that in the text of al-Durar he divided i'tikaf into three categories and then said: 'Fasting is a condition for the validity of the first (obligatory), not the third (mustahabb),' and he did not address the second (Sunnah), neither negating nor affirming, because it is known that it does not occur without fasting customarily. And soon will come the explanation of the differing reports about the obligation of fasting in nafl i'tikaf based on the difference of reports about whether it is limited to a day or not. And the implication is that limitation necessitates the obligation of fasting in it, and it is not hidden that i'tikaf of the last ten days is limited, so fasting is a condition in it. So reflect on his statement: (If he intends the day with it, it is not valid). Al-Ramli said: Discussion on that will come in the explanation of his statement 'two nights with a vow of two days', so refer to it. Reflect.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, defining the ruling and conditions of i'tikaf. The author begins by stating the basic ruling: it is Sunnah to stay in a mosque with fasting and intention, with the minimum for voluntary i'tikaf being one hour. Women perform i'tikaf in the mosque of their house (i.e., a designated prayer space at home). The description (sifah) of i'tikaf is that it is Sunnah, but there is a debate about its exact classification. The passage clarifies that i'tikaf is divided into three categories: wajib (by vow), Sunnah mu'akkadah (in the last ten days of Ramadan), and mustahabb (at other times). The author supports the view that i'tikaf is essentially Sunnah, as in al-Bada'i', but emphasizes that in the last ten days it is Sunnah mu'akkadah due to the Prophet's continuous practice. The condition of fasting is a point of discussion: it is a condition only for vowed i'tikaf, not for voluntary i'tikaf. However, the Sunnah i'tikaf of the last ten days customarily includes fasting, and if one performs it without fasting due to an excuse, it may be invalid according to some, but the author indicates that this is not a strict condition because the minimum is one hour. The passage also addresses the issue when a vow is made for i'tikaf during a night or a day already eaten, and related rulings. The overall aim is to delineate the precise legal boundaries of i'tikaf as practiced in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): To stay in a mosque for devotion with specific conditions, including intention and for some, fasting.
السنية (al-sunniyyah): The characteristic of being Sunnah (recommended, emphasized practice of the Prophet).
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow, making a practice obligatory upon oneself by saying 'for Allah I must...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is the minimum duration for a nafl (voluntary) i'tikaf?
A) One day and one night
B) One hour
C) The entire last ten days of Ramadan
D) There is no minimum

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is Sunnah mu'akkadah in the last ten days of Ramadan, mustahabb otherwise, and wajib by vow; fasting is a condition only for vowed i'tikaf.

Minimum Duration and Condition of Fasting for Supererogatory I'tikaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum duration and fasting condition for supererogatory i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum duration of supererogatory i'tikaf according to Zahir al-Riwayah, explain why fasting is not a condition, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority and Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Core Idea
Supererogatory i'tikaf has no fixed minimum: any moment suffices, and fasting is not required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two key questions about supererogatory i'tikaf: how short can it be, and must one be fasting? Using Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl as a foundation, the author defends the majority Hanafi view that any duration (even a moment) is valid and that fasting is not a condition. The passage also engages with an objection from the investigator of Fath al-Qadir, showing how later scholars resolved the tension between rational possibility and authoritative transmission.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah
Identify the ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl: entering the mosque with intention makes one a mu'takif for as long as one stays. Conclude that the minimum is any portion of time (saa'ah) and fasting is not required.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the derivation from al-Asl
The early scholars (mashayikh) derived that fasting is not a condition because supererogatory acts are treated leniently (e.g., prayer sitting/riding). Also, supererogatory i'tikaf is not limited in duration, whereas a fast must be a full day, making it incompatible as a condition.
The derivation is based on the principle that supererogatory acts are based on leniency (mubah al-nafl).
3
Examine the objection from Fath al-Qadir
Al-Marghinani objected that rationally, it is possible to require fasting even for a short i'tikaf; the condition could be longer than the conditioned. Understand the logical point but note the author's response.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq responds that the objection, while logically sound, does not undermine the transmitted ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah) and its supporting proofs.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi variant
Note that Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that fasting is a condition. This difference stems from whether supererogatory i'tikaf is considered limited to a day or not. Imam Muhammad's original text indicates it is not limited, so fasting cannot be a condition.
The mufta bihi (operative view) is the majority position without fasting.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: if someone intends i'tikaf for a short time without fasting, it is valid per the majority, but invalid according to Hasan's riwayah. In practice, the majority position is followed.
This shows how a difference in usul leads to a difference in fatwa.

Source Text

His statement: (Its minimum supererogatorily is one hour because Muhammad said in al-Asl: If he enters the mosque with the intention of i'tikaf, he is a mu'takif as long as he stays, leaving it when he leaves) so it was the apparent transmission. The scholars derived from it that fasting is not a condition according to the apparent transmission because supererogatory acts are based on leniency, such that his prayer sitting or riding while able to mount and dismount is permissible. The investigator in Fath al-Qadir objected to it saying: It is not rationally impossible to say that i'tikaf of an hour is valid while requiring fasting for it, even though fasting cannot be less than a day... (Translation continues as per arabic_clean)
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the minimum duration of supererogatory i'tikaf and the condition of fasting. It begins by stating the ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl: entering a mosque with the intention of i'tikaf makes one a mu'takif for as long as one stays, so the minimum is any moment (saa'ah). From this, the early scholars (mashayikh) derived that fasting is not a condition for supererogatory i'tikaf, because supererogatory acts are treated leniently—e.g., one may pray sitting or riding even if able to stand. Al-Marghinani (in Fath al-Qadir) objects to this derivation, arguing that rationally there is no contradiction in requiring fasting even for an hour's i'tikaf, since the condition could be longer than the conditioned. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq defends the derivation, citing many authoritative works (al-Mabsut, Sharh al-Tahawi, Fatawa Qadikhan, etc.) that all affirm that in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), fasting is not a condition. The passage then notes that Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that fasting is a condition, and this difference stems from whether supererogatory i'tikaf is considered limited to a day or not. Imam Muhammad's original statement indicates it is not limited, so fasting (which is limited to a day) cannot be a condition. The passage also clarifies that the term 'saa'ah' in fiqh means any portion of time, not a specific astronomical hour.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Seclusion in a mosque for worship with specific intention.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent and well-known transmission from Abu Hanifa through his students, found in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
الساعة (al-saa'ah): A portion of time, not limited to a specific measured hour; interpreted broadly in fiqh as any duration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the minimum duration for supererogatory i'tikaf?
A) One day
B) One hour (saa'ah)
C) Ten days
D) It must include a full day and night

Key Takeaway
Supererogatory i'tikaf is valid for any duration, and fasting is not a condition according to the well-known transmission of the Hanafi school.

Permissible Exits from I'tikaf: Religious and Natural Needs
States the exceptional exits allowed during i'tikaf with proof and details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible reasons for exiting i'tikaf and explain the Hanafi definition of 'sā'ah' (hour).

Core Idea
Leave i'tikaf only for genuine need; 'hour' is flexible, not astronomical.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on exiting the mosque during i'tikaf. The default is that one must remain inside. However, the law recognises unavoidable human needs, both religious (e.g., Friday prayer) and natural (e.g., answering the call of nature). The passage clarifies that the duration allowed is a flexible 'hour' (sā'ah) according to jurists, not the fixed hour of astronomers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Recognise that the default ruling for a person in obligatory i'tikaf is that they must not leave the mosque.
2
Note the exceptions
Identify the two categories of permissible exit: religious needs (like Friday prayer) and natural needs (like urination/defecation).
3
Examine the evidence
The proof is the hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) that the Prophet ﷺ would not leave i'tikaf except for human need.
The hadith is ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut.
4
Understand the temporal limit
The passage states that the duration of exit is 'an hour' (sā'ah), which jurists define as a flexible period, not bound by astronomical precision.
This is a Hanafi position; other schools may vary.
5
Recognise the separate discussion on fasting
The passage also touches on whether fasting is a condition for voluntary i'tikaf, but this is a distinct issue not affecting the main ruling on exits.
In the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), fasting is not a condition for voluntary i'tikaf.

Source Text

He does not leave it except for a religious need like Friday prayer or a natural need like urination and defecation. If he leaves for an hour without i'tikaf… and he corrected and others, and all declare that in the apparent transmission fasting is not a condition…
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage states the general ruling that a person in obligatory i'tikaf must not leave the mosque except for a legitimate need: a religious necessity (e.g., Friday prayer) or a natural one (e.g., answering the call of nature). The proof is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet ﷺ would not leave his i'tikaf except for human need. The text then discusses the definition of 'an hour' (sā'ah) for jurists, which is a flexible period of time, not strictly fifteen degrees as astronomers hold. The author also introduces the intra-Hanafi dispute about whether fasting is a condition for voluntary i'tikaf, but this is a separate issue.

Key Terms
ساعة (sā'ah): A flexible period of time, not precisely defined; the jurists use it for a short, indeterminate duration.
حاجة شرعية (hājah shar'iyyah): A religiously recognized necessity, such as attending Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
