Fasting and Voluntary I'tikaf: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fasting condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on fasting for voluntary i'tikaf and explain the basis of the intra-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
Voluntary i'tikaf does not require fasting; a contrary transmission is weak because it contradicts the nature of an unlimited act.

This lesson examines a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school: must a person be fasting for a voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf to be valid? The authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah says no, while Hasan ibn Ziyad transmitted the opposite. Understanding the rationale behind each view reveals how Hanafi jurists handle conflicting transmissions and the role of conceptual analysis (ta'lil) in resolving them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine the exact legal issue: is fasting a condition (shart) for the validity of voluntary i'tikaf?
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Summarize the majority view: fasting is not a condition. Cite the source: Imam Muhammad's al-Asl.
3
Present the opposing view
State Hasan ibn Ziyad's position: fasting is a condition. Recognize this as a rare transmission (nawadir).
4
Analyze the basis of disagreement
Examine the ta'lil: voluntary i'tikaf is not limited (ghayr muqaddar) in duration; fasting applies only to a full day; therefore fasting cannot be a condition for something that may be shorter.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
Confirm that the majority view is operative; explain what this means for someone performing i'tikaf without fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتکاف وصحح وغيرهم، والكل مصرحون بأن ظاهر الرواية أن الصوم ليس من شرطه لكن وقع لصاحب المبسوط أنه قال : وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز النفل من الاعتكاف من غير صوم فإنه قال في الكتاب : إذا دخل المسجد بنية الاعتكاف فهو معتكف ما أقام تارك له إذا خرج، وظاهره أن مستند ظاهر الرواية ما ذكره في الكتاب. ولا يمتنع أن يكون مستنده صريحاً آخر بل هو الظاهر لنقل الثقات وعبارة البدائع وأما اعتكاف التطوع فالصوم ليس بشرط لجوازه في ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن أنه شرط واختلاف الرواية فيه مبني على اختلاف الرواية في أنه التطوع مقدر بيوم أو غير مقدر ذكر محمد في الأصل أنه غير مقدر فلم يكن الصوم شرطاً لأن الصوم مقدر بيوم إذ صوم بعض اليوم ليس بمشروع فلا يصلح شرطاً لما ليس بمقدر ا هـ وهي تفيد أن ظاهر الرواية مروي لا مستنبط وأشار إلى أنه لو شرع في النفل ثم قطعه لا يلزمه القضاء في ظاهر الرواية لأنه غير مقدر فلم يكن قطعه إبطالاً
I'tikaf… and he corrected and others, and all declare that in the apparent transmission fasting is not a condition thereof, but it occurred from the author of al-Mabsut that he said: In the apparent transmission voluntary i'tikaf is permissible without fasting…
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether fasting is a prerequisite for voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf. The reliable position (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that fasting is not required. This is supported by Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl that voluntary i'tikaf is not limited to a specific duration; since fasting is only valid for a full day, it cannot be a condition for an act that may be shorter than a day. A conflicting transmission from Hasan ibn Ziyad states that fasting is a condition. The basis of the difference lies in whether voluntary i'tikaf is considered to have a minimum duration (a day) or not. The text also notes that if one begins a voluntary i'tikaf and then abandons it, he does not need to make it up, because it is not a measured act (muqaddar).

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent or transmitted body of rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books, which carry the highest authority.
مقدر (muqaddar): Having a fixed measure (e.g., amount, time). Here, voluntary i'tikaf is 'ghayr muqaddar' (not limited to a specific time like a day).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reliable Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the ruling on a person performing voluntary i'tikaf without fasting?
A) It is invalid because fasting is a condition.
B) It is valid because fasting is not a condition for voluntary i'tikaf.
C) It is valid only if he intends to fast later.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary i'tikaf is valid without fasting because it is not a measured act (ghayr muqaddar), unlike obligatory i'tikaf.

Validity of I'tikaf in Mosques with Congregation
The commentator expands on the validity conditions of i'tikaf and the preferred mosques.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid i'tikaf and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding which mosque qualifies.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is valid in any mosque with congregation, but the exact definition is debated among Hanafi imams.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator discusses the validity of i'tikaf across different mosques. While the matn used an absolute term 'the mosque', the commentary clarifies that certain conditions must be met. The dominant view requires that the mosque has an imam and mu'adhdhin and that the five daily prayers are performed in congregation. However, there is a well-known dispute within the Hanafi school about whether only jami' mosques qualify or any mosque with congregation. This lesson unpacks the conditions and the differing positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
From the majority Hanafi view, what is the minimum requirement for a mosque to be valid for i'tikaf?
Look for 'adhan and iqamah' or 'congregational prayers'.
2
Understand the absolute statement
The matn says 'in the mosque' (absolute); how is this qualified by the commentators?
The verse 'while you are staying in the mosques' is general but the practice restricts it.
3
Distinguish between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
What is the difference in their conditions for obligatory vs. voluntary i'tikaf?
Abu Yusuf restricts the condition of congregation to obligatory i'tikaf.
4
Apply the mufta bihi view
According to al-Tahawi and al-Ramli, what is the easiest position for our time?
They adopt the view that any mosque with congregation suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في المسجد فأفاد أن الاعتكاف يصح في كل مسجد وصححه في غاية البيان لإطلاق قوله تعالى وأنتم عاكفون في المساجد) [البقرة: ۱۸۷] قاضيخان في فتاواه أنه يصح في كل مسجد له أذان وإقامة . واختار في الهداية أنه يصح إلا في مسجد الجماعة، وعن أبي يوسف تخصيصه بالواجب أما في النفل فيجوز في غير مسجد الجماعة. ذكره في النهاية وصحح في فتح القدير عن بعض المشايخ ما روي عن أبي حنيفة أن كل مسجد له إمام ومؤذن معلوم ويصلى فيه الخمس بالجماعة يصح الاعتكاف فيه. وفي الكافي : أراد به أبو حنيفة غير الجامع فإن الجامع يجوز الاعتكاف فيه وإن لم يصلوا فيه الصلوات كلها ويوافقه ما في غاية البيان عن الفتاوى: يجوز الاعتكاف في الجامع وإن لم يصلوا فيه بالجماعة. وهذا كله لبيان الصحة وأما الأفضل فأن يكون في المسجد الحرام ثم في مسجد المدينة وهو مسجد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ثم مسجد بيت المقدس، ثم مسجد الجامع ثم المساجد العظام التي كثر أهلها كذا في البدائع وشرح الطحاوي. وظاهره أن المجاورة بمكة ليس بمكروه والمروي عن أبي حنيفة الكراهة وعلى قولهما لا بأس به فتدبر قوله : (وأطلق في المسجد الخ كان الأولى ذكره قبل قوله وأقله نفلاً ساعة»، وقوله «فأفاد أن الاعتكاف الخ قال في النهر فيه نظر ففي الخلاصة والخانية ويصح في كل مسجد له أذان وإقامة هو الصحيح وهذا هو مسجد الجماعة كما في العناية ونقل بعضهم أن صحته في كل مسجد قولهما: وهذا الكتاب لم يوضع إلا لبيان أقوال الإمام نعم اختار الطحاوي قولهما ! الرملي : ما اختاره الطحاوي أيسر خصوصاً في زماننا فينبغي أن يعول عليه والله تعالى أعلم. قوله : (وظاهره أن المجاورة بمكة غير مكروهة الخ) قال في النهر : لا يخفى أنه لا دلالة في الكلام على ما ادعى، أما أولاً فلأنه لا يلزم من الاعتكاف في غير أيام الموسم المجاورة بل قد يكون خالياً عنها فيمن كان حول مكة، وأما ثانياً فلأنه لا يلزم أيضاً من كراهة المجاورة كون اعتكافه في المسجد ليس أفضل، ألا ترى إلى أن الصلوات ونحوها من المجاور أفضل من غيرها اهـ. واستظهره الشيخ إسماعيل قوله : (وهو مكروه) أي تنزيهاً كما هو ظاهر قوله قبله أفضل وهو ظاهر كلام البدائع آت
And he made absolute in the mosque, so it indicates that i'tikaf is valid in every mosque, and he corrected it in Ghayat al-Bayan due to the generality of His statement 'while you are staying in the mosques'...
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of i'tikaf in different types of mosques. The author of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) apparently used an absolute term 'the mosque', so the commentator clarifies that i'tikaf is valid in any mosque, but there are conditions. The reliable position is that i'tikaf is valid in any mosque where the call to prayer (adhan) and the congregational prayer (iqamah) are held, i.e., a mosque that is regularly used for prayers. Some opinions restrict this to jami' mosques (Friday mosque), but the easier view (especially for our time) is that i'tikaf is valid in any mosque where prayer is performed in congregation, as chosen by al-Tahawi and al-Ramli. The passage ends by noting that living near the Kaaba (mujawara) is not disliked, though Abu Hanifa held it to be makruh; the Sahibayn have no problem with it.

Key Terms
مسجد الجماعة (masjid al-jama'ah): A mosque where the five daily prayers are performed in congregation, as opposed to a jami' (Friday) mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position for modern times, in which mosques is i'tikaf valid?
A) Only in the three holy mosques (Makkah, Madinah, al-Aqsa).
B) Only in the Friday mosque (jami').
C) In any mosque where the adhan and iqamah are performed for the daily prayers.
D) In any mosque, regardless of whether prayers are held there.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is valid in any mosque where the adhan and iqamah are established for the five daily prayers, with the easiest position being that of al-Tahawi and al-Ramli.

The Best Mosques for I'tikaf and the Ruling on Mujawarah
The commentator lists the best mosques and addresses the ruling on mujawarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to rank the best mosques for i'tikaf and state the ruling on mujawarah (residing near the Kaaba for devotion).

Core Idea
The best mosques for i'tikaf are the three harams, then Friday mosques, then those with large congregations.

This passage also addresses the preference of mosques for i'tikaf. After discussing validity, the commentator lists the most virtuous mosques, culminating in the best being the Sacred Mosque in Makkah. He then addresses the ruling of residing near the Kaaba (mujawarah) for devotion, noting a difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This lesson focuses on the hierarchy of preferred mosques and the ruling on mujawarah.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the hierarchy
List the mosques in order of preference according to the passage.
Makkah, Madinah, al-Aqsa, jami', large mosques.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why are these mosques preferred? (Closeness to the Prophet, increased reward, larger community).
The reward for prayer in these mosques is multiplied.
3
Identify the ruling on mujawarah
What did Abu Hanifa say, and what did the Sahibayn say?
Abu Hanifa: makruh tanzihan; Sahibayn: no problem.
4
Apply to practice
How does this hierarchy affect a person's choice of where to perform i'tikaf?
One should prefer the best possible mosque, but validity does not require the best.

Women's I'tikaf: The Home Prayer Area as Her Mosque
Ruling on women's i'tikaf location and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a woman's i'tikaf, identify the conditions and invalidators, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding validity in the congregational mosque.

Core Idea
A woman's 'mosque' is her designated home prayer area; i'tikaf there is best, but valid in the congregation mosque with dislike.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the preferred and permissible places for a woman's i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school. While the home prayer area is considered her mosque and the most meritorious location, i'tikaf in a congregational mosque is valid though disliked. The text also clarifies key conditions such as husband's permission and the effect of menstruation on obligatory i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text states that a woman performs i'tikaf in the mosque of her house, meaning the place prepared for prayer. Understand that this is the best location.
Note the term 'masjid baytiha' – her home prayer area is legally equivalent to a mosque for her i'tikaf.
2
Distinguish between best, valid, and disliked
The passage contrasts i'tikaf in the home prayer area (best) with i'tikaf elsewhere in the house (valid but less meritorious) and in the congregation mosque (valid but makruh tanzihan).
Dislike is for her leaving the home, not for the i'tikaf itself.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some early texts (zahir al-riwayah) suggested invalidity of i'tikaf in the women's section of the mosque, but al-Bada'i' affirms validity without dispute. The mufta bihi is valid but disliked.
The apparent contradiction is resolved by interpreting 'invalid' as 'lacking virtue'.
4
Examine conditions and invalidators
Note the conditions: husband's permission (even for obligatory i'tikaf), and the ruling that leaving the prayer area to the rest of the house invalidates obligatory i'tikaf. Menstruation also invalidates obligatory i'tikaf, requiring makeup.
For voluntary i'tikaf, leaving ends the i'tikaf without penalty.
5
Understand the vow and menstruation scenario
If a woman vows a month of i'tikaf and menstruates, she must make up the missed days consecutively after purification, otherwise she restarts from the beginning.
This highlights the strictness of obligatory i'tikaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمرأة تعتكف في مسجد بيتها يريد به الموضع المعد للصلاة لأنه أستر لها . قيد به لأنها لو اعتكفت في غير موضع صلاتها من بيتها، سواء كان لها موضع معد أو لا، اعتكافها. وأشار بقوله تعتكف دون أن يقول يجب عليها إلى أن اعتكافها في يصح مسجد بيتها أفضل فأفاد أن اعتكافها في مسجد الجماعة جائز وهو مكروه، ذكره قاضيخان وصححه في النهاية : وظاهر ما في غاية البيان أن ظاهر الرواية عدم الصحة. وفي البدائع اعتكافها في مسجد الجماعة صحيح بلا خلاف بين أصحابنا، والمذكور في الأصل محمول على نفي الفضيلة لا نفي الجواز. وأشار بجعله كالمسجد إلا أنها لو خرجت منه ولو إلى بيتها بطل اعتكافها إن كان واجباً وانتهى إن كان نفلاً والفرق بينهما أنها تثاب في الثاني دون الأول وهكذا في الرجل. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : ولو نذرت المرأة اعتكاف شهر فحاضت تقضي أيام حيضها متصلاً بالشهر وإلا استقبلت، وقد تقدم أنها لا تعتكف إلا بإذن زوجها إن كان لها زوج ولو واجباً. وفي المحيط : ولو أذن لها في الاعتكاف فأرادت أن تعتكف أن يأمرها بالتفريق لأنه لم يأذن لها في الاعتكاف متتابعاً لا نصاً ولا دلالة، ولو أذن لها في اعتكاف شهر أو صوم شهر بعينه فاعتكفت أو صامت فيه متتابعاً ليس له منعها لأنه أذن لها في التتابع ضرورة أنه متتابع وقوعاً. متتابعاً فللزوج
His statement: (And the woman performs i'tikaf in the mosque of her house) meaning the place prepared for prayer because it is more concealing for her. He restricted it because if she performs i'tikaf in other than her prayer place in her house, whether she has a designated place or not, her i'tikaf is valid. And he indicated by saying 'she performs i'tikaf' without saying 'it is obligatory upon her' that her i'tikaf in her home mosque is better, so it indicates that her i'tikaf in the congregational mosque is permissible but disliked...
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for women's i'tikaf. A woman's 'mosque' is the designated prayer area in her home, as it is more private and appropriate. If she performs i'tikaf elsewhere in the house, it is still valid, but the specific prayer spot is best. The text clarifies that her i'tikaf in a congregation mosque is permissible but makruh tanzihan (disliked). There is disagreement with the apparent transmission; some say it is invalid, but the correct view (as in al-Bada'i') is that it is valid, only less meritorious. The passage also covers that if a woman leaves her home prayer area to another part of the house, her i'tikaf is invalid if obligatory, but it ends (not requiring qada) if voluntary. Additional rules: if a woman vows a month of i'tikaf and menstruates, she must make up after purification continuously, otherwise restart. She must have her husband's permission for i'tikaf, even obligatory. If he gives permission for a specific month, she must do it consecutively, and he cannot stop her.

Key Terms
مسجد بيتها (masjid baytihā): The designated prayer area inside a woman's house, considered her 'mosque' for i'tikaf.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhah tanzīhiyyah): A light dislike; not sinful but abandoning it is better.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or transmitted ruling from the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where is the best place for a woman to perform i'tikaf?
A) In the local congregational mosque
B) In her designated home prayer area
C) In any part of her house
D) In a women-only mosque

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a woman's i'tikaf is best performed in her designated home prayer area, valid in the congregational mosque but disliked, and requires her husband's permission.

The Baseless Practice of Four Rak'ahs After Jumu'ah
Critique of the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah as baseless

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and identify the evidence that refutes it.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah as 'akhir zuhr' have no basis in the Hanafi school and lead to harm.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq critically examines a common practice among some Hanafis: praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah with the intention of the last zuhr. The author, Ibn Nujaym, declares this practice baseless and warns against it. This lesson will help you understand the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Practice
Recognize that the passage refers to the four rak'ahs prayed after Jumu'ah with the intention of making up the zuhr prayer in case Jumu'ah was invalid.
This is called 'ākhir ẓuhr'.
2
Author's Claim
Note that the author states this practice has no basis in the Hanafi school ('lā aṣla lahā fī al-madhhab').
He also mentions that earlier scholars only prescribed the post-sunnah prayer, not these four.
3
Examine the Evidence
Understand that the justification of later scholars was based on doubt about the validity of Jumu'ah due to the presumed impermissibility of multiple congregations. The passage cites Imam al-Sarakhsi's statement that the correct Hanafi view permits multiple Jumu'ah congregations, thus removing the doubt.
This is the key dalil that undermines the practice.
4
Recognize the Harm
Realize that the author warns the practice leads to laziness about Jumu'ah and may even cause disbelief if one believes Jumu'ah is not obligatory.
The fatwa against it is firm.
5
Apply the Ruling
Conclude that the mufta bihi is to abandon the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and only pray the regular sunnah (4 or 6 rak'ahs).
Do not intend 'ākhir ẓuhr'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غيرها في تحقيقها وكذا السنة فما قالوه هنا من صلاة التحية ضعيف ويصلي بعدها السنة أربعاً على قوله وستاً على قولهما ولو أقام في الجامع أكثر من ذلك لم يفسد اعتكافه لأنه موضع الاعتكاف إلا أنه يكره لأنه التزم أداءه في مسجد واحد فلا يتمه في مسجدين من غير ضرورة، وقد ظهر بما ذكروه أن الأربع التي تصلى بعد الجمعة وينوي بها آخر ظهر عليه لا أصل لها في المذهب لأنهم نصوا هنا على أن المعتكف لا يصلي إلا السنة البعدية فقط، ولأن من اختارها من المتأخرين فإنما اختارها للشك في أن جمعته سابقة أولاً بناء على عدم جواز تعددها في مصر واحد، وقد نص الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي على أن الصحيح من مذهب أبي حنيفة جواز إقامتها في مصر واحد في مسجدين فأكثر ـ قال وبه نأخذ. وفي فتح القدير وهو الأصح فلا ينبغي الإفتاء بها في زماننا لما أنهم تطرقوا منها إلى التكاسل عن الجمعة بل ربما وقع عندهم أن الجمعة ليست فرضاً وأنَّ الظهر كاف، ولا خفاء في كفر من اعتقد ذلك فلذلك نبهت عليها مرارا .
Other than it in its realization, and also the sunnah, so what they said here about the prayer of greeting is weak. He prays after it four rak'ahs according to his statement and six according to their statement. And if he stayed in the mosque more than that, his i'tikaf does not become invalid because it is the place of i'tikaf, except that it is disliked because he committed to performing it in one mosque, so he does not complete it in two mosques without necessity. And it has become clear from what they mentioned that the four rak'ahs that are prayed after Jumu'ah intending by them the last zuhr have no basis in the school, because they explicitly stated here that the mu'takif only prays the post-sunnah prayer only. And because those among the later scholars who chose it only chose it due to doubt whether their Jumu'ah was early or not, based on the impermissibility of multiple congregations in one city. And Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi explicitly stated that the correct view from Abu Hanifa is the permissibility of holding it in one city in two or more mosques – he said: and we take that. And in Fath al-Qadir, it is the most authentic, so it is not appropriate to give fatwa with it in our time because they have used it as a means to become lazy about Jumu'ah; rather, it might occur to them that Jumu'ah is not obligatory and that zuhr is sufficient. And there is no concealment of the disbelief of one who believes that, so I have warned about it repeatedly.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a critical ruling regarding the practice of praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah with the intention of the last zuhr (salat al-akhir al-zuhr). The author states that this practice has no basis in the Hanafi school. He first discusses the ruling for a mu'takif who enters the mosque: the tahiyyat al-masjid is considered weak, but the sunnah prayer after Jumu'ah is either four rak'ahs (according to one opinion) or six (according to the two companions). If the mu'takif stays longer, it does not invalidate i'tikaf but is disliked. Then the author directly addresses the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah: they are not part of the madhhab because scholars only mention the post-sunnah (sunna ba'diyya). The justification of later scholars for these four rak'ahs is based on doubt about the validity of Jumu'ah due to the earlier view that multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city were impermissible. However, Sarakhsi confirms that the correct Hanafi position is the permissibility of multiple Jumu'ah congregations in one city. Therefore, the fatwa on these four rak'ahs should not be given, as it leads to neglect of Jumu'ah, and even disbelief if one considers Jumu'ah non-obligatory.

Key Terms
آخر ظهر (ākhir ẓuhr): Four rak'ahs prayed after Jumu'ah with the intention of making up the zuhr prayer in case Jumu'ah was invalid.
صلاة التحية (ṣalāt al-taḥiyya): Prayer of greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) – considered weak in this context.
السنة البعدية (al-sunna al-ba‘diyya): The post-sunnah prayer after Jumu'ah, which is either 4 or 6 rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bahr al-Raiq, what is the ruling on praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah with the intention of the last zuhr?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is wajib for those who doubt their Jumu'ah.
C) It has no basis in the Hanafi school and should not be practiced.
D) It is recommended to avoid disagreement.

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah as 'ākhir ẓuhr' have no basis in the Hanafi school and should not be practiced.

Al-Maqdisi's Objection on the Four Rak'ahs After Jumu'ah
Objecting to an earlier critique of the four rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Maqdisi's two objections to the critique of the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf of the dispute.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah are not rejected; they serve as a precaution when doubt about Jumu'ah's validity arises.

This brief passage presents a critical refinement of the earlier claim that the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah have no foundation. Al-Maqdisi, a later Hanafi scholar, raises two objections that shift the discussion from outright rejection to a nuanced understanding: the context of the earlier chapter and the assumption of certainty. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
List al-Maqdisi's two points: (1) the chapter on i'tikaf is not the place to discuss those four rak'ahs; (2) earlier scholars did not mention them because they assumed Jumu'ah is valid with certainty.
2
Analyze the first objection
Explain why the i'tikaf chapter is not the proper locus for Jumu'ah post-prayer rak'ahs. The chapter's purpose is to explain the rulings of i'tikaf, not the details of Jumu'ah prayers.
3
Analyze the second objection
Clarify that the silence of earlier scholars is not a rejection; rather, they built their rulings on the default assumption that Jumu'ah is valid. The four rak'ahs are only needed when there is doubt about that validity.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: some scholars recommend the four rak'ahs as a precautionary measure (mustahabb), while others reject them entirely. This passage does not settle the matter but legitimizes the precautionary view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يخشى منه ذلك كما مر مبسوطاً عن المقدسي وغيره. ثم رأيت العلامة المقدسي اعترضه في شرحه بوجهين: أحدهما أنه ليس باب تلك الأربع المعقود لبيان أحكامها الثاني أن عدم ذكرهم بناء على وقوع الجمعة صحيحة مستجمعة لشرائطها بيقين كما هو الأصل إذا صليت والإتيان لأربع عند وقوع شك واحتمال ا هـ . وهذا ما قدمناه أولاً.
He fears that from it as it has been detailed from al-Maqdisi and others. Then I saw al-Allama al-Maqdisi objecting to it in his commentary with two points: One is that it is not the chapter of those four rak'ahs appointed for explaining their rulings. The second is that their not mentioning them is based on Jumu'ah occurring validly fulfilling its conditions with certainty, as is the original when prayed; and performing four rak'ahs occurs when there is doubt and probability. End quote. And this is what we presented earlier.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage presents an objection by the scholar al-Maqdisi to the earlier criticism that the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah have no basis. He raises two points: First, the chapter under discussion (i'tikaf) is not the place for the rulings of those four rak'ahs. Second, the fact that earlier scholars did not mention the four rak'ahs is because they assumed Jumu'ah was valid with certainty; the four rak'ahs are only for cases of doubt. This objection supports the view that there is room for the practice, albeit for the purpose of precaution. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq then notes that he had already mentioned this view earlier in his commentary on Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
الإتيان لأربع عند وقوع شك (al-itiyān li-arbaʿ ʿinda wuqūʿ shakk): Performing four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah when there is doubt about its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they considered them bid'ah.
B) Because they assumed Jumu'ah is valid with certainty.
C) Because they were unaware of the practice.
D) Because the practice was not established in their time.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maqdisi's objection shows that the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah have a legitimate basis in Hanafi fiqh as a precaution against doubt, challenging the earlier absolute rejection.

Disliked Acts During I'tikaf: Bringing Items, Silence, and Speech
Commentary on matn rulings regarding makruh actions during i'tikaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on three disliked acts in i'tikaf, distinguish between makruh tahrimi and tanzihi, and apply the conditions under which the ruling changes.

Core Idea
In i'tikaf, silence as worship and idle speech are disliked; the mosque is a sanctuary from worldly affairs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains three actions that are disliked (makruh) during i'tikaf: bringing a purchased item into the mosque, observing silence as a form of worship, and speaking except for good. The commentary clarifies the reasoning, the level of dislike (tahrimi vs. tanzihi), and exceptions. Understanding these nuances helps the mu'takif preserve the sacredness of i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three disliked acts
The matn states three acts: bringing a sold item, silence, and speech not for good. Recognize each as a separate ruling.
2
Analyze the first ruling: bringing a sold item
The reasoning is that the mosque is protected from worldly rights; items that occupy space distract. The commentator indicates the dislike is tahrimi. Note exception: small non-occupying items are not disliked.
3
Analyze the second ruling: silence (samt)
Silence as a worship act is disliked because it resembles Magian practice. Exception: without intent of worship, silence is not disliked (hadith 'Whoever remains silent is saved').
4
Analyze the third ruling: speech
Quranic command to speak well (al-Isra: 53) applies generally; in mosque it is even more emphasized. Intra-madhhab difference: some say permissible speech is disliked, others only sinful. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that permissible speech is disliked for the mu'takif.
5
Apply the preferred view to a scenario
Given a mu'takif discussing a permissible topic like weather, most authorities say it is makruh tahrimi. He should engage in beneficial acts instead.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكره إحضار المبيع والصمت والتكلم إلا بخير) أما الأول فلأن المسجد محرز عن حقوق العباد وفيه شغله بها ولهذا قالوا لا يجوز غرس الأشجار فيه. والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية لأنها محل إطلاقهم كما صرح به المحقق في فتح القدير أول الزكاة، ودل تعليلهم أن المبيع لو كان لا يشغل البقعة لا يكره إحضاره كدراهم ودنانير يسيرة أو كتاب ونحوه. وأفاد الإطلاق أن إحضار الطعام المبيع الذي يشتريه ليأكله مكروه، وينبغي عدم كراهته كما لا يخفى. وأما الثاني وهو الصمت فالمراد به ترك التحدث مع الناس من غير عذر وقد ورد النهي عنه وقالوا: إن صوم الصمت من فعل المجوس لعنهم الله تعالى. وخصه الإمام حميد الدين الضرير بما إذا اعتقده قربة، أما إذا لم يعتقده قربة فلا يكره للحديث «من صمت نجا». وأما الثالث وهو أنه لا يتكلم إلا بخير فلقوله تعالى (وقل لعبادي يقولوا التي أحسن) [الإسراء: ٥٣] وهو بعمومه يقتضي أن لا يتكلم خارج المسجد إلا بخير فالمسجد أولى. كذا في غاية البيان. وفي التبيين وأما التكلم بغير خير فإنه يكره لغير المعتكف فما ظنك للمعتكف ا.هـ. وظاهره أن المراد بالخير هنا ما لا إثم فيه فيشمل المباح وبغيره الخير ما فيه إثم، والأولى تفسيره بما فيه ثواب يعني أنه يكره للمعتكف أن يتكلم بالمباح بخلاف غيره ولهذا قالوا الكلام المباح في المسجد مكروه يأكل الحسنات كما تأكل النار الحطب. صرح به فتح القدير قبيل بال الوتر لكن قال الأسبيجابي: ولا بأس أن يتحدث بما لا إثم فيه. وقال في الهداية لكنه يتجانب ما يكون مأثماً. والظاهر ما ذكرناه كما لا يخفى قالوا: ويلازم قراءة القرآن والحديث والعلم والتدريس وسير النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقصص الأنبياء وحكايات الصالحين وكتابة أمور الدين.
His statement: (And it is disliked to bring the sold item, silence, and speech except with good) As for the first, because the mosque is preserved from the rights of people and it involves preoccupation with them; hence they said it is not permissible to plant trees in it. The apparent view is that the dislike is prohibition-level (tahrimi) because it is the place of their absolute statements as verified by al-Muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir at the beginning of Zakat. Their reasoning indicates that if the sold item does not occupy a space, its bringing is not disliked, like a few dirhams and dinars or a book and the like. The absolute expression implies that bringing food that is sold and which he buys to eat is disliked, but it should not be disliked as is not hidden. As for the second, i.e., silence, what is meant is refraining from speaking with people without an excuse, and prohibition has been reported against it, and they said: The fast of silence is an act of the Magians, may Allah curse them. Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir specified it for when he believes it to be an act of worship; if he does not believe it to be an act of worship, it is not disliked due to the hadith 'Whoever remains silent is saved'. As for the third, i.e., that he should not speak except with good, due to His statement (And say to My servants that they should say that which is best) [al-Isra: 53], and its generality requires that he should not speak outside the mosque except with good, so the mosque is more deserving. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in al-Tabyin: As for speaking without good, it is disliked for a non-mu'takif, so what do you think for a mu'takif? End. Its apparent meaning is that what is meant by 'good' here is that which has no sin, thus it includes permissible, and by 'other than good' is that which has sin. The preferable interpretation is to explain it as that which has reward, meaning it is disliked for a mu'takif to speak about permissible matters, unlike others; hence they said: Permissible speech in the mosque is disliked and eats up good deeds as fire eats firewood. Fath al-Qadir explicitly stated it before the section on Witr, but al-Asbijabi said: There is no harm in talking about matters with no sin. And in al-Hidayah: But he should avoid sinful matters. The apparent is what we mentioned, as is not hidden. They said: He should constantly engage in reciting Quran, hadith, knowledge, teaching, the Prophet's biography, stories of prophets and righteous people, and writing religious matters.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a matn ruling about three disliked acts during i'tikaf: bringing a sold item into the mosque, observing silence (as a form of worship), and speaking except for good. The commentator explains each. For bringing a sold item, the reasoning is that the mosque is a sacred place reserved for worship, and trade distracts from it. However, if the item doesn't occupy space (like coins or a small book), it is not disliked. The commentator notes a difference of opinion on whether the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitory) or tanzihi, leaning towards tahrimi. For silence, the prohibition is based on reports that it resembles the practice of the Magians, but if one does not intend it as worship, it is not disliked (supported by a hadith). For speech, the Quranic verse commands speaking well generally, and being in the mosque is even more deserving. The commentator resolves differing views: some say permissible speech is disliked, others say only sinful speech. The preferred view is that permissible speech is disliked for the mu'takif, especially if unnecessary. The passage ends with recommended activities for the mu'takif.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karāhah taḥrīmiyya): A level of dislike that approaches prohibition, meaning the act is sinful but not invalidating the i'tikaf.
صمت (ṣamt): Observing silence as a form of worship, i.e., refraining from speech intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a mu'takif bringing a small book (sold item) into the mosque for study?
A) It is haram.
B) It is makruh tahrimi.
C) It is not disliked because it does not occupy space.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
In i'tikaf, avoid worldly distractions like trade and idle talk; silence is only disliked if intended as worship; the mufta bihi is that permissible speech is makruh tahrimi.

Prohibition of Intercourse and Its Preliminaries in I'tikaf
Ruling with proof on the prohibition of sexual intercourse and its preliminaries during i'tikaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on intercourse and its preliminaries during i'tikaf, identify the Quranic proof, and distinguish the nullification rules from those in fasting.

Core Idea
The prohibition of intercourse in i'tikaf is explicit and extends to all preliminaries; forgetfulness does not excuse because the mu'takif's state is constantly reminding.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the prohibition of sexual intercourse and its immediate preliminaries (kissing, touching) during i'tikaf. Based on the Quranic verse 'Do not have sexual relations with them while you are in i'tikaf' (al-Baqarah: 187), the Hanafi school rules that all forms of mubasharah are haram. The commentary compares this to Hajj, istibra', and zihar, and contrasts it with menstruation and fasting, where preliminaries are not prohibited. It also clarifies the conditions for nullification, emphasizing the unique concept of a 'reminding state' that distinguishes i'tikaf from fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its proof
The passage states that intercourse and its preliminaries are prohibited (haram) during i'tikaf. The proof is the Quranic verse 'Do not have sexual relations with them while you are in i'tikaf in the mosques' (al-Baqarah: 187). The term 'mubasharah' covers both intercourse and foreplay.
The prohibition is explicit (sarih al-nahy) and general.
2
Understand the extension to preliminaries
The commentator argues that because the prohibition of intercourse is established by explicit text, it extends to its preliminaries (kissing, touching) by analogy with Hajj, istibra', and zihar, where similar prohibitions also extend.
In fasting and menstruation, the ruling differs because the prohibition is not explicit or would cause hardship.
3
Analyze the nullification rules
Intercourse invalidates i'tikaf regardless of intent, memory, day/night, or ejaculation. Kissing/touching with desire invalidates only if accompanied by ejaculation. This differs from fasting, where forgetfulness preserves validity.
The key reason: the mu'takif's state is 'mudhakkirah' (constantly reminding), like ihram and prayer.
4
Contrast with fasting and other contexts
In fasting, the prohibition of intercourse is not explicit, and preliminaries are not prohibited due to hardship. Forgetfulness excuses in fasting for eating/drinking but not in i'tikaf for intercourse, because the prohibition is i'tikaf-specific.
The passage emphasizes that i'tikaf-specific prohibitions do not differentiate between intentional/forgetful, while fasting-specific prohibitions do.
5
Examine the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is hold that i'tikaf is not invalidated by intercourse unless it is intentional and with full penetration. Hanafis are stricter, invalidating even forgetful intercourse and extending the prohibition to preliminaries.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a mu'takif's i'tikaf may be valid in Shafi'i school after forgetful intercourse but invalid in Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويحرم الوطء ودواعيه) لقوله تعالى (ولا تباشروهن وأنتم عاكفون في المساجد) [البقرة: ۱۸۷] لأن المباشرة تصدق على الوطء ودواعيه فيفيد تحريم كل فرد من أفراد المباشرة جماع أو غيره لأنه في سياق النهي فيفيد العموم والمراد بدواعيه المس والقبلة وهو كالحجج والاستبراء والظهار لما حرم الوطء لها حرم دواعيه لأن حرمة الوطء ثبتت بصريح النهي فقويت فتعدت إلى الدواعي أما في الحج فلقوله تعالى (فلا رفث) [البقرة: ١٩٧] وأما في الاستبراء فللحديث «لا تنكح الحبالى حتى يضعن ولا الحيالي حتى يستبرئن بحيضة». وأما في الظهار فلقوله تعالى (من قبل أن يتماسا) [المجادلة: ٣] بخلاف الحيض والصوم حيث لا تحرم الدواعي فيهما لأن حرمة الوطء لم تثبت بصريح النهي. ولكثرة الوقوع فلو حرم الدواعي لزم الحرج وهو مدفوع، ولأن النص في الحيض معلول بعلة الأذى لا يوجد في الدواعي قوله: (ويبطل بوطئه لأنه محذور بالنص فكان مفسداً له. أطلقه وهو فشمل ما إذا كان عامداً أو ناسياً نهاراً أو ليلاً أنزل أو لا بخلاف الصوم إذا كان ناسياً. والفرق أن حالة المعتكف مذكرة كحالة الإحرام والصلاة وحالة الصائم غير مذكرة، وقيد بالوطء لأن الجماع فيما دون الفرج أو التقبيل أو اللمس لا يفسد إلا إذا أنزل وإن أمنى بالتفكر أو النظر لا يفسد اعتكافه وإن أكل أو شرب ليلاً لم يفسد اعتكافه، وإن أكل نهاراً فإن عامداً فسد لفساد الصوم، وإن ناسياً لا لبقاء الصوم والأصل أن ما كان من محظورات الاعتكاف وهو ما منع عنه لأجل الاعتكاف لا لأجل الصوم لا يختلف فيه العمد والسهو والنهار والليل كالجماع والخروج، وما كان من محظورات الصوم وهو مانع لأجل الصوم يختلف فيه العمد والسهو والنهار والليل كالأكل والشرب. كذا في البدائع.
His statement: (And intercourse and its preludes are prohibited) due to His statement (And do not have sexual relations with them while you are in i'tikaf in the mosques) [al-Baqarah: 187] because 'mubasharah' applies to intercourse and its preludes, so it indicates the prohibition of every individual of mubasharah, whether intercourse or other, because it is in the context of prohibition, so it indicates generality. What is meant by its preliminaries is touching and kissing, and it is like (the prohibitions) in Hajj, istibra', and zihar: when intercourse is prohibited, its preliminaries are also prohibited because the prohibition of intercourse is established by explicit text (sarih al-nahy), so it is strong and extends to preliminaries. As for Hajj, due to His statement (so no sexual intercourse) [al-Baqarah: 197]; as for istibra', due to the hadith 'Do not marry pregnant women until they give birth, nor barren until they are cleared by one menstrual period'; as for zihar, due to His statement (before they touch each other) [al-Mujadilah: 3]. Unlike menstruation and fasting, where the preliminaries are not prohibited, because the prohibition of intercourse is not established by explicit text, and due to frequent occurrence; if they were prohibited, it would lead to hardship, which is negated, and because the text in menstruation is based on the cause of harm, which is not present in preliminaries. His statement: (And it becomes invalid by intercourse, because it is prohibited by text, so it is a corruptor of it. He gave it generally, which includes whether intentional or forgetful, day or night, whether he ejaculated or not, unlike fasting if one is forgetful. The difference is that the state of the mu'takif is reminding (of the prohibition) like the state of ihram and prayer, and the state of the fasting person is not reminding. And it is restricted to intercourse because coitus without penetration, kissing, or touching does not invalidate unless he ejaculates. If he experiences seminal emission by thinking or looking, his i'tikaf is not invalidated. If he eats or drinks at night, his i'tikaf is not invalidated. If he eats during the day, if intentionally it becomes invalid due to the invalidation of fasting; if forgetfully, it does not. The principle is: what is among the prohibitions of i'tikaf, i.e., what is prohibited for the sake of i'tikaf and not for fasting, does not differ regarding intentional or forgetful, day or night, like intercourse and exiting. And what is among the prohibitions of fasting, i.e., a prevention for the sake of fasting, differs regarding intentional and forgetful, day and night, like eating and drinking. This is in al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that sexual intercourse and its immediate preliminaries (kissing, touching with desire) are haram during i'tikaf, based on the Quranic verse 'Do not have sexual relations with them while you are in i'tikaf in the mosques' (al-Baqarah: 187). The commentator explains that the term 'mubasharah' encompasses both intercourse and its preliminaries, and the prohibition is explicit (sarih al-nahy), so it covers all forms. He compares it to Hajj, istibra', and zihar where similar prohibitions extend to preliminaries. However, in menstruation and fasting, preliminaries are not prohibited because the prohibition of intercourse is not explicit; in menstruation, the prohibition is based on the cause of harm, which is not present in preliminaries; in fasting, it would cause undue hardship. The passage also discusses nullification: i'tikaf is invalidated by intercourse regardless of intent, memory, day/night, or ejaculation, unlike fasting where forgetfulness preserves validity. This is because the mu'takif's state is 'mudhakkirah' (reminding of the prohibition) similar to ihram and prayer. The distinction is important: prohibitions specific to i'tikaf (like intercourse and leaving) are not excused by forgetfulness, while prohibitions related to fasting (like eating) differ based on intent.

Key Terms
المباشرة (al-mubāsharah): Sexual contact, includes both intercourse and foreplay (kissing, touching).
حالة مذكرة (ḥālah mudhakkirah): A state that constantly reminds the person of the prohibition, like ihram or prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mu'takif forgetfully has intercourse during i'tikaf, what happens according to the Hanafi school?
A) His i'tikaf remains valid because it was forgetful.
B) His i'tikaf is invalidated because the state is mudhakkirah.
C) He must offer kaffarah.
D) He must repeat only the day.

Key Takeaway
In i'tikaf, the prohibition of intercourse is absolute and extends to preliminaries; forgetfulness does not excuse nullification because the mu'takif is in a constantly reminding state, unlike in fasting.
